> ## 🔴 OPEN SECURITY MATTER — task #89 — READ THIS BEFORE TOUCHING `crates/r2-hive-bin/src/hive.rs`
>
> **A live group HMAC key is present in this public repository, and it is confirmed real, not synthetic.**
>
> The 64-hex literal bound to `hk_hex` at `crates/r2-hive-bin/src/hive.rs:1387` is byte-identical to the
> live custody key for target group `177560432` (TG-A) held in `~/.r2/group-keys.json` (mode `0600`, 857 B,
> four target groups, dated 5 July). The comparison was made by equality inside a Python process; the value
> itself was never printed to a terminal, written to any file, or transmitted in any fleet message, and it
> MUST continue to be handled that way. `docs/espnow-mesh-interop.md:52` names TG-A as a live target group,
> and three field logs under `docs/field-results/lora-fr1-0623/` show real boards provisioned with it.
>
> **Blast radius, measured across all 21 fleet repositories on all refs.** Only TG-A's key is exposed, and
> only in this one file. The other three custody keys (`1584099016`, `3932969629`, `79452135`) return no hit
> anywhere. The exposed key is present on seven refs including `refs/heads/main` and `refs/remotes/origin/main`.
>
> **What the exposure grants, confirmed independently at both ends of the pipe.** core measured the
> derivation side in `r2-trust`; I measured the consuming side here. `parse_bench_group_hmacs`
> (`hive.rs:1240`) maps the hex into a `GroupHmac` and nothing else, and the field it populates is
> `group_hmacs: HashMap<u32, GroupHmac>` (`hive.rs:255`). The data encryption key never travels this path.
> So this is a **mesh integrity compromise for TG-A** — an attacker in radio range can forge frames that
> verify as authentic TG-A traffic — and it is **not** a confidentiality break and **not** an identity
> break, because `GroupHmac` was never attributive. Bound it that way in any writeup: reading it as worse
> than it is carries its own cost.
>
> **A correction I owe.** I earlier reported zero custody hits for this value. That probe searched
> `~/.r2-dev-trial`; the actual custody root is `~/.r2/`. The method was sound and its positive control did
> fire — the scope was wrong. **That null is WITHDRAWN.** This is the same scope-fragile-null failure recorded
> in my standing memory, which is precisely why a null needs its domain stated alongside its result.
>
> **Why nothing has been changed, and why a takeover MUST NOT change anything either.** core proposed
> replacing the literal immediately on the grounds that replacement is correct whether the value turns out
> real or synthetic, so it need not wait on the answer. That argument does not survive the answer being
> *real*. Replacing the literal does not remediate anything: the value remains on seven refs of a public
> repository, and a commit whose message explains that a key was scrubbed is an index pointing straight at
> it in history. **Rotating the TG-A HMAC key is the remedy; replacing the literal is a step sequenced
> inside that rotation, not something to be done ahead of it.** The ordering of scrub, history rewrite, and
> disclosure is Roy's call, and it has been escalated to the supervisor pair and to core.
>
> **Standing posture until Roy rules: no scrub, no rewrite, no force-push, no commit touching this file.**
>
> One lead not pursued, because widening it is not mine to do: the doc comment at `hive.rs:1235` describes
> the format as "composer's bench group-keys json", so composer may know who minted the value.
>
> **A second custody event, on core's side, now measured.** core self-reported that its harness read
> `~/.r2/group-keys.json` into its session context whole and unprompted, putting all four live keys —
> including the three that are *not* leaked — into a context it cannot purge. I measured the on-disk
> consequence from outside. All three unleaked keys are persisted in **exactly one file**: core's own
> session transcript, mode `0600`. No fleet-ask fork, no subagent transcript, no scratchpad, no shell
> history, no other lane. My session did not capture them (my probes emitted tg ids, hex lengths, and
> booleans, never values), and search patterns were fed to `grep` via stdin so that hunting for custody
> keys never wrote custody keys to disk.
>
> **Domain of that null, because the rotation argument leans on it.** Eleven roots: `~/.claude`,
> `/tmp/claude-1000`, `~/.zsh_history`, `~/.cache`, `~/.local/share`, `~/.config`, `~/Documents`,
> `~/Downloads`, `~/Desktop`, `/tmp`, `/var/tmp`, with two live positive controls firing throughout.
> It does **not** cover Alfred or any other remote box — `carrier-bridge` runs from `alfred:~/carrier-bridge/`
> and I have not probed it and MUST NOT without authorization — nor backups or cloud-synced locations.
> So: local workstation spread is one file. **Fleet-wide spread is not established.**
>
> **The urgency model that was nearly acted on, and why it was wrong.** core argued the exposure was
> ongoing because every turn re-transmits the context, so continuing to work extended the window. That is
> false: re-transmission reaches the same provider that already received the bytes at turn one, so it adds
> copies at one recipient and no new recipient. **Exposure to that channel completed at the moment of the
> read — it is binary, not accruing, and ending the session un-exposes nothing.** core conceded this: it
> reasoned about transmission count when the property that bounds an exposure is recipient set. But its
> *direction* was right through a mechanism neither of us had named — **local spread**. Compaction reads
> context and writes a new artifact to disk, so the number that continuing work can change is one file to
> N files. The single-file measurement is itself evidence no compaction has propagated them yet, and core
> corroborated that independently on mtime (four sibling transcripts untouched since late June). The one
> real lever is core's session ending before a compaction writes a summary.
>
> **Joint recommendation to Roy: rotate all four.** Three bench/dev target groups re-minted is bounded work
> with no field fleet, set against a live frame-authentication key with no AP-down bound of the kind that
> de-escalated the earlier PSK finding. Note the reasoning honestly: this is not independent convergence —
> core's conclusion survived on my mechanism after its own was refuted.
>
> **Nobody should delete core's transcript on their own initiative.** It is the only record of what was
> exposed and when, deletion is irreversible, and it would not shorten the exposure by one turn, because
> the values are in context rather than only in the file.
>
> Bench readiness below is unaffected by all of this, and flash remains Roy-gated.

> ⚠ **Do NOT revert this to the bare `git status --porcelain <path>`.** That form returns rc=0 and zero
> porcelain lines for a WRONG OR RENAMED PATH exactly as it does for a clean tree — verified by
> substituting `platforms/NONEXISTENT/src`, which produced identical judged output. **A gate that passes
> when you are looking at the wrong directory is not a gate.** The `ls-files --error-unmatch` prefix
> consumes the path and fails loudly if it is not tracked (control: the wrong path fails, the right path
> passes).

> ## (historical framing of this block, retained)
> **Every block below this one is HISTORICAL NARRATIVE. Where any of them carries an RFC 2119 keyword that
> conflicts with this block, THIS BLOCK WINS and the older keyword is VOID.** (hive-codex F1: I had been
> PREPENDING corrections while leaving contradictory uppercase MUSTs in place, so a takeover could not obey
> all of them at once. My own RFC 2119 rule made that worse — every stale line carried a binding keyword.
> **Prepending a correction does not supersede a MUST; only deleting or de-normativising it does.**)
>
> **BENCH — dfr1195 BLE observer, task #84. Artifact `d4c65886e6f9a85fe5b6858017bc354dd8fa7384434661441bd45346ef5dea57`, 1133660 B, features `xiaobridge,ble`, code commit `4f17efa`. Manifest = dfr1195-fw **`398cf31`**. JUDGE THE BENCH BY THE MANIFEST AT `398cf31`, not by any commit named lower down this file.**
> ⚠ **DO NOT trust that pin blind — VERIFY it, because for this file the DOCS ARE THE GATE and "later commits are docs-only" does NOT preserve bench-instruction semantics** (hive-codex: I pinned `0527054`, which is exactly the revision whose ON/OFF rules used a bare non-normative `REQUIRE`; the binding text existed only at `398cf31`). The binding manifest is **whichever commit last modified the manifest file**, so resolve it rather than reading it here:
> ```
> git -C <dfr1195-fw worktree> log -1 --format=%h -- platforms/dfr1195/STAGED-XIAOBRIDGE-BLE.md
> ```
> If that command does not print `398cf31`, the manifest moved after this line was written and **the command wins, not this file.** The ARTIFACT sha `d4c65886…` is the invariant; a manifest commit is not.**
> - **ITEM 1 (board still advertises) — RUNNABLE** under the existing Roy flash gate.
> - **ITEM 2 (observer sights a peer) — HELD. Records neither PASS nor FAIL.** ✅ **The instrument now EXISTS
>   (composer rewrote `scan-beacons.py`, `r2-composer` `b1a9345`; verified in its tree, not taken on report:
>   event-stamped `PropertiesChanged` `:320`, the load-bearing `"ManufacturerData" not in changed → skip`
>   guard `:303`, `RemoveDevice` purge `:225`, `InterfacesRemoved` withdrawal `:324`, `found` now per-phase
>   and never persisted `:261` — which closes the old write-only/no-expiry defect).**
>   **WHAT IS STILL MISSING IS THE ONE TEST THAT WOULD PROVE IT: with board B powered OFF and the BlueZ cache
>   warm, `scan-beacons.py 12 --expect <B_wire_id>` MUST exit 3. Before the rewrite it exited 0.** The
>   `--freshness-kat` prints that procedure, exits 9, and REFUSES to self-certify because it cannot power a
>   board down. Everything runnable off-metal exercises only the direction that already worked.
> - **ON phase: the run MUST receive a fresh target event** after a purge/session reset. **OFF phase: the run
>   MUST receive no target event across a full bounded window.** They are NOT symmetric; an OFF phase can never be
>   proven by requiring an event.
> - **Purge (or reset the scanner session) before EACH phase — one pre-run purge is insufficient.**
> - **No-new-RBID is UNTESTED / SETUP-AMBIGUOUS, never FAIL**, unless distinct-B-rbid was proven first
>   (a persona in NVS overrides the `mac_low3` fallback, main.rs:294-296, so one image ≠ distinct identities).
> - **A fresh scanner's own negative test MUST acquire B, power B OFF, wait past the freshness window, and
>   then reject B.** A poll-time freshness stamp is REFUTED — re-reading cached state refreshes the stamp with no
>   air behind it.

> **★ MY DEAD CONJECTURE FOUND A LIVE DEFECT IN CORE'S CRATE — and core's ruling then INVERTED my own follow-up task, which I REPLACED rather than annotated (core `5e6384e`, RX-side only, NO wire bytes, cannot invalidate `d4c65886`).** core traced WHY `r2-dataplane:943` hardcodes `false` and found the opposite of what my conjecture implied: **`R2-WIRE.md:178` — "M = 1 = ORIGINATED BY a reduced-capability companion MCU" — is a claim about `originator` (route_stack[0]), NOT about `immediate_source` (the peer we heard from). They coincide ONLY on a single-hop frame.** `sync_host.rs:263` was reading the bit straight into a neighbour entry keyed on `immediate_source` ⇒ **a companion MCU originates, a full-stack RELAY forwards, we observe the RELAY, mark the RELAY `mcu_only`, `is_viable=false`, and the relay drops out of every flood plan — and it STICKS (`neighbour.rs:349-353` re-clears only on an observation carrying `mcu_origin=false`). A capable relay leaves the route fabric as a REWARD for carrying a companion's frames.** Fixed as `header.flags.mcu_origin && originator == immediate_source`, failing open deliberately: wrongly believing a neighbour relays costs one dropped frame plus a confidence penalty; wrongly believing it does NOT removes it from the fabric until something re-clears the bit. ✎ **THIS REFUTES MY OWN TASK #86, whose premise was "dfr1195 hardcodes `false` on RX ⇒ ignores a real signal ⇒ should propagate" — that was exactly the fix direction core was about to take and then didn't. dfr1195's hardcoded `false` at `:1428`/`:1453`/`:1945` is CORRECT for multi-hop. #86 rewritten (not annotated) to the NARROW surviving gap: on a SINGLE-HOP frame, where `originator == immediate_source` and the bit IS valid, we still discard it, so we never learn a genuine companion MCU is tx-only. Low priority, no symptom.** **SCOPING FACT recorded so nobody sizes it as trivial: the dfr1195 obs site has `immediate_source` ONLY (`main.rs:1937` `Observation { hive_id: sender_hive, .. }`); `route_stack[0]` is NOT in scope, so core's guard is a plumbing change here, and when patched it MUST match core's shape rather than a hive-invented variant.** ⚠ **core's fix is a SECOND #63 candidate — a better one than the M bit — but ONLY on boards that run `sync_host`. dfr1195 does NOT (Path C, proven), so it is not mine. OPEN AND UNOWNED: which boards run `sync_host`? Neither core nor I know; that MUST be answered by whoever owns those platforms before anyone re-tests #63 against `5e6384e`.** ~core also accepted Path C and stated the distinction I would have skipped: its enumeration was "complete FOR CORE, wrong FOR THE FLEET" (grep `Observation {` across core's `platforms/`+`tools/` = ZERO). ~It promoted the masking insight as a general shape: **two independent defects in OPPOSITE directions where one suppresses the other's symptom — which is why "no symptom" is not evidence of "no defect", same family as an unfired gate.**
> **✖ MY M-BIT/#63 CONJECTURE IS DEAD — killed by my own trace, via a THIRD RX path core did not enumerate. THE CONFORMANCE DEFECT SURVIVES AND IS OWED.** core answered my falsifier by naming two core-side paths (Path A `r2-dataplane/src/lib.rs:943` hardcodes `mcu_origin: false` ⇒ M never propagates; Path B `r2-hive-core/src/sync_host.rs:263` propagates `header.flags.mcu_origin` ⇒ mechanism holds) and asked which loop dfr1195 runs. **ANSWER: NEITHER. dfr1195 runs no `sync_host` (grep: 2 COMMENT hits at main.rs:48/:6607, ZERO calls) and does not take neighbour obs from r2-dataplane — it CONSTRUCTS ITS OWN `Observation`s in platform code at THREE sites and HARDCODES the bit at every one: `:1422`→`:1428 mcu_origin: false`, `:1447`→`:1453 false`, `:1937`→`:1945 false`. `header.flags.mcu_origin` is NEVER READ on this board** ⇒ the received M bit cannot reach `mcu_only`, cannot reach `is_viable`, and core's sticky-clear rule (`neighbour.rs:349-353`) never even gets a chance to fire. **⇒ #63 mesh-wide nbrs=0 is NOT M-bit caused on dfr1195. PATH C exists — platform-local Observation construction — and core's two-path model is incomplete; any platform doing this is immune to the M bit in BOTH directions regardless of which core loop it links.** ★ **THE TWO DEFECTS MASK EACH OTHER, which is why neither surfaced: RX hardcodes `false` (we IGNORE a real signal, treating even a genuine companion MCU as relay-viable) while TX emits `true` (we SEND a false signal, advertising tx-only while relaying). Opposite directions — and the RX bug is precisely what stops the TX bug producing the symptom that would have exposed it. Two independent defects, NOT one bug that cancels.** ⇒ **core's ruling stands unweakened and I am not letting the dead conjecture argue it away: M=1 at a relaying dfr1195 is a FALSE SELF-CLAIM on the wire (R2-WIRE §4.2.1 v0.45), a conformance defect independent of #63. Mine to patch, core's to rule — it ruled M MUST be 0 at the six TX sites.** ⚠ **SEQUENCING HELD AND ESCALATED, NOT DECIDED ALONE: the staged artifact `d4c65886…` is PINNED (manifest `398cf31`) awaiting a Roy-gated flash, and patching main.rs moves the bytes on six emit paths. I MUST NOT silently invalidate a staged artifact mid-flight — that is exactly the stale-artefact-vs-moved-tree divergence composer caught here once. Options put to supervisor: (A) patch AFTER the bench, my recommendation — the defect is long-standing, not a live safety risk, and no bench item measures the M bit; (B) patch now + rebuild + new sha + re-offer to Roy; (C) patch without rebuilding — REJECTED outright. NOTHING PATCHED pending the ruling.** ✎ **SECOND defect flagged and UNSCOPED: the RX hardcoding is its own patch; I have not sized it and am not claiming it.**

> **⚔ GRUNT 0.1 REFUTATION (my assigned lens: reality check — encode a REAL message and report what breaks). VERDICTS: §3 KILLED · §4 KILLED · §6 WOUNDED (not for the stated reason) · §8 SURVIVED-my-axis. Roy-authored draft; NOT ratified; attack-before-hardening was the instruction.** All numbers measured with the fleet's own `tools/comms-fitness.py` (o200k_base) on messages I actually sent today — and supervisor's polarity count-fix is live in it, which is what produced finding 1. ★ **FINDING 1 — §3+§4 CANNOT ENCODE A NEGATIVE OBLIGATION. That is a GRAMMAR failure, not a budget one, and it kills both sections for safety traffic.** §3's closed set is `ASK | TELL | DO | DONE | FAIL | NEED | GOT | UPD` — **eight performatives, not one expressing PROHIBITION** (no DENY, no HOLD, no MUST-NOT form); and §4's "CONTENT WORDS ONLY" means "MUST NOT" does not survive the register. **MEASURED on my real refutation of the scorer: v2 as sent = 535 tok, 8/8 facts. GRUNT under the 128 cap = 26 tok, 0/8 facts, REJECT. GRUNT with FULL evidence = 106 tok — INSIDE the cap — 6/8 facts, STILL REJECT, losing `MUST NOT` and `dcee2a9`, polarity reporting "7 negative obligations before, 0 after".** ⇒ **the budget was never the binding constraint; the grammar is. Supervisor's finding 4 said a budget with no capability gate becomes PRESSURE to drop a MUST NOT — it is worse: there is NO SLOT to drop it from.** ★ **FINDING 2 — GRUNT would force me to MIS-ENCODE today's live state as its OPPOSITE.** "Item 2 HELD / NO INSTRUMENT — never pass, never fail" has no performative: `TELL` asserts a fact, but a HOLD is a prohibition on judging, and the nearest fit is `FAIL item2 ; cause no-instrument` — **which says the observer FAILED. It did not; it has never been judged. A takeover reads FAIL, concludes the firmware is broken, and "fixes" working code — the exact false-red class this whole day was spent eliminating.** ★ **FINDING 3 — §4 "NO META" DIRECTLY CONTRADICTS COMMS.md §2, and both are Roy-authored.** §4 forbids restating/editorializing; COMMS.md §2 requires a refutation keep its evidence chain and says refutation reasoning MUST NOT be compressed. **The 535→106 gap is almost entirely `^` scope/mechanism lines — §4 calls them meta, COMMS.md calls them the evidence. One MUST yield in text, or every refuter guesses differently.** ~**§6 WOUNDED:** my five messages that turn measured 354/454/486/523/555 tok (mean 474), all over the 128 hard cap, none padding; §6 says over-budget MUST go to the blackboard, but §5 needs §9's ETS/`:pg`/GenServer runtime that does not exist ⇒ **today the only conformant way to obey §6 is TO DELETE EVIDENCE.** ~§8 survived my axis (cache invalidation is circuits' lens). ~§2/§5/§7 NOT attacked by me — **my silence there is not a pass.** **Open question routed to Roy, needs a ruling not an opinion: is GRUNT meant to carry SAFETY traffic at all, or only task/status coordination with refutations staying in v2? > **✅ ANSWERED core's open question — THE WORKSPACE EXCLUSION IS NOT INERTIA, so its new grep gate is the CORRECT PERMANENT FIX rather than a stopgap.** `Cargo.toml:38-44` carries the reason inline on every entry: `platforms/esp32` is a **different target triple** (`xtensa-esp32s3-espidf`, `:39`), and likewise dfr1195 (`xtensa-esp32s3-none-elf`), nrf54-lr2021 (`thumbv8m.main-none-eabi`), rak4630 (`thumbv7em-none-eabihf`), and rak4630-bootloader (a DIFFERENT embassy than the app). > **✅ SUPERVISOR FIXED MY `comms-fitness.py` FINDING (`claude-fleet dcee2a9`) — I RE-RAN IT RATHER THAN INHERITING IT, AND FOUND A RESIDUAL HOLE.** The fix holds on 6 probes, 3 of which I invented beyond my original report: MUST NOT→MUST REJECTs (polarity is flagged even when the caller declared ONLY "MUST" — the independent check earns its keep exactly there), `recipe.rs:1749`/`17490` REJECTs, SHOULD NOT→SHOULD REJECTs, an honest MUST NOT ADOPTs, a declared-MUST-NOT inversion REJECTs, and supervisor's own `:`-exclusion over-correction is genuinely closed (`repo@abc1234:src/main.rs:42` survives as one fact). ★ **RESIDUAL — COUNT-BLINDNESS: polarity is PRESENCE-based while obligation loss is COUNT-based.** `"=MUST NOT flash and MUST NOT push @d4c65886"` → `"=MUST NOT flash @d4c65886"` scores `facts_lost []`, verdict **ADOPT** — **one of TWO MUST NOT obligations silently dropped, because "MUST NOT" is still present.** **This is the ORIGINAL defect one level in: declared as presence, matched as presence, never COUNTED — the fix moved it from substring-blind to count-blind.** Live, not theoretical: fleet messages routinely carry several MUSTs (mine that turn carried four). ⇒ the polarity check SHOULD compare per-keyword OCCURRENCE COUNTS before-vs-after, not membership. ~Precision cost flagged as a CHOICE not an accident: MUST NOT→SHALL NOT REJECTs, which is a legitimate RFC 2119 synonym; defensible (keyword churn is bad) but supervisor's own crying-wolf warning applies — a scorer that rejects legal rewrites gets routed around.

> **★★★ "EXPECTATION IS WHAT MAKES A DEAD INSTRUMENT INVISIBLE" (core) — THE FINDING OF THE DAY, AND I ACTED ON IT RATHER THAN AGREEING.** Across seven instrument defects: **the ones producing WRONG findings were caught by PEERS within minutes; the ones producing the EXPECTED answer were caught ONLY by a CONTROL.** ~core diagnosed why my probe died and I could not have found it myself: **TWO `merge-tree` forms share ONE command name with DIFFERENT output** — legacy 3-arg emits a conflict diff containing markers; `--write-tree` writes a tree and signals by EXIT CODE with no markers to grep. **So my probe was not unlucky, it was STRUCTURALLY INCAPABLE of disagreeing.** A lane copying either probe MUST match the grep to the FORM. ★ **I THEN APPLIED THE RULE TO MY OWN LIVE EXPECTATION-CONFIRMING NULL AND THE FIRST CONTROL FAILED: my standing claim "r2-hive 0 carriers across 10 refs" had NO control in its own loop — expected clean, got clean, reported it TWICE. Control attempt 1 grepped a token I ASSUMED was universal (`public-content-hygiene`) and went SILENT on 3 of 10 refs — exactly the three whose missing gate WAS the finding.** ⇒ **A CONTROL THAT SHARES AN ASSUMPTION WITH THE CLAIM IS NOT A CONTROL; IT INHERITS THE BLIND SPOT. A control MUST be derived from the TARGET, not from the HYPOTHESIS.** Attempt 2 self-calibrated (derive a token from a file known to be on THAT ref, then grep it there): **DENOMINATOR 10 refs, control ALIVE 10/10, CARRYING 0 — the null is NOW readable, and was not when I first reported it.** ~core ran its own control retroactively and its probe was alive, its answer right — and it held itself to the same line I drew on myself: **"the control passing afterwards makes my LUCK good, not my METHOD sound."** Two sound answers, two unsound processes, and **zero difference in the output at the time.** ✎ Recorded durably in [[never-conclude-from-a-null]] with all six family forms.

> **✅ OPTION D EXECUTED BY core (`514d43b`) AND INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED — but MY FIRST TWO VERIFICATION ATTEMPTS WERE DEAD INSTRUMENTS THAT BOTH RETURNED THE ANSWER I EXPECTED.** Confirmed read-only, no mutation: `514d43b` IS a merge (parents `7a34d97` branch + `4c1fbbe` main), main is NOW an ancestor of the branch, and **`git merge-tree --write-tree main origin/r2-core-consolidation` ⇒ exit 0 (clean), with a LIVE CONTROL: the same probe against the true pre-merge tip `7a34d97` ⇒ exit 1 (conflicts).** The scheduled manual edit inside the security guard is GONE. ★★ **THE PROCESS FAILURE IS THE PART WORTH KEEPING: attempt 1 grepped merge-tree output for `^<<<<<<<` and got 0 — CONTROL ALSO 0, wrong output format for that merge-tree form. > **⚠ android RETRACTED its 30 s evidence-TTL claim to me (2026-07-19) and I had ALREADY moved my risk posture on it — manifest now states the TTL MUST NOT be cited as an adv+scan coexistence safety net.** It bounds a CLEAN STOP only (carrier stops, TTL expires, phone resumes ~5 s). It does NOT bound a STUCK carrier: sightings are unauthenticated BY DESIGN (`core-ffi/src/beacon.rs:350` — "No HMAC — a sighting is unauthenticated discovery, not a member Event"), there is no replay/counter/nonce in `core-ffi/src/control.rs`, and `R2UsbDriver.kt:454` stamps receipt time on EVERY valid sighting ⇒ one cached observation re-emitted under 30 s refreshes the evidence forever and holds the phone deaf indefinitely **with no attacker involved**. The gate proves a REPORT ARRIVED, not that ACQUISITION HAPPENED. **Nothing unsafe today:** `feat/carrier-ble-handoff` is HELD/unmerged, `carrierBleProven` absent from `master`, deployed APK has NO handoff ⇒ the phone's BLE cannot stand down at first light ⇒ bench unaffected, observer image needs no change. **★ Checked my own file with a POSITIVE CONTROL before claiming the clean state: `grep -i ttl` = 0 hits, and the same grep fires 6× on `d4c65886`/`bearer` and 2× on `handoff` ⇒ the null is from absence, not a broken instrument ([[never-conclude-from-a-null]]).** Counter-conjecture sent back to android on its paused fix: a periodic independent phone-scan override bounds suppression by TIME, but the poisoning is by CONTENT — consecutive-identical observation bytes are a stronger stuck-detector than a timer and cost no extra radio; asked whether core-ffi retains the raw AD post-parse to allow byte-equality.
> **✖ MY duplicate-detection counter-conjecture KILLED by android (2026-07-19) — and its premise is TRUE IN MY OWN TREE, which is where I should have checked before proposing it.** I argued consecutive-identical observation bytes beat a timer as a stuck-carrier detector. android refuted on merits AND answered the FFI question: the raw AD does NOT survive to Kotlin (`FfiSighting` = parsed fields only, `uniffi/r2_core_ffi.kt:4644-4680`), so byte-equality would need an FFI change — but the idea fails before that cost. **VERIFIED AT MY SOURCE, stronger than android's parsed-field argument: `anti_collision: 0` is HARDCODED (main.rs:3545), `LegacyBeacon` is built ONCE outside the advertise loop (main.rs:3535), and `let epoch: u64 = 0;` (main.rs:3533, comment: "epoch=0 placeholder until the shared coarse-time base wires in") ⇒ every AD byte from a stationary board is LITERALLY IDENTICAL every time.** So identical-content is the HEALTHY NORM at epoch 0 and my detector flags every healthy stationary device — false positive on the common case. The only varying field is `rssi`, which is carrier-MEASURED not in the AD, so a stuck carrier replays cached rssi too and any firmware can jitter one byte: weak and spoofable. **Time-bounded max-off watchdog CONCEDED as primary — it bounds suppression regardless of report CONTENT, the property that survives an adversary CHOOSING the content (same shape as our no-simulated-red bar).** ✎ **COUNTER-FINDING handed back on android's "MAY revisit post-rotation" variant: it would false-positive on THIS firmware permanently — `current_beacon_epoch()` (main.rs:4807) returns literal `0`, and `LORA_BEACON_T_ROTATE_S = 3600` (main.rs:4768) is referenced only by `let _ =` to silence dead-code ⇒ dfr1195 NEVER rotates rbid on either bearer, so "unchanged rbid across a T_rotate boundary is diagnostic" would fire continuously against a correctly-working board. The detector's precondition is a firmware capability that does not exist yet.** Also queried: android cites BLE `T_rotate` = 900 s, my LoRa constant is 3600 s (§8.1.3) — if the bearers genuinely differ that's fine, but one of us may hold a stale number and it should settle before either side builds on it.
> **🚨 THE FLEET'S NEW ADOPTION GATE BLESSES A SAFETY INVERSION — `comms-fitness.py` WOUNDED, reported to supervisor (claude-fleet is ITS repo; I did NOT edit it).** Roy's PROTOCOL-EVOLVES directive makes fitness = fewer tokens AND capability maintained, measured by `tools/comms-fitness.py`, with capability as a GATE not a term. **I applied today's own rule before trusting it: caller-grepped (all 5 fns wired) and RAN it (`.venv/bin/python3`, "ALL CONTROLS FIRED"). The 3 shipped negative controls are REAL — they simply do not RANGE OVER this class.** ★ **ROOT CAUSE (`:40`): `lost = [f for f in facts if f and f not in after]` — facts are DECLARED as tokens but MATCHED as UNANCHORED SUBSTRINGS.** **PROBE A, reproducible, verbatim output: before `"=MUST NOT flash board B without the Roy gate @d4c65886"` → after `"=MUST flash B @d4c65886"`, facts `["MUST","d4c65886"]` ⇒ `facts_kept 2`, `facts_lost []`, `delta -6`, `pct -37.5`, verdict **`ADOPT`**. "MUST" IS A SUBSTRING OF "MUST NOT", so the gate scores a REVERSED SAFETY DIRECTIVE as capability-preserved and RECOMMENDS it — the single most dangerous compression available in this fleet.** PROBE B: fact `recipe.rs:1749` vs after `@recipe.rs:17490` ⇒ `facts_kept 1`, `ADOPT` — a WRONG `file:line` scores as kept. ⇒ **MUST NOT treat `facts_kept` as capability-preserved until matching is BOUNDARY-ANCHORED; RFC 2119 negatives MUST be a CLOSED VOCABULARY matched LONGEST-FIRST (MUST NOT / SHALL NOT / SHOULD NOT are DISTINCT facts, never substrings of MUST / SHALL / SHOULD); and the selftest MUST gain BOTH as negative controls, else the fix is unverifiable in the direction that matters.** ★★ **Supervisor said a PROSE fitness function would have been phantom gate #6. This one is NOT phantom — it emits, and its controls fire. The defect is narrower and nastier: ITS PREDICATE CANNOT SEE THE FAILURE IT EXISTS TO CATCH. Same family as my console that does not print, my MAC probe already on the allowlist, and my scanner that cannot parse the advertiser — the fourth instance today, and the first one I caught in someone ELSE's instrument before it was used on me.**
> **⚠ codex F1-F3 ON MY OWN FRESHNESS WRITE-UP — ALL THREE CONFIRMED, landed dfr1195-fw `eac59d4` (docs-only, sha `d4c65886…` unchanged). TWO ARE ERRORS I MADE WHILE RECORDING SOMEONE ELSE'S CATCH.** **F1 — TOOL-LOCAL STALENESS IS A SECOND, INDEPENDENT DEFECT: fixing BlueZ freshness does NOT close it.** `found = {}` is initialised once (`:181`), only ever written (`:202`), never expired or cleared, and `--expect` evaluates `any(found)` (`:250-253`) ⇒ **one RBID observed at ANY point stays PASS for the WHOLE PROCESS even with a perfectly fresh BlueZ layer underneath.** Fix must expire by fresh-event time OR run each phase as an isolated cache-purged process. **F2 — MY OVER-CLAIM: I asserted "BlueZ retains the device object and its `manufacturer_data` after the advertiser stops" as FACT, then called persistence UNMEASURED in the same breath.** Inconsistent, and the assertion went past its evidence: `TEST-RIG.md:246-258` documents stale **PRE-advertiser** caching, **which is NOT evidence of POST-STOP retention.** The manifest now claims ONLY that an OFF-phase reading CAN be cached and is therefore not proof of air; **no stop-retention behaviour is asserted.** **F3 — MY MEASUREMENT PROPOSAL WAS WRONG TWICE, do not run it as written:** (a) `parse_r2_mfr` (`:109-119`) accepts only R2-shaped manufacturer data (`COMPANY_AS_EMITTED`, or `COMPANY_DOCUMENTED` with `p[0] == MAGIC`) ⇒ **an arbitrary BLE device NEVER ENTERS `found`**, so my "advertise from anything" test would have measured NOTHING and returned a clean null — **a null from an instrument that cannot see the phenomenon, which is the exact defect I have now made three times today**; a synthetic R2-shaped advertiser is REQUIRED. (b) Even run correctly, **one observed cache lifetime is implementation/config-specific and MUST NOT become an OFF-wait timeout — it can REPRODUCE the risk, it cannot SIZE the acceptance.** ⇒ **Acceptance MUST rest on an explicit fresh EVENT or a verified purge per isolated phase, NEVER on a wait bound.**

> **📡 STANDING (Roy 2026-07-19) — CAVEMAN COMPRESSION APPLIES AGENT-TO-AGENT, not just agent-to-human.** Fleet token spend is dominated by per-turn context; inter-agent messages are a large share. Unsure? Write it long; a re-ask costs more than the tokens saved. [[compress-agent-to-agent-comms]]

> **📏 STANDING (Roy 2026-07-19, relayed by supervisor) — AGENT-TO-AGENT COMMS MUST USE RFC 2119 NORMATIVE LANGUAGE.** Appended to `AGENTS.md` V2 OVERRIDE block, commit `9f883a0` on main (pure append: `git diff --numstat` = 27 added / 0 removed; 8 top-level sections before and after; `ci/public-hygiene.sh` OK). **RFC 8174 is the load-bearing half: ONLY UPPERCASE IS NORMATIVE** — lowercase "must" is prose and binds nobody, so an instruction without a capitalised keyword is INFORMATIONAL and the recipient MUST say so rather than obeying it. This COMPOSES with the compression rule instead of fighting it: RFC 2119 REPLACES hedged prose ("it would be good if this were verified before freeze" → "This MUST be verified before freeze") = shorter AND unambiguous. SHOULD = MAY deviate WITH a stated reason; MUST = MAY NOT deviate, and on inability the lane MUST STOP and report rather than work around. Do NOT capitalise for emphasis (a keyword is a contract, not a shout). RELAYED requirements MUST name the source lane so obligation and provenance stay separable.
> **📏 RULING (supervisor, fleet-wide 2026-07-19) — MEMORY.md COMPRESSION IS OFF; the discriminator is LINK DENSITY.** High link-or-reference density ⇒ index-like ⇒ DO NOT COMPRESS; prose with few refs is the only safe target. **WHY it matters more than the token count: my caveman-compress defect was LOUD on RESUME.md (headings 17→0, ~1000 inline spans, it aborted and wrote nothing) — on an INDEX the same defect is SILENT, the file still reads fine while the `[[links]]` stop resolving. Damage you cannot see is worse than damage that aborts.** Archival split does not rescue an index either (no dated tail to move). **Final fleet position on the three files: `MEMORY.md` never compress/split · `RESUME.md` manual archival split ONLY (move verbatim, diff the tail byte-identical) · `AGENTS.md` append-only, never rewrite.** hive `memory/MEMORY.md` = 19942 B, never compressed, unchanged. ✎ **Correction I sent back (source lane = hive):** the ruling quotes specs' measurement (58 links / 6 headings / 4 backtick spans in 9758 B) as fleet-wide ground; that is SPECS' file — hive's is ~2× the size and I have not measured its link density. The conclusion holds for hive on the STRUCTURAL argument, but a per-lane number MUST NOT be relayed as a fleet measurement. ✎ Supervisor also closed its own error: it had told the fleet RESUME.md was the per-turn token win; composer refuted it and hive+specs confirmed in their own trees — three lanes, no repo CLAUDE.md ⇒ **RESUME.md is takeover-read cost only. GREP THE LOADER, never assume a file auto-loads.** The RESUME splits still stand on verified ground: both specs and composer found STALE takeover headers naming merged/abandoned branches, and composer's named a branch that STILL EXISTS ⇒ a takeover would have checked it out successfully and worked dead code with no error. **A stale pointer that RESOLVES is worse than one that errors.**

> **🔒 CUSTODY / NO-LITERALS RULE (supervisor fleet-wide ruling 2026-07-17 — I VIOLATED this; see the incident note below).**
> Real attribution (hive_id / origin / tg_hash / hk) and any vector DERIVED from a real persona are SECRETS and MUST NOT appear as
> literals in ANY tracked artifact — code, comments, examples, test fixtures, docs, RESUME prose, or COMMIT MESSAGES. Documenting a
> secret IS publishing it. **The public-hygiene gate does NOT protect this class** (it matches 12-hex MAC shapes; an 8-hex hive_id /
> tg_hash sails straight through — a green gate is NOT a leak-check). Committed content stays SYNTHETIC-BY-DEFAULT; real values are
> read AT RUNTIME from gitignored custody (`~/.r2-dev-trial/*.bin`, mode 600) or env — the hive-live-view.mjs pattern. "Lock to
> PROVISIONED" ALWAYS means at RUNTIME, never "commit the values". Regenerate vectors locally via the scratchpad vecgen harness
> (parses the custody persona with r2-trust + the real r2-wire codec); hand them to peers over fleet, never via a tracked file.

ANY GATE WHOSE ACCEPTANCE SET DIFFERS FROM THE DECISION IT PROMISES ABOUT IS LYING — IN BOTH DIRECTIONS.*** The discriminator is **NOT** *"is the check structural?"* but ***"WHAT DOES THE CHECK'S OUTPUT CONTROL?"*** — **diagnostic** output ⇒ independence is right; output that **GATES passage** ⇒ it **must share the consumer's acceptance set or it lies.** ⇒ my hand-rolled walk was **RIGHT for #72** (where `parse_persona`'s blind spot WAS the defect ⇒ a second instrument was mandatory) and **WRONG for #72a** (where the question became *"will the runtime accept this aggregate?"*). **THE QUESTION MOVED AND THE INSTRUMENT DID NOT.** Already resolved in `aa9d273` — I deleted the walker before core-codex's amendment landed, for the duplicate-key divergence.

> **✅✅✅ #72(a) **LANDED AND FIRED BOTH WAYS THROUGH THE REAL GATE** — rak4630-fw `50131a7` + `5a2208e` (2026-07-17). Branch-only, unpushed, nothing flashed.**
> **SHIPPED:** `crates/r2-persona-gate` = a **BUILD-ONLY helper**; private `const ANCHORS`; single public `validate_prod(persona)` (bytes only — no table param, no clock param: neither is offered because both are what an attacker or a tired operator would want to choose); build-dep on the **VENDORED** r2-trust; calls `DeviceCertificate::verify`, never reimplements. `build.rs` calls it **unconditionally** — there is no env var to leave unset, so **no absent-input branch to fail open through.**
> **★ THE ANCHOR LITERAL VERIFIES ITSELF:** `anchor_table_is_self_consistent` asserts every entry satisfies canon's `tg_id == UUID-RAW(SHA-256(tg_pk)[0:16])`. **A hardcoded 32-byte key is NOT an unverifiable literal when the table checks itself** — a typo breaks the relation and fails the build. **That was the last objection to consts, and the relation I derived from bytes this morning is what answers it.**
> **CONTROLS — THROUGH THE GATE, NOT THE PREDICATE:** **positive** = `rak-persona.bin` + anchored TG → `credential VERIFIED — tg_id=730c29e7… role=Member (TG-attested, not self-asserted)`, thumbv7em **FINISHED** · **negative** = **SAME ARTIFACT**, anchor swapped away → `REFUSING TO BAKE AN UNTRUSTED PERSONA / UnknownTrustGroup`, build **FAILED**. **Same artifact, varied anchor, both directions.** Plus **10 helper unit tests** minting a throwaway TG **in memory** (chosen AND synthetic — the correctly-scoped use of the seed rule; **no artifact exists on disk to be mistaken for an image candidate — the THIRD and cleanest kill of composer's gate-test-TG offer**): matching anchor ACCEPTS · **internally-coherent-but-FOREIGN-issuer REJECTS** (composer's face-four made concrete — *self-consistency is NOT authenticity*) · unknown TG · empty cert · cross-paired key0/key5 · window NotYetValid/ACCEPT/Expired · signature byte-flip · **key5≠anchor (constraint 4)**.
> **CORE'S CONSTRAINT 4 — LANDED THOUGH ALREADY CLOSED TRANSITIVELY, AND THAT IS THE POINT:** self-consistency ⇒ `key0==uuid(key5)`; lookup ⇒ `anchor.tg_id==key0`; table test ⇒ `anchor.tg_id==uuid(anchor.tg_pk)` ∴ `key5==anchor.tg_pk`. **REFUSED TO DEPEND ON IT: the middle link is a TEST not a GATE — delete the test and the proof evaporates SILENTLY while every build stays green — and the last step leans on second-preimage resistance of a 128-BIT-TRUNCATED hash.** One direct comparison needs neither. *Make the bad state unrepresentable; don't reason about why it can't arise.* Its control fires **directly** (persona self-consistent for A; table maps A's tg_id to **B's key**) so self-consistency **cannot** be what catches it.
> **★★ TWO INSTRUMENT FAILURES I CAUGHT ON MYSELF WHILE BUILDING IT — both are shapes I had banked hours earlier:** **(1) MY FIRST NEGATIVE CONTROL WAS INVALID** — the staged repeater persona failed on the **OLD #72 empty-cert check and NEVER REACHED #72a**. It has **both** defects and the earlier gate **short-circuits**. I nearly banked *"the build failed"* as proof of anchor discrimination. **Verifying logic AFTER a gate cannot catch a GATE failure — and this time the gate in front was MINE.** **(2) MY ATTRIBUTION LOG WAS A DOUBLE-COUNT** — `issuer_anchor_fp` digested the matched **KEY**, but `tg_id` **IS** `uuid(sha256(tg_pk)[0:16])`, so that fingerprint is literally the tg_id prefix. **A line whose entire purpose was INDEPENDENT attribution was restating the persona's own claim as corroboration** — **android's exact catch on composer's bind evidence, sitting UNREAD in my inbox while I made it.** Now digests the anchor **TABLE** (`fp=cd5eeb9f`): independent, and it changes when the table does.
> **★★★ NEW FINDING → TASK #75 — THE BOOTLOADER'S `0x22000` OTA TRUST ANCHOR IS COMPLETELY UNGATED.** core's constraint-4 premise was **MIS-AIMED at my gate** (it thought the bootloader's key5 was the persona my gate validates) — but **its SHAPE was right and pointed somewhere it did not follow: *"ask WHICH VALUE THE CONSUMER READS."*** Asked properly, **per consumer**: **APP (baked build) reads `BAKED_PERSONA` rodata (main.rs:490) ⇒ #72a covers it · BOOTLOADER reads FLASH `0x22000` (`r2_trust::persona_tg_pk`, bootloader main.rs:34; rak-geometry consts.rs:11 *"sealed TG_PK anchor — read by BOTH app + bootloader"*) ⇒ NOTHING COVERS IT · APP (non-baked) also reads `0x22000` ⇒ also uncovered.** **TWO DIFFERENT ARTIFACTS — different storage, different bytes, no build-time relationship.** **`0x22000` is the UPDATE AUTHORITY** and has **zero** build-time validation. **#72 closed the funnel from a bad persona to a RADIATING app; it did NOT close the funnel from a bad persona to a TRUSTED UPDATE PATH.** **UNMEASURED, DO NOT GUESS:** how is `0x22000` written? (a) same host tooling ⇒ wants the same gate · (b) only Channel-A ⇒ BOM-blocked with #74 · **(c) NOBODY ⇒ the bootloader reads an EMPTY/STALE partition as its update authority — the worst of the three.** Opened as a task rather than banking a story.
> **core's correction of MY over-correction, accepted:** *"you did not win a concession with a non-applicable argument in any way you should regret — your production argument KILLED const-in-a-shared-crate, which was correct and load-bearing. It just did not reach the helper, and NOBODY had the helper yet, so no argument in play could have."* Fair. **An argument that correctly kills the option on the table is not defective because a better option later appears outside its scope.** The regret-worthy version would be *claiming* it reaches the helper — neither of us did.

> **✅✅ #72(a) MECHANISM **RULED** — CONST IN A **BUILD-ONLY HELPER CRATE**; core REVERSED its concession and the synthesis is NEITHER lane's original (core a64e858, 2026-07-17).**
> **THE THREE-WAY RESOLUTION:** **(i) const-in-a-SHARED-crate** — killed by **my** production argument (correctly) · **(ii) env build-input** — killed by **core's** anchor-mutability argument (*"a trust anchor that can change without a commit is not an anchor"*; *"an env var is a value someone TYPES; a const is a value someone REVIEWS"*) · **(iii) CONST IN A SEPARATE BUILD-ONLY HELPER** — **beats both, and was neither of ours.** It exists **only because composer refused to let my "we settled it" stand.**
> **★★ CORE'S REVERSAL CUTS AGAINST ME AND I CONCEDE IT PLAINLY: I WON A CONCESSION WITH AN ARGUMENT THAT DOES NOT REACH THE ANSWER.** I asked core to re-examine on the production argument alone; it did and found **more than I asked** — my objection (*"a real TG's pk must not be baked into a SHARED CRATE"*) **is an argument about a SHARED RUNTIME CRATE. A build-only helper NEVER SHIPS IN THE IMAGE, so the objection does not reach it.** **And the cleaner point neither of us made: a `tg_pk` IS PUBLIC** — there was never a *secrecy* reason to keep an anchor out of a const. **The only real objection was shared-with-the-runtime, and the helper deletes it.** *An anchor is SUPPOSED to be baked and reviewed — that is what an anchor IS.*
> **CORE'S CONSTRAINT 1:** the helper holds the **TABLE**; **r2-trust holds the VERIFY** — the helper MUST call `DeviceCertificate::verify` and **never grow its own** (the gate's question is *"WILL THE RUNTIME ACCEPT THIS?"* — only the runtime's predicate answers it; an independent impl is a **second opinion, not a stronger one**, and it drifts).
> **CORE'S CONSTRAINT 2:** the const table MUST be **PRIVATE** with a **SINGLE public production entry** — *"if the validation fn is public AND takes the table as a parameter, build.rs can pass any table and you are back to a value someone types — **unswappable leaks through the parameter**."* Shape: private `const ANCHORS` · `pub fn validate_prod(persona)` taking **only** the bytes · **cfg-test injection INSIDE the helper**.
> **⚠️ MY CONSTRAINT 3 — NOT A PROPOSAL, A **LIVE DEFECT IN MY OWN CONTROLS**: THE HELPER MUST LINK THE **SAME r2-trust THE IMAGE LINKS** (the VENDORED one), AND THE MATCH MUST BE **CHECKED, NEVER ASSUMED**.** **MEASURED:** `platforms/rak4630/Cargo.toml:110` → `r2-trust = { path = "../../crates/r2-trust" }` = **VENDORED**; **my scratchpad rig linked `/home/roycdavies/Development/R2/r2-core/crates/r2-trust` = THE LIVE CORE CHECKOUT.** ⇒ **EVERY CONTROL I REPORTED FIRED AGAINST A DIFFERENT COPY OF THE CRATE THAN THE IMAGE RUNS.** Diffed after the fact: vendored `cert.rs` is **BYTE-IDENTICAL** to live ⇒ **my controls DO transfer — BY LUCK, NOT BY CONSTRUCTION.** **In THIS repo that was a live coin-flip: #71 EXISTS PRECISELY BECAUSE A VENDORED COPY IS STALE.** The vendored **dataplane** drifted; the vendored **r2-trust** happened not to. **⇒ MY CONCLUSION SURVIVES; MY METHOD DID NOT ESTABLISH IT.** And **#71 will MOVE the vendored copy — today's match is not tomorrow's.** Core's constraint 1 *implies* this but doesn't say it, and the implication is where it bites: **a wrong path in a manifest silently converts the gate's question into *"will SOME runtime accept this?"*** See [[shared-checkout-path-dep-coupling]], [[tn-base-is-mixed-sha-assembly]].
> **OPEN INTERACTION (asked core to rule): `validate_prod` must select WHICH anchor by the persona's OWN `tg_id` (key0) — *the input choosing its own judge*, the family we hunted all night.** **My read: SAFE** — selecting a *legitimate* table anchor doesn't help an attacker who cannot forge a signature for a TG whose sk they lack; the lookup picks the judge, but the judge is incorruptible. **BUT ⇒ `validate_prod(persona)` ALONE CANNOT ENFORCE "this image is for TG X"** — any persona whose tg_id is in the table builds fine. **That is exactly what `RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID` is for, and it lands on core's OWN split: the ANCHOR = private const (unswappable, absence = compile error); the EXPECTATION = env var in build.rs (optional but LOUD when unset). Two legs, two mechanisms, for a principled reason — only the ANCHOR may not be typeable.**

> **R2-KEYSTORE §9:463-485 requires ALL THREE hardware roots for a PERSISTENT CLAIM-STATE profile:** **(a)** irreversible OTP VIRGIN sentinel · **(b)** a **DEDICATED MONOTONIC HARDWARE `hw_epoch` COUNTER** — canon's words, ***"the SOLE anti-rollback and linearisation root"*** · **(c)** a per-device HUK/SE key from which `K_slot` **AND** `K_persona` derive. **§9:485 verbatim: *"A platform lacking ANY of these three roots MUST FAIL CLOSED at build / provision time."***
> **MY SPIKE #73 ASKED ABOUT (c). THE PART CANON-LACKS (b).** **VERIFIED MYSELF FROM SPEC TEXT** (two lanes were citing canon at me; after tonight I take neither's say-so): **§9:489-492** — *"parts without an on-die OTP monotonic counter — **e.g. nRF52840/RAK4630** — MUST pair an external secure element (ATECC608 / NervesKey / TPM) … **else they are non-persistent-only**"* · **R2-UPDATE §9.2:1119** — *"**Honest platform delta — nRF52840 has NO HW-OTP counter (the RAK4630 backend).**"* · **§9** — *"There is **NO software-only persistent claim-state**; hardware-where-available is **NOT permitted**."*
> **⇒ EVEN A PERFECT POSITIVE ON (c) CHANGES NOTHING** — the part still lacks (b), remedy is the same external SE either way. **THE SPIKE COULD ONLY CHANGE *WHICH* ROOT I'M MISSING, NEVER THE OUTCOME.** Channel-A **IS** a persistent claim-state profile (§5.1.1 stages at `hw_epoch+1` → marker → **increments `hw_epoch`** = root (b)). **⇒ CONFORMANT-PERSISTENT CHANNEL-A ON A BARE RAK4630 IS A *ROY BOM DECISION*, NOT AN ENGINEERING SCHEDULE.** Canon defers the per-board matrix to *"a **Roy-gated R2-HW reconciliation**"*. **No date until Roy rules the BOM.**

> **⚖️ SUPERVISOR'S SEED SPLIT — REFUTED (chosen-vs-derived is the WRONG TEST HERE).** It proposed: TG seed = published-by-design (rule 8 recomputability), master seed = the real leak. **BOTH are the same class and it is the LEAK class.** **(1) CHOSEN ≠ SYNTHETIC — two axes collapsed:** CHOSEN-vs-RANDOM = how bytes are GENERATED; SYNTHETIC-vs-REAL = what they PROTECT. **Determinism doesn't make a key fake — it makes it reproducible, which is exactly what makes publishing the seed identical to publishing the key.** **(2) The contrast class is in MY OWN RESUME:** `uuid(0x42*32)` / `hive(0xAA*32)` = chosen **AND** synthetic (no board runs them) ⇒ *those* are rule-8 artifacts; the repeater TG is **chosen-but-LIVE** (minted to be baked; it WAS staged `ee3b7791`). **(3) GROUND TRUTH composer does NOT treat it as published-by-design:** its own `tg.txt` header says **"SENSITIVE: tg_sk + master secrets in plaintext"**; it lives in **mode-600 custody**, not a docs dir; composer's own words — its derivation *"needs a custody-unlocked run"*. **(4) THE KILLER — rule 8 does NOT compel publishing this seed: recomputability requires the PUBLIC key be checkable, and VERIFYING A PUBLIC KEY NEVER REQUIRES PUBLISHING THE GENERATOR OF THE PRIVATE ONE.** tg_pk could have been handed directly (it already sits in this file classified public). **The auditability requirement is satisfied ONE BIT SHORT of the disclosure.** **(5) The split is unstable — siblings from one file, same construction/batch/custody: applied consistently it makes both benign (false) or both leaks (true).**

EVERY leak instrument we built matches the SHAPE OF THE OUTPUT (hex); a seed has the shape of PROSE ⇒ all of them were STRUCTURALLY BLIND, not merely unlucky:** the hygiene gate (12-hex MAC shapes) → **green**; my width-RANGE sweep (`{8,}`/`{32,}`) → **no hex in a seed at all**; and **the 342-token "SYSTEMATIC IDENTITY SWEEP" (line ~16) extracted *7-8-hex tokens* ⇒ it COULD NOT have found this class in principle.** ⇒ **THAT SWEEP'S COMPLETENESS CLAIM DOES NOT COVER GENERATORS** — supervisor verified it, and the endorsement propagated the gap (peer praise is not coverage). **Same error shape as the empty-cert: a positive control that fires on the fields it can see, and is incapable of ranging over the one in question.** **DOCTRINE FIX (owed to specs as gate owner): a leak-scan MUST scan for GENERATORS — prose seeds, passphrases, derivation recipes — not only hex outputs. THE RECIPE IS WORTH EXACTLY WHAT THE VALUE IS WORTH.**
> **★ AND THE MIRROR, RECORDED HONESTLY: in the very message where I warned composer that *"your auditability rests on tg_sk being derivable from a published string — fine for dev-trial, catastrophic in production"*, MY OWN TRACKED FILE HAD BEEN CARRYING THAT EXACT STRING FOR HOURS.** I diagnosed the disease in composer's design while carrying it in my own repo — the third time tonight this shape has fired (core: *"my own disease pointed back at me"*). **The gap is not knowing the rule; it is never turning the rule on my own artifact.** ⇒ **after stating a principle about a peer's work, immediately run it against your own.** See [[never-conclude-from-a-null]], [[identity-verified-is-not-function-verified]].

> **🛑🛑 RED — THE STAGED RAK CANNOT RELAY D4's COMPACT FRAME; IDENTITY ✓ BUT RELAY-FUNCTION ✗ (2026-07-17, supervisor's will-actually-work challenge — android's flag CONFIRMED).** My 3-way confirm-match proved the RAK **is** the right node; it NEVER proved the RAK can **decode** what D4 sends. Verified at source, both halves:
>   - **D4 originates COMPACT on LoRa** — dfr1195 main.rs:117-119 *"R2-LORA §5.1 compact-on-LoRa (core 2026-07-10): the LoRa bearer originates COMPACT"* → `encode_compact`/`sign_compact`; the ef6f95a design EXCLUDES extended from the LoRa arm. On LoRa, D4 sends compact ONLY.
>   - **The RAK's VENDORED dataplane (4a3f57d) decodes EXTENDED-ONLY** — `crates/r2-dataplane/src/lib.rs:517` `match decode_extended(frame) { Err(_) => return no }`; NO `decode_compact` anywhere (positive control: grep fired on decode_extended ×5; the 7 "compact" hits are all Compact-CBOR keepalive PAYLOAD + §16.6 comments, not wire-frame decode). RAK main.rs sets NO `WireFormat` (real null: the vendored dataplane has no such type).
>   - **⇒ The RAK calls `decode_extended` on D4's compact frame → `Err` → SILENT DROP.** (Even an accidental Ok would misparse the u16-vs-u32 msg_id / route → wrong origin → no correct relay. No branch relays compact correctly.)
>   - **WHY MY PRIOR "MECHANISM VERIFIED" MISSED IT (proxy-boundary trap, [[never-conclude-from-a-null]]):** I verified the F2/authenticated EXCLUSION logic (lib.rs:126/:620/:669 — "different-TG member relays auth-free") — TRUE, but that logic runs AFTER decode. The frame dies at step-1 decode and never reaches the exclusion I checked. I verified the relay LOGIC, not the DECODE GATE in front of it.
>   - **CORE HAS THE FIX (canonical r2-dataplane @9d742dc): `decode_compact` + `WireFormat` enum + `set_wire_format` + tier-dispatched `handle_rx_frame` (:817/:858). Core's own comment names this exact bug — :860 "a compact-radio node that decoded extended would silently drop every [frame]"; :345 "a constrained-radio platform (LoRa/FLRC/BLE) MUST call this with WireFormat::Compact at construction, else its compact frames are decoded as extended and dropped."** ⇒ FIX = **RE-VENDOR, not core-write.**
>   - **FIX SCOPE (hive-owned, my rebuild):** (1) re-vendor `crates/r2-dataplane` from core @9d742dc into rak4630-fw-wt; (2) main.rs must declare `WireFormat::Compact` on EVERY DataPlane arm (750/760/781/793 — the RAK is always a LoRa node; core's `new()` has no tier arg, tier is set via `set_wire_format`, so main.rs edits are REQUIRED beyond the re-vendor); (3) rebuild no_std thumbv7em; (4) re-verify identity UNCHANGED (persona bakes the same) PLUS a compact-decode→relay trace. **GOOD NEWS: RAK's vendored r2-wire ALREADY exposes decode_compact/encode_compact/classify_compact_full/sign_compact/CompactMessage (compact.rs:14/67, hmac.rs:171/401) — likely dataplane-only re-vendor, but the newer dataplane's `handle_rx_frame`/`DataPlane::new` signatures may ripple into main.rs; MUST verify no_std compile.**
>   - **ROY IS NOT CLEAR TO FLASH the current staged ee3b7791 for a WORKING end-to-end reading — the RAK would silent-drop D4's frame.** ⚠ At 30cm the DIRECT D4→XIAO path (route_len=1) masks this: a naive presence-check PASSES with the RAK relaying nothing (decorative repeater) — the EXACT thing the RAK-off counterfactual (route_len=2 must vanish, route_len=1 remains) is designed to expose. Without this fix the "2-hop relay" demo is indistinguishable from "1-hop direct."
>   - **⚠ SCOPE CORRECTED — NOT dataplane-only (my "likely dataplane-only" hope REFUTED by evidence; verify-then-record caught the under-scope).** Diffed the two crates: `handle_rx_frame` signature is IDENTICAL (RX-loop call at main.rs:954 unchanged, GOOD), but core's `DataPlane::new` @9d742dc added a **`my_build_mode: BuildMode`** arg (feeding `RouteEngine::new(my_build_mode)`), which the vendored `new` lacks. RAK firmware has only a BUILD_MODE_TAG **string** (main.rs:605), NOT the BuildMode **type**; vendored `RouteEngine::new()` (r2-route engine.rs:234) takes **zero args**. BuildMode is defined in **r2-route** (neighbour.rs:87). ⇒ the re-vendor is a **coupled multi-crate uptake**: r2-route (BuildMode enum + mode-viability, core a5d2d7e) + dataplane (compact tier 215fce2 + build_mode new-sites f87aac9) + main.rs threading a BuildMode value into all 4 DataPlane::new sites + set_wire_format(Compact). **Core history proves there is NO compact-fix SHA WITHOUT BuildMode** — 215fce2 (compact) sits ON TOP of a5d2d7e/f87aac9 (BuildMode). This overlaps hive's own in-progress task #50 (R2-BUILDMODE).

Diff vs core = **13 lines in src/beacon.rs, ALL doc-comment; the class_hash VALUE is byte-identical `[0x00,0xfc,0x1f,0x17]`. ZERO logic.** A wholesale replace clobbers a COMMENT. > **★ CORE'S "INVERTED RISK" RE-INVERTED — THE STAGED RAK IS *NOT* DEAF (verified at source, positive-controlled, 2026-07-17).** core retracted its sx1262 clobber-fear (direction misread — matching my independent finding) and replaced it with: *"the danger is the STAGED FIRMWARE IS RUNNING WITHOUT core's duty-cycle/RX-arming path."* **TRUE as stated, MIS-STATED as a risk.** Vendored r2-sx1262 has `SET_RX = 0x82` (continuous SetRx), `fn listen()` :525 ("enable the RX path (RXEN HIGH) before SetRx"), `fn read()` :554 → RxInfo; main.rs RX loop = `radio.poll()` → `RadioEvent::RxDone` → `radio.read()` → `handle_rx_frame(..., PHY_LORA, ...)`. **A complete, working CONTINUOUS RX path.** core's `listen_duty_cycle`/`set_rx_standby`/`set_rx_continuous` are the **SetRxDutyCycle (0x94) POWER-SAVING** path — an enhancement; missing them costs POWER, not hearing. **⇒ THE RISK INVERTS AGAIN: for a USB-powered bench, CONTINUOUS RX is the SAFER mode (it cannot miss); duty-cycled RX would ADD the [[setrxdutycycle-preamble-sizing]] hazard (rxPeriod+sleepPeriod ≤ TX preamble airtime, else HARD-MISS). Recommendation: take the APIs in a snapshot if we escalate, but do NOT enable duty-cycled RX for the demo.** Corroborated by history: first light RAN; nbrs=0 was SF-attributable (DFR SF7 vs RAK SF12) ⇒ RX was alive, hence **benchsf7 MANDATORY**.
>   - **METHOD NOTE (4th near-miss, caught by my own rule): my first 3 RX greps returned EMPTY and I did NOT report them.** The positive control showed the crate has 8 `pub fn` + real RX symbols ⇒ the nulls were **my scope** (core's duty-cycle names live in r2-transport; the RAK's LoRa RX isn't where I grepped — those hits were USB CDC), not absence. Reporting them would have been a false "the RAK never arms RX" alarm.
>   - **core's TWO live questions — ANSWERED:** **(1) any GENUINE firmware-only hardware fix? NO** — the closure gate settles it by construction: a byte-exact PRISTINE copy contains zero firmware-local code, and 19/20 are pristine at core-lineage bases; the ONLY hive-local work is r2-discovery's 13-line doc comment. `relay_as923_nz`/`leaf_as923_nz` are in the vendored copy because they're in its BASE (core@1275732) = core's own historical code, later removed at c4c0681 as forbidden per-role overrides; zero production consumers ⇒ replace removes them harmlessly. **(2) whole-crate-tree vendor unit — ALREADY SATISFIED** (my gate v2/closure compares every tracked file, both directions — that's what exposed my false r2-wire base). core's manifest point CONFIRMED + material: firmware r2-trust/r2-engine manifests match their OLDER bases (3e15d75/fbee20d) ⇒ diverge from the pin (core has ed25519-dalek `features=[rand_core]`, r2-engine adds `sha2`) ⇒ **new src on an old manifest = missing dep/feature. RUNBOOK: re-vendor takes WHOLE TREES and REGENERATES the firmware workspace lock from the pinned manifests.**
>   - **composer CONCEDED step 3.5 was ITS instruction** ("copy main.rs verbatim") — refined rule banked: **anchor verbatim on the CONSTRUCTION (call shape), NEVER on the FILE, across a purpose boundary**; the anchor heuristic silently assumes the anchor is a superset/equivalent of the target — core's main.rs is SMALLER with a DIFFERENT PURPOSE (bring-up, not product). **MEASURE both files before accepting any "copy X verbatim."**
>   - **★ composer's DURABLE INSIGHT (the real prize of the gate exercise): my scope bugs are SPECIFIC TO *SEARCHING FOR AN UNKNOWN BASE*.** composer never had them because composer always had a MANIFEST — it **VERIFIES against a DECLARED pin, never SEARCHES for one**. Immune by structure. **A declared pin is not bookkeeping — it ELIMINATES AN ENTIRE CLASS OF INFERENCE ERROR.** rak4630-fw had no manifest ⇒ I had to search ⇒ the scope bit, three times. **`crates/_VERSIONS.toml` (rak4630-fw 8a66d9c) closes it permanently — that is the bigger deliverable than the shas.** Also composer: the count moved 18→37→38 across three measurements while the CONCLUSION (clean contiguous forward-move, pristine, replace-safe) held every time — **the number was never load-bearing; that is what a robust conclusion looks like.**

> **▶▶ REBUILD REQUIREMENTS — PINNED BY SUPERVISOR (2026-07-17). Three, all load-bearing, all already in the runbook; consolidated here so they are not scattered:**
>   1. **`benchsf7` IS MANDATORY — it is the THIRD SILENT-FAILURE GATE.** Evidence (my first-light corroboration, which supervisor made the key fact): the RAK's `nbrs=0` was **SF-ATTRIBUTABLE** (DFR SF7 vs RAK SF12) — **the RX path was ALIVE and heard nothing purely from the SF mismatch.** ⇒ **without `benchsf7` the RAK is DEAF regardless of a perfect compact decode.** **The three silent gates each produce "no reading" with NO error: (a) compact decode [the RED], (b) the bridge leg [REFUTED — XIAO is compact-native], (c) SF match [benchsf7].** All three must hold; any one fails silently. See [[shared-radio-config-is-a-base-not-a-guarantee]].
>   2. **Do NOT ENABLE duty-cycled RX on the bench — stay CONTINUOUS.** Take core's 0x94 APIs as part of a snapshot; **do not turn them on.** SX1262 0x94 requires `(rxPeriod + sleepPeriod) <= TX preamble airtime` or **HARD-MISS**; on USB power continuous RX **cannot miss**, so duty-cycling would ADD a failure mode we do not have. [[setrxdutycycle-preamble-sizing]].
>   3. **WHOLE TREES + REGENERATE the workspace lock from the PINNED MANIFESTS.** core's manifest point is material: firmware r2-trust/r2-engine manifests match their OLDER bases (3e15d75/fbee20d) ⇒ **new src on an old manifest = missing dep/feature** (core has ed25519-dalek `features=[rand_core]`; r2-engine adds `sha2`).

It is fail-closed for **DELIVERY** but **fail-OPEN for IDENTITY**: a wrong/corrupt persona silently yields a **RADIATING KEYLESS RELAY**, violating Roy's ABSOLUTE no-TG-less canon ("there is no device with group = none") + forbidden-to-radiate.

[[never-conclude-from-a-null]] says verbatim: *"we UNDER-AUDIT DE-ESCALATIONS because they lower the stakes… a softening claim needs the SAME positive control as a hardening one… applies to my own de-escalations too."* **I wrote the rule, then did the thing — on my OWN firmware's defect, where the incentive to soften is highest.** composer, verbatim: *"a fail-OPEN that happens to be fed good input is still fail-open; the next build is the one that bites."* **Correct: my ELF proof is an IDENTITY fact about THIS artifact; the defect is a CONTROL-FLOW fact. > **🛑🛑🛑 FLASH-BLOCKER — THE STAGED PERSONA HAS AN EMPTY CERTIFICATE. `ee3b7791` WAS NEVER FLASHABLE. (core-codex filed, core re-derived, I VERIFIED FROM THE BYTES, 2026-07-17.)**
>   - **MEASURED (my own independent hand-decode of the 188B `persona-rak-repeater.bin`):** `a7` map(7); key `0x00` text(36) tg_id; `0x01/0x02/0x03` bytes(32) dek/hk/master; **★ key `0x04` → header `0x40` = bytes(0) = EMPTY CERT**; `0x05` bytes(32) tg_pk; `0x06` uint. **NEGATIVE CONTROL — and it sat in the SAME DIRECTORY the whole time: `rak-persona.bin` / `d4-persona.bin` / `xiao-persona.bin` (336B each) ALL carry key04 = `04 58 93` = bytes(147) = a real cert147.** `336-188 = 148` = exactly the missing cert + header — the arithmetic confirms the decode.
>   - **★★★ WHY MY "EXEMPLARY" 3-WAY PROOF MISSED IT — THE DEEPEST LESSON OF THE CAMPAIGN, and it detonated MY OWN RULE ON MY OWN FLAGSHIP PROOF.** `tg_hash`/`wire_id`/`rbid` **all derive from key0 (tg_id) + key3 (master) (+ key2 hk)**. So my confirm-match ranged over keys **0/1/2/3/5** and was **STRUCTURALLY INCAPABLE** of saying anything about **key 4**. core's formulation, exactly right: **"A PROOF THAT THE GOOD FIELDS ARE GOOD IS NOT A PROOF THAT THE BAD FIELD IS ABSENT."** **My positive control DID fire — on the wrong fields.** ⇒ **SCOPE-IS-PART-OF-THE-METHOD, sharpened: a positive control must fire ON THE FIELD IN QUESTION, not merely somewhere in the artifact.** I taught the fleet that rule tonight; my flagship proof violated it, and three lanes (supervisor "exemplary", composer "the model", core "the right kind of evidence") all praised it — **peer praise is not coverage.**
>   - **★ COMPOUNDING — THE INSTRUMENT WAS THE BLIND SPOT: my verification tool was `r2_trust::parse_persona`, and it returns `Ok` on an empty cert.** The tool I verified WITH is the tool that CANNOT SEE the defect. ⇒ core's fix is the right SHAPE: **require cert147 BY TYPE so an empty cert is UNREPRESENTABLE — a CONSTRUCTION, not a check** ([[never-conclude-from-a-null]]'s "convert convention → construction"). **It makes my old proof impossible to write.** core's hardened parser will make the CURRENT artifact FAIL TO PARSE — that is the point; re-mint and fix land together.
>   - **★ IDENTITY, THIRD AXIS, SAME DAY: identity ≠ FUNCTION (the compact silent-drop) · identity ≠ CONTROL-FLOW (the fail-open) · identity ≠ COMPLETENESS (this).** I proved the persona **IS** the right identity; never that it is a **COMPLETE** persona. **One artifact, three axes, and I kept re-verifying the axis I had already verified.** [[identity-verified-is-not-function-verified]].
>   - **SAME WOUND AS #72:** build.rs embeds `RAK_PERSONA_PATH` **raw, no parse** (:96-107) ⇒ an invalid persona is embedded silently; main.rs then maps parse-failure → **RADIATING KEYLESS relay** (:778-789 logs VALID + enables GroupHmac). **A persona invalid in a way `parse_persona` cannot see is the worst case of both.**

>   - **HARNESS: `scratchpad/derivemap`** — a cargo bin on the **REAL crate** `r2-trust` (features=[std]). NOT a re-implementation; NOT the original `persona_map.py` (session-scoped scratchpad, gone) ⇒ **re-running against the canonical crate is STRONGER than re-running my old script.**
>   - **DERIVATION:** `parse_persona() → Persona.hive_id`, computed internally per **hkdf.rs:145** `derive_hive_id(master_secret, tg_id) = fnv1a_32(uuid(HKDF(master,"r2-hive-id-v1",tg_id)[0:16]))` ⇒ **hive_id is DERIVED from key3(master)+key0(tg_id), never stored.**
