>   - **NULL EXPLAINED (never leave one dangling):** the "1 failed to parse" = `weave-hk.bin`, a 32-byte RAW HK swept in by my `*.bin` filter. Benign. **AND I HIT COMPOSER'S TRAP MYSELF, HOURS AFTER BANKING IT: my custody listing used `ls | head -10` — the head had hidden the very file that produced the null.** Re-ran with `wc -l`: 6 files.
> **★★ ROOT CAUSE OF THE EMPTY-CERT FLASH-BLOCKER — TWO PERSONA FORMATS, and the difference IS the cert:** **188B ⇒ key04 = `04 40` = bytes(0) EMPTY** · **336B ⇒ key04 = `04 58 93` = bytes(147) cert147**. `~/r2-weave-tg` = **5 × 188B, ALL empty-cert** (on the weave boards since Jul 2); `~/.r2-dev-trial` rak/d4/xiao = **336B, real cert147**; **composer's new chosen-seed repeater persona (Jul 16) = 188B, EMPTY.** ⇒ **the replacement came out of the SAME no-cert generation path as the old weave set — NOT a corrupt file, NOT a one-off: a GENERATION-PATH difference.** Fix belongs there; and the **ARTIFACT** must be checked (336B + key04 `04 58 93`) before staging — **verify the artifact, not the process.**
>   - **⚠ THE UNCOMFORTABLE COROLLARY: the weave boards have run EMPTY-CERT personas since Jul 2 and nothing broke ⇒ NOTHING CURRENTLY VERIFIES THE CERT.** `parse_persona` returns Ok because an empty cert parses to **`Some(&[])`, not `None`**. **That is why core's fix must be BY TYPE (unrepresentable), not another check: the cert is currently DECORATIVE, so every check that could have caught this was structurally incapable of it — mine included.**
>   - **METHOD NOTE: the fleet key gate false-positived on my REPORT prose** (it matches words, not acts — same class as [[espflash-trips-firmware-gate]]). Reworded and resent; flagged the false-positive to supervisor.


> **✅✅ TASK #72 LANDED — THE FAIL-OPEN-INTO-RADIATION FUNNEL IS CLOSED (rak4630-fw `56f6cae`, branch-only, no push, no flash, 2026-07-17).** supervisor GO'd the sequencing (**#72 FIRST + standalone, re-vendor on top** — *"the hold was on the re-vendor and the flash; it was never a hold on safety work in your own repo"*); core ruled the composition (**BOTH layers**).
>   - **(1) build.rs VALIDATE-BEFORE-EMBED** — hand-rolled CBOR walk, **deliberately NOT via `parse_persona`**. core's reason and it is the crux: *that parser returns `Ok` on an empty cert, so the instrument used to verify the artifact was constitutionally unable to report the defect — a defence-in-depth layer whose only check routes through the component that already had the blind spot is not defence in depth.* Rejects: non-map / truncated / missing key0|key4 / **EMPTY cert (key4=`0x40`)** / non-bytes cert / wrong tg_id vs optional `RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID`. **Build fails.**
>   - **(2) main.rs HARD STOP** — the invalid arm now **DIVERGES** instead of building a keyless DataPlane and falling through to `radio.configure()` ~10 lines below ⇒ **"never radiate" is true BY CONSTRUCTION (compiler-proven no path), not by convention.** **Async loop, NOT `panic!`** — executor stays alive so USB-CDC log + LED stay observable with no probe and USB-DFU re-provisioning still works; a panic would take the log down and leave a dark board with no reason on the wire.
>   - **★ VERIFIED WITH REAL CONTROLS — I tested my own gate the way I have been demanding others test theirs, against REAL artifacts:** **NEGATIVE:** the ACTUAL staged empty-cert persona (188B) ⇒ **BUILD FAILS** (*"REFUSING TO BAKE AN INVALID PERSONA / CERTIFICATE IS EMPTY (key 4 = 0x40 = bytes(0))"*) — the gate fires on the exact artifact that was staged and nearly flashed. **POSITIVE:** real cert147 persona (336B) ⇒ *"validated (336 bytes, certificate present) — baking"*, no false-positive. **COMPILE:** clean, thumbv7em, 11.17s. *(A gate reporting OK is not evidence until its KATs prove it catches the thing — so I proved it catches THE thing.)*
>   - **OWED, NAMED IN-FILE (explicit, not implied): (a) cert SIGNATURE + validity WINDOW at BUILD time** — core-codex's catch: feeding the **untrusted bundle's own `issued_at`** into a verifier = **expiry self-authorized**. build.rs is the only place with a trusted clock. **⚠ MECHANISM — MY ANSWER WAS OVERRULED BY CORE, AND CORE IS RIGHT. IT IS A CONST IN A SHARED CRATE, NOT AN ENV PATH.** ~~BUILD INPUT = env path~~ **REFUTED**: (i) *an env path is the `RAK_PERSONA_PATH` trap one level up* — a value nobody reviews, a file nobody diffed, **which is HOW the empty cert got in**; (ii) **the natural implementation of an absent env var is SKIP THE CHECK = a FAIL-OPEN BY DEFAULT in the gate whose whole job is to fail closed**, failing silently and looking exactly like success; (iii) **"an env var is a value someone TYPES; a const is a value someone REVIEWS"** — git-auditable, diff-visible, unswappable per-build, and **absence is a COMPILE ERROR, not a skipped branch**; (iv) composer's production objection is answered by a **const TABLE keyed by tg_id, fail-closed on unknown** — and **"if a new TG needs a commit to add its anchor, THAT IS THE FEATURE: a trust anchor that can change without a commit is not an anchor."** **★ THE DECIDING CONSTRAINT (core-codex) — NEVER verify the cert against the persona's OWN key 5:** the baked app carries tg_pk+cert+hk+dek+master together in plaintext, so that proves only **SELF-CONSISTENCY** — an image replacement swaps BOTH and still passes. **The issuer key MUST come from OUTSIDE the bundle.** ⇒ **THIS KILLS composer's "issuer pk = its tg_pk" OFFER, WHICH I HAD ACCEPTED — one message after banking the rule that forbids it ("an untrusted input trusted to describe itself; never let an input supply the predicate that judges it"). Third time today I banked a rule and violated it on the next claim (direction-misread → wrong-board → this). The rule is not the hard part; APPLYING it to the thing in front of me is.** composer's *recomputability* argument survives but does not save it: **seed-derivability makes the const AUDITABLE to a REVIEWER; it does not make the bundle AUTHENTIC to the VERIFIER.** Right property, wrong risk. — in PRODUCTION the issuer is a REAL TG whose pk must NOT be baked into a shared crate, and a dev-trial shortcut becomes the production shape by default unless refused up front; dev-trial supplies its value THROUGH the general mechanism. **composer IS the issuer, and the key is PUBLIC + RECOMPUTABLE**: the repeater-TG cert issuer is the repeater TG ⇒ issuer pk = its `tg_pk` = the ed25519 verifying key of `tg_sk = SHA-256('<TG-SEED — REDACTED: this string IS the TG key; custody-only>')`. ⇒ composer's decisive line: **"a hardcoded const would be an UNVERIFIABLE literal; a documented-seed-derived const is a CHECKABLE one"** — a literal I cannot recompute is a literal I cannot audit (the rbid-resolve.py property, applied to the issuer). **★ NOT LANDING IT UNTIL I CAN FIRE IT BOTH WAYS** (a matching pk must ACCEPT, a wrong pk must REJECT): the repeater persona has NO cert yet (that IS the flash-blocker), and rak-persona.bin's cert is from a DIFFERENT TG ⇒ a negative-control candidate only. **(a) lands WITH composer's cert-bearing persona, both controls fired — building it blind and calling it done is the identical error I just conceded.** R2-PROVISION:324 (NOT R2-RUNTIME — core relayed the wrong number, specs caught it, I propagated it) = signature ALWAYS, expiry only where offline-checkable; **no-clock never excuses a bad signature**. **(b) runtime strict STRUCTURAL decode (no clock)** — lands with core's hardened `parse_persona` (cert147 by type); my fail-stop turns its `Err` into the hard stop. **(c) NOT VERIFIED: on-metal runtime** (no board) — the no-path-to-radio property is **compiler-checked, not observed**; claiming no more than that.
>   - **INTERLOCK:** composer re-produces the persona via the **cert-bearing** path (**188B = the known-bad no-cert generation path** — same one that made the 5 old weave personas, all empty-cert; **good = ~336B, key04 = `0x58 0x93` = bytes(147)**), **held pending a specs ROLE ruling — and composer is right to hold: a wrong-role cert PARSES and radiates; an empty one now fails loudly at build.** That asymmetry is why the role question outranks the empty cert. **#71 transplant lands ON TOP of this and gets re-touched exactly once — which is why safety-first was the right sequence.**


> **⚠⚠ I BUILT A FAIL-OPEN INTO THE FAIL-CLOSED GATE — core's principle caught it in code core had never seen (rak4630-fw `ce69273`, 2026-07-17).** core, ruling on the issuer key: *"the natural implementation of an absent env var is SKIP THE CHECK — a fail-open by default, in the gate whose whole job is to fail closed; the failure would be silent and would look exactly like success."* **That is a description of my own v1**: the expected-tg_id binding was an OPTIONAL `env::var` ⇒ **absent var = NO CHECK**. Worse than useless — **it READ like a TG binding existed**, so a reviewer would believe the image was bound when by default it was not. **That is THE SAME MISLABELLING I WAS REPAIRING** (main.rs called a fail-OPEN-on-identity path "FAIL-CLOSED"). **I reproduced the defect's shape INSIDE the fix for the defect.** REMOVED rather than left as false assurance; **both controls re-fired after** (empty-cert 188B ⇒ build FAILS; cert147 336B ⇒ validated). core's reasoning recorded in-file — **the reason outlives the answer**.
> **★ SPECS VINDICATED THE GATE AS CANON-MANDATED, NOT CONSERVATISM — R2-PROVISION:326:** *"Persona present but invalid (corrupt, fails self-consistency, seal/CRC-invalid) → the device MUST fail closed and require a physical reset."* **An empty certificate fails self-consistency** ⇒ my build failure + hard stop are **the MUST we were violating**, not caution we chose. Reframes #72 from "a good idea" to "the rule we were breaking".
> **🛑 #72 DOES *NOT* UNBLOCK THE FLASH (core's picture-correction, and I will not let it blur):** a conformant persona in a **BAKED** image is **still non-conformant** — **R2-PROVISION §5.1 step 3 requires the generic image + Channel-A**, and the RAK bootloader has **ZERO Channel-A implementation**. So **#72 closes the fail-open funnel and NOTHING ELSE**; **the baked path itself is Roy's call.** "Safety fix landed" must not read as "flash unblocked" — that is exactly the **loud-fix-hides-the-silent-hole** shape both core and composer caught me on tonight. Sequencing still stands: #72 is decision-independent.


> **↔ MECHANISM RESOLVED — CORE CONCEDED TO ME, I CONCEDED ITS INVARIANT (2026-07-17; rak4630-fw `0df2c85`).** Two reversals in one exchange, each on evidence:
>   - **core CONCEDED the mechanism: BUILD-INPUT (env path), not a const.** My production argument won: *a dev-trial shortcut becomes the production shape by default unless refused up front; the production issuer is a REAL TG whose pk must not sit in a shared crate.* core, on itself: *"MY OWN DISEASE pointed back at me — a const would have been CURRENTLY fine and STRUCTURALLY wrong. I have spent this night naming currently-true-vs-structurally-true and I proposed the currently-true option."*
>   - **★ core DERIVED composer's claim instead of taking it** — no crypto lib, so it implemented **RFC-8032 pubkey derivation in pure python**, got `tg_pk` from the documented seed, and **matched it against the staged persona's key 5**. That is the difference between accepting evidence and having it. **AND its reading of what it proves is sharper than mine was: composer's argument is about the VALUE's AUDITABILITY, not the MECHANISM** — a seed-derived value is checkable whether it arrives by const or env ⇒ **it never chose build-input; my production argument did.** I had called composer's *"the better half"* — **wrong: different axes, only one load-bearing for the question on the table.**
>   - **✅ CORE'S INVARIANT ADOPTED (non-negotiable, and it survives the mechanism change intact): THE ISSUER PK CHECK IS UNCONDITIONAL — absent anchor = BUILD FAILURE, same loud refusal as the empty cert, NEVER a skipped branch.** core's objection was never the mechanism; it was that *the natural implementation of an absent env var is a skipped branch = a fail-open inside the gate whose entire job is to fail closed.* **Plus core's attribution point I had missed: LOG THE ANCHOR'S SHA — "validated" without naming WHICH issuer it validated against is unattributable; a gate that cannot say what it checked against cannot be audited.**
>   - **⚠ AND CORE'S EXPECTATION-vs-ANCHOR DISTINCTION SHOWS I OVER-CORRECTED — I had DELETED `RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID` outright.** core: *an EXPECTATION may be optional; only the ANCHOR may not.* **v1's real defect was not optionality — it was optional AND SILENT** (unset ⇒ no check, while the code READ like a binding existed). **I fixed the lie by removing the capability: the cheap fix, not the right one. RESTORED with the ABSENCE MADE LOUD** — unset now emits *"NO RAK_EXPECT_TG_ID SET — image is NOT bound to any expected trust group; this build will accept a structurally-valid persona for ANY tg_id"*. **THREE controls fired: empty-cert ⇒ FAILS · cert147 ⇒ validated · no-expectation ⇒ ANNOUNCED.**
>   - **★★ THE GENERAL FORM (mine, taken from being wrong twice in one file): MY FIRST INSTINCT ON FINDING A MISLEADING CHECK WAS TO DELETE IT — but the check was never the problem, its SILENCE was. Deleting a misleading signal removes the lie AND the capability together; making it HONEST keeps both halves.** I had been doing exactly this all night in the other direction (naming gaps rather than papering them) and did not apply it to my own code. *An optional check that announces when it is off is honest; one that stays quiet is a lie of omission.*
>   - **NEGATIVE CONTROL CONFIRMED BY CORE'S OWN DERIVATION:** staged repeater `tg_pk = da1aa7f9…` vs rak-persona.bin `tg_pk = 3992f89b…` ⇒ **genuinely different TGs** ⇒ rak-persona.bin is a **negative**-control candidate and **I still have NO positive control**. **(a) lands with composer's cert-bearing persona, both directions fired** — core endorsed the hold rather than pushing me to ship blind.
>   - **ROLE ENFORCEMENT (core's, not mine to duplicate): specs ruled Member `0x02` canon (R2-RUNTIME §3.2.2:246) — the RULING closes the question but NOT the ENFORCEMENT; neither core's parse-hardening nor my gate reads the role byte.** core's framing worth keeping: **it surfaced by auditing the SHADOW of a fix rather than its target.**

> **▶ ESP L2CAP CoC FIX — co-review turn (2026-07-16): answered core's one-per-ACL POLICY Q from metal ground truth; NO edit/push/hardware.**
> Core's ARCH-refined design (fixed command slots not stack-local args; fixed NPL pools BLE_HOST_EV_COUNT=19/SEM_COUNT=10
> → one persistent dispatcher event + bounded app ring + app-level FreeRTOS sem/notify pool; logical channel-generation
> handle not chan*; host-owned registry). My caller-contract UNCHANGED (8 sync-Result send_to sites). Core asked ME (metal-usage
> owner) the one-per-ACL policy Q. **ANSWERED (read-only, verified against canonical `crates/r2-esp/src/l2cap.rs` @ r2-core-consolidation):**
> - **CONFIRM one-per-ACL is R2's real model.** Firmware = PURE CoC SERVER, single PSM 0x00D2 (create_server L171), ZERO
>   connect-out (no `ble_l2cap_connect` anywhere). `send_to` (L185-188) resolves by peer_addr → first non-closing channel; a
>   2nd CoC to the same peer_addr is dead weight send_to never selects. R2 has NO USE for >1 CoC/peer. I back enforce-one-per-ACL fail-closed.
> - **Sharpened the ENFORCEMENT POINT (concrete gap I found):** server-only means we do NOT control how many CoC a REMOTE peer
>   opens on one ACL. `handle_accept` (L398-437) has NO per-conn_handle dedup — accepts a 2nd CoC on the same conn_handle
>   unconditionally. Reject there (non-closing PeerChannel already exists for conn_handle → return error rc) → NimBLE refuses
>   the 2nd channel → core's conn_handle-keyed retain (L460/487) becomes correct-by-construction, aliasing killed at source, not peer-trust.
> - `handle_connected` L460 retain already assumes one-per-conn_handle but SILENTLY evicts a live sibling — same aliasing other side; accept-reject fixes both.
> - Completeness: COC_MAX_NUM=3 is the STACK-WIDE ceiling, NOT per-ACL; one-per-ACL → 3 concurrent peers max; more peers = separate config bump (orthogonal).
> - Sent to core (queued, core busy). STILL GATED: co-review the compile-verified rewrite when core routes it (read-only, allowed); metal validation on Roy hardware GO.
>

> DISCONNECTED removes EXACT chan+generation = root fix for sibling-aliasing). My earlier "I back one-per-ACL enforcement at handle_accept" is
> SUPERSEDED — generation-per-chan is a strict superset that drops the need for accept-time dedup. My sync-Result send_to caller-contract + 8 sites

> - **CORRECTION (2026-07-16, android refutation WON against source — my earlier "data-path-current@HEAD / relay works" was WRONG on the RAK relay hop):** the multi-hop demo BREAKS as-is at the RAK relay, and it is a CODE DROP not a metal issue. GROUND TRUTH: (a) DFR sensor emits COMPACT on LoRa UNCONDITIONALLY — apiary_bus_task (dfr1195 main.rs:6033-6065) encode_compact, has_route=1, route_stack[0]=(my_hive>>16) upper-16, event_hash=nz.r2.apiary.reading 0x64cedb11, target=my_tg_hash. benchsf7 changes SF ONLY, codec stays compact (NOT SF-gated). (b) RAK handle_rx_frame (r2-dataplane lib.rs:35) = decode_extended(frame) -> Err => return no; r2-dataplane has NO decode_compact + NO transcode (grep empty); RAK RX (rak main.rs:954) feeds raw LoRa bytes straight in. => RAK drops D4's compact frame at decode_extended Err, relay_on NEVER evaluated. The supervisor/core keyless-relay-rule question is MOOT (returns before any relay/keyless logic). This would fire even with a perfect RAK PA — so my earlier "hive-side code-complete, only metal PA-radiate unknown" was INCOMPLETE: the push_masked->transmit wiring IS complete, but handle_rx_frame never reaches it for a compact frame. XIAO SEAM: xiao_bridge_task (main.rs:5141) decode_compact + forwards COMPACT verbatim to phone (USB SYNC flags bit0=0x00=compact-stream, [len u16 LE][frame]); NO transcode to extended, NO origin zero-extend. So the intended demo path is COMPACT end-to-end EXCEPT the RAK relay. FIX is CORE-owned (r2-dataplane): add compact-tier RX/relay to handle_rx_frame (keep the wire compact through the relay — transcode-at-RAK would break the compact-only XIAO+phone). NOTE core doc-vs-code gap: compact.rs header claims 'called by r2-dataplane (compact-tier RX/relay)' but handle_rx_frame is extended-only (compact RX/relay speced, never wired). > - **WIRE CONTRACT PUBLISHED (nz.r2.apiary.reading COMPACT origin, 29B, byte-exact from apiary_bus_task + r2-wire compact.rs/hmac.rs):** [0]=0x06 (ver0|Event|R|H) [1]=0x53 (ttl5|k3) [2..4]=msg_id u16 BE (apiary seq, from 1) [4..8]=event_hash BE=0x64cedb11 (BUTTON=nz.r2.apiary.button distinct) [8..12]=target BE=my_tg_hash (provisioned <PROV-TG-HASH>; code literal <DEMO-TG-HASH> STALE) [12]=route_len 1 [13..15]=route_stack[0] u16 BE=(my_hive>>16) upper-16 (provisioned D4 <D4-HIVE-ID>-><D4-ORIGIN>; code literal <FALLBACK-ORIGIN> STALE=unprovisioned mac_low3) [15..21]=payload 6B RAW seq(u32 BE)+value(i16 BE, sinf*1000 +/-1000) NOT CBOR (payload seq independent of header msg_id) [21..29]=HMAC-8 = HMAC-SHA256(persona hk) over authenticated_bytes_compact = msg_type|msg_id(2BE)|origin(2BE=route[0])|event_hash(4BE)|target(4BE)|payload(6)=19B, flags EXCLUDED. Origin = compact 16-bit upper-half of FNV-32; full 32-bit NOT on compact wire (resolve <D4-ORIGIN>->D4). >   - **CRACK 1 — core's premise "DATA_TX_LORA is the ONLY way onto the LoRa carrier" is FALSE.** The real carrier edge is `lora.send`, and it has **TWO** sites: main.rs:5043 (the DATA_TX_LORA drain core enumerated) **and main.rs:5055 — `build_lora_beacon` → `lora.send`, bypassing DATA_TX_LORA entirely**, inside `lora_route_task` (cfg `loraroute`) ⇒ **it IS in the demo image.** Core enumerated a QUEUE that FEEDS the edge. **Core's conclusion survives via an argument core never made:** the missed sender emits a §8.1 discovery beacon (magic 0xB2, ver 0x01, ≤17B) built by DIRECT byte-assembly at main.rs:4684 — it never touches `encode_extended`, so it cannot carry an extended frame.
>   - **CRACK 2 — core's "xiao_bridge_task:5419 is compact BY CONSTRUCTION, phone-originated" is FALSE.** It is an **UNVALIDATED OPAQUE PASSTHROUGH**: `copy_from_slice(&inbuf[3..3+bl])` → `try_send`, **no decode, no format check**. The 2 `decode_compact` calls in that task are the OPPOSITE direction (LoRa→USB egress; its own comment: *"the phone does the authoritative verify_compact"*). A host tagging an **extended** frame with `LORA_LOCAL_ID` gets it radiated verbatim. Compact by **HOST CONVENTION**, not construction.
>   - **SCOPE, HONESTLY — crack 2 does NOT touch the demo, twice over:** (i) 5419 is `cfg(feature="xiaobridge")`; the demo compose is `fakesensor,benchsf7,dev,baked_persona` and `fakesensor = [otaengine, loraroute, loratcxo]` ⇒ xiaobridge NOT pulled ⇒ **task compiled OUT**; (ii) independently, 5419 is the **phone→LoRa** direction while the demo data path is sensor→LoRa→bridge→phone — **the opposite way**. Real property of the *xiaobridge* image; **tracked, NOT patched before Roy's slot.**
>   - **★ THE PROOF THAT ACTUALLY HOLDS (demo image, by construction):** `lora.send` = exactly 2 sites, both in `lora_route_task`. **5043** ← DATA_TX_LORA ← senders: `mesh_broadcast:4199` (sole caller **6143**, traced to `encode_compact`) + `xiao_bridge_task:5419` (compiled out under fakesensor). **5055** ← `build_lora_beacon` (direct assembly, never `encode_extended`). ⇒ **every byte reaching the LoRa carrier in the demo image is either `encode_compact` or a §8.1 beacon. No extended, by construction — closed over the REAL edge.** ⇒ **VERDICT UNCHANGED: GO TO METAL.**
>   - **★★ THE RULE (banked in [[never-conclude-from-a-null]]): CLOSE OVER THE ACTUAL BOUNDARY, NOT A PROXY FOR IT.** *"Enumerate everything that reaches X"* is a proof only when X is the real edge. Ask **"what is the LAST thing before the air/disk/socket?"** and enumerate THAT — a queue/channel/wrapper is an *implementation* of the edge and there can be a second one. **Dangerous because it is proof-SHAPED, so it disarms review**; its null ("no other senders") reads as a theorem when the method could never see the bypass. **Positive control: grep the PRIMITIVE and check your enumeration already contains every hit.** You pick the proxy because it's where the DESIGN says data flows — **but the bypass never read the design.**
>   - **HONEST SYMMETRY:** core was right that my count couldn't prove there was no 7th site — there were in fact **EIGHT** `encode_extended` sites, not 6 (**1783** + **5949**), and **both go to `socket.send_to` (UDP/WiFi), where extended is canon-legal**. So my count was wrong **AND harmless**, exactly as core's method predicts. **Core's METHOD beat mine; my EXECUTION beat core's. Keep both halves.**

>   - **CORE'S OWN NAMING OF ITS ERROR (better than my polite version):** *"I took a CODE COMMENT as a construction proof."* :5419's comment says "TX the compact body on-air"; core read that **prose** and wrote "compact by construction". *"That is strictly worse than your call-site count: you at least enumerated real code and got a wrong-but-harmless answer; I enumerated prose."*
>   - **★★ THE RULE, IN ITS FINAL FORM (core's sharpening of my diagnosis — keep this one):** *"You picked the queue because the queue is where the DESIGN says frames go — but the beacon never read the design."* ⇒ **a proxy-closure only covers the paths that OBEY the architecture, so it is exactly blind to the bypass — and a bypass is the only thing a closure proof exists to catch. THE PROXY IS CHOSEN BY READING THE DESIGN; THE VIOLATION IS DEFINED BY NOT READING IT.** So **"close over the boundary"** and **"the design cannot be the search index"** are the SAME rule. **Generalises past LoRa: any "all writes go through the repository / logger / queue / API" argument is a proxy-closure until someone enumerates the syscall.** Sits beside the day's other two — *state the SCOPE with the result* (a null needs a positive control) and *close over the EDGE* (a closure needs the real boundary): **both are one disease — a confident green over the wrong universe.**
>   - **★ MY REFUTATION OF CORE'S MITIGATION — the finding is SHARPER than core's own sharpening.** Core softened it: *"the host is paired (r2-usb-pair), so this is not a stranger-on-the-wire — but trusted host is an authorisation argument, not a conformance one."* Right about the KIND of argument; **WRONG on the fact. PAIRING DOES NOT GATE THE LoRa TX PRIMITIVE** (VERIFIED main.rs:5410-5419): the demux has **three SIBLING branches** — `looks_control(0xFF)` → `pairing.handle` → `persist_link_key`; `!synced && looks_sync` → consume SYNC; **`plen>1 && inbuf[2]==LORA_LOCAL_ID` → `copy_from_slice` → `DATA_TX_LORA.try_send`**. The third checks **NO** pairing state, **NO** link_key, and does **NOT** require `synced` — **it SETS `synced=true`**. `persisted_link_key` is loaded (:5220) and handed to `Peripheral::new` (:5228), then **NEVER consulted on the TX path** (grep positive-controlled: 11 `pairing` hits ⇒ the null is real; link_key touches = :299/:304 load, :2726/:2742 flash record, :5399/:5406-7 inside the pairing branch — **none gate the radiate**). ⇒ **an UNPAIRED host, with NO SYNC, that never ran the SM, can radiate.** The pairing SM runs **ALONGSIDE** the primitive, not **IN FRONT OF** it ⇒ **it provides ZERO protection here.** The only real bound is **PHYSICAL USB ACCESS** — the same bound with or without pairing. **So: not "a paired host can radiate any bytes" — "ANY host that can reach the port can radiate any bytes."** Both of core's axes survive; the authorisation axis no longer softens it.
>   - **★★ NEW COROLLARY (banked in [[never-conclude-from-a-null]]): WE AUDIT *ESCALATIONS* HARDER THAN *DE-ESCALATIONS*, SO DE-ESCALATIONS ARE WHERE UNVERIFIED CLAIMS SURVIVE.** Core's concession was rigorous on the 3 refuted claims and then added a 4th, unverified, that made the finding smaller. **Not motivated — the same reflex as "compact by construction": a plausible fact read off the DESIGN instead of the code.** The SM *is* there, *is* wired, *looks* like it guards the port. **A softening claim needs the SAME positive control as a hardening one, and gets LESS scrutiny precisely because it lowers the stakes.** ⇒ **Applies to MY OWN de-escalations** ("only cosmetic", "compiled out", "not on the demo path") — each is a claim; scope-verify it as hard as an alarm.
>   - **THE PROPERTY, STATED PLAINLY (core asked for it harder than "a xiaobridge quirk", and it's right): the xiaobridge image will RADIATE VERBATIM ANY BYTES the USB host tags with `LORA_LOCAL_ID`.** Not "may carry extended" — **ANY bytes.** An **arbitrary-LoRa-transmit primitive exposed to the host**, whose conformance consequence is that the image can violate **R2-LORA §5.1** at the host's discretion **with no code in the DFR disagreeing.** **Tracked: hive task #69. NOT patched before Roy's slot** (flashed image in the proven anchor path ⇒ unpriced risk, zero demo benefit).
>   - **⚠ SPEC Q ROUTED TO SPECS — I HAVE THE PATCH READY AND DELIBERATELY WILL NOT PICK THE RULING THAT SUITS IT:** is an MCU bridge **REQUIRED** to enforce bearer tier on host-originated frames (⇒ DFR non-conformant TODAY, validate MANDATORY), **or** is the **R2-USB seam a TRUST BOUNDARY** where §5.1 conformance is the **HOST's** obligation (⇒ fix belongs in R2-USB as a host MUST; my validate is defence-in-depth)? **Beyond my patch:** if the seam is trusted, **EVERY** bridge implementing §3.5 is an arbitrary-transmit primitive for its host **BY DESIGN** and the spec should say so; if not, §3.5 needs an explicit *"the bridge MUST reject frames violating the target bearer tier"* and every existing bridge is non-conformant until it validates. **§5.1 names the tier rule but names no ENFORCEMENT POINT at a host seam — so nobody enforced it.** (Mirror of the day's other canon item: *a physical limit is not a conformance check*.) Candidate fix post-ruling: byte0/`decode_compact` validate before `try_send`, reject non-compact, real error to the phone instead of silent garbage on the air.

>   - **SPECS' READ ON THE FIX (advisory): (1) — the validate is a CONFORMANCE fix, not defence-in-depth — but NOT because the host is untrusted. Because "§5.1 binds the BEARER, and you ARE the bearer."** The `faculty` framing seals it: **a faculty is the only part of the organism touching the air, so it is the only place the bearer invariant CAN be enforced — not because it distrusts the rest of itself.** ⇒ **MY PATCH MUST BE A TIER CHECK, NEVER A PAIRING/AUTH GATE**: a pairing gate fixes nothing (a paired host can still send extended) **AND** would contradict `R2-USB:32/:260/:329`. Also: specs named my question a **FALSE DICHOTOMY** — trust and conformance are **independent axes**; option (2)'s premise ("the seam is a trust boundary") is **foreclosed**, but that does *not* make §5.1 the host's obligation. *"My TCP stack trusts my own application completely and still won't emit a malformed IP packet."*
>   - **★★ MY CHALLENGE 1 — "THE DFR IS NON-CONFORMANT TODAY" OVERSTATES IT, and the distinction IS the spec gap.** §5.1's MUST NOT binds **BEHAVIOUR**. The DFR only violates it if it **EMITS** extended — and today the host sends compact, so **it does not**. Accurate: **CONFORMANT IN BEHAVIOUR but UNENFORCING**, its conformance **CONTINGENT ON THE HOST** rather than guaranteed. ⇒ **THE REAL QUESTION: does a MUST NOT bind only BEHAVIOUR, or also require an ENFORCEMENT POINT at the last node that can still stop it?** Canon does not say — **that ambiguity IS the gap**. It prices the fix: *"non-conformant today"* = shipping a violation (urgent); *"unenforced"* = a defence + a text fix (not urgent). **Specs is right about the FIX and wrong about the LABEL.**
>   - **★★ MY CHALLENGE 2 — §5.1 IS INTERNALLY INCONSISTENT (sharper than either of us framed).** Sentence 1: *"The extended format… **MUST NOT** be used on the LoRa bearer"* — **ABSOLUTE**. Closing sentence: *"If 32-byte-HMAC extended-e2e is ever required on LoRa it needs a **Roy-gated NAMED PHY profile** whose MTU ≥ the signed-extended size (e.g. `SF9/BW125` = 115 B, or a BW250 profile)"* — **CONDITIONAL**. **It cannot be both.** It **reads as absolute and means profile-conditional**; the live thread must pick one.
>   - **★★★ AND THE ACCIDENT HAS ALREADY STOPPED HIDING IT — NOT IN A FUTURE PROFILE, ON ROY'S BENCH TONIGHT.** Specs located the escape at SF9/115 B as *prospective*. **It is not prospective.** §5.1's ENTIRE stated rationale is the 54 B signed-extended floor vs the **51 B SF12/BW125** MTU. But **`R2-LORA:401`: `lora_mtu` BW125 = SF7-8 → **222 B**, SF9 → 115 B, SF10-12 → 51 B**, and **the demo runs `benchsf7`** — a profile **canon itself blesses** (`:386` *"a labelled WHOLE-MESH SF7/BW125 profile"*). ⇒ **On the profile Roy powers up tonight, extended fits with 168 B to spare, §5.1's justification is ALREADY DEAD, and the MUST NOT survives ON TEXT ALONE.** **`ef6f95a` is the ONLY thing enforcing §5.1 on that board, and it is 6 hours old. The rule has been unenforced on SF7 for as long as SF7 has existed.** ⇒ core's *gate-it* call was right for a **stronger reason than either of us gave**: it is not tidying a wart. Banked as memory [[s5-1-extended-on-lora-rests-on-text-alone]].

>   - **★★ SPECS CHALLENGED MY STRONGEST CLAIM ("the justification is ALREADY DEAD") — RIGHT INSTINCT, REFUTED BY THEIR OWN TABLE.** Their steelman: maybe §5.1 rests on **ToA**, not MTU (`:401` *"1/s at 10% needs ToA ≤ 100 ms → only SF7 qualifies (all sizes ≤ 51 B)"*), so 54 B busts the envelope ⇒ my claim is only *half* dead. **REFUTED, structurally: ToA is a function of SIZE, not FORMAT** — a 54 B compact and a 54 B extended frame have **identical** airtime ⇒ ToA **cannot ground a format-keyed MUST NOT**. The floor-steelman (extended ≥54 B always) dies on canon's **own rows**: `:377` *"These rows are COMPACT-format sizes"*, **SF7 = 51 B→103 ms, 115 B→195 ms, 222 B→348 ms**; a 54 B extended frame at SF7 ≈ **110 ms**. ⇒ **canon TABULATES compact frames at SF7 costing 195 ms and 348 ms as legitimate operating points — 2× and 3× the airtime of the extended frame it FORBIDS.** A ToA rationale would ban 54 B extended while blessing 222 B compact at 3× the cost. **No coherent rule does that.** ⇒ **§5.1 states EXACTLY ONE ground (MTU); the paragraph never mentions airtime. MY CLAIM STANDS UNQUALIFIED: on SF7 the justification is not half dead — it is dead.** *What survives of their instinct:* extended costs **+24 B for the same content** (32 B vs 8 B HMAC) — the apiary 29 B/67 ms reading → ~53 B/~105 ms, ~1.6× airtime, marginally busting 1/s@10%. **A real efficiency reason to prefer compact; NOT the ground of a MUST NOT.** *Free nit:* `:401`'s takeaway overstates its own table — **SF7/51 B = 103 ms = 0.97/s**, already missing both 1/s and 100 ms. ⇒ asked specs to **DROP/RECAST their proposed 3rd defect**; the real one is *"canon states a rationale that DOES NOT BIND on the bench profile canon itself blesses (`:386` labelled WHOLE-MESH SF7/BW125)"*.
>   - **★★ NEW GROUND TRUTH I DID NOT HAVE — verified both: `R2-USB:98` *"USB uses COMPACT R2-WIRE format… This matches BLE and LoRa"*; `R2-USB:100` *"An implementation MAY negotiate EXTENDED format via the SYNC handshake (§3.3) if both ends support it."*** ⇒ **MY BRIDGE IGNORES THAT NEGOTIATION ENTIRELY** — the SYNC branch comment is literally *"version/flags negotiation ignored for the MVP"*. So it **never assents to extended** ⇒ satisfies specs' first horn (*"either never negotiates extended"*) — **BY ACCIDENT, NOT BY CONSTRUCTION.** **Ignoring a negotiation ≠ refusing one:** a host that sends extended **without** negotiating still gets it radiated. ⇒ **specs' two horns are NOT EXHAUSTIVE for a real implementation — there is a THIRD state, NEGOTIATION-IGNORING: conformant on the handshake, unenforcing on the air.** Flagged for §3.3.

>   - **★ MY REFINEMENT TO THE RULING (offered; specs may decline):** their formulation **over-reaches** — taken literally, *"WOULD radiate if fed"* makes conformance mean **PROVABLY-CANNOT-VIOLATE**, which no real system meets (**my io_task "would" emit extended too, if someone flipped a cfg**) ⇒ the word does no work in the *other* direction. **THE LINE I THINK THEY WANT: CONFORMANCE IS A PROPERTY OVER THE *DESIGNED INPUT DOMAIN*** — conformant iff the invariant holds for **all inputs the device is DESIGNED TO ACCEPT**. Bridge domain = *"any framed bytes the host sends"* (**that IS its function**, per `R2-USB:32` — the host is not a foreign party but the same organism) ⇒ extended is **inside** it ⇒ **non-conformant, no malice or mistake required**. io_task's domain **excludes** *"an extended frame to radiate"* — reaching it requires **EDITING THE BUILD, not supplying an input** ⇒ **conformant**. Keeps the teeth, drops the over-reach, **and is TESTABLE**. ⇒ **It is the egress-closure rule pointed at the ingress: for ENFORCEMENT close over the EGRESS (cannot be outflanked); for CONFORMANCE close over the INPUT DOMAIN.**

> - **✅✅ CORE'S §5.1 ESCAPE-HATCH UNSOUNDNESS — VERIFIED, AND §5.1'S *OWN CITED AUTHORITY* CONVICTS IT.** Core's argument: MTU was never the real obstacle — compact/extended aren't self-describing, so a receiver **MIS-PARSES** the wrong tier rather than rejecting it; **raising the MTU creates NO discriminator**, so the hatch licenses exactly the failure the rule exists to prevent. **CONFIRMED FROM SOURCE, and the spec convicts itself:** §5.1:326 cites *"R2-WIRE §4.3.5 **format-detection**"* as though a discriminator existed. **`R2-WIRE.md:453`, verbatim: *"A receiving hive distinguishes compact from extended format **BY TRANSPORT CONTEXT**: messages received on BLE or LoRa adapters are parsed as compact."*** ⇒ **IT DETECTS NOTHING — IT ASSUMES.** The section named *Format Detection* hard-codes format per bearer, so **a LoRa receiver parses everything as compact BY SPEC** ⇒ an extended frame on LoRa isn't rejected, it's **mis-parsed**. Core was right and didn't need me to be.
>   - **★★ MY STRENGTHENING — THE HATCH IS NOT A PHY DECISION, IT IS A BREAKING WIRE CHANGE.** If Roy gated the SF9/115 B profile, **§4.3.5:453 would STILL mandate "messages received on LoRa adapters are parsed as compact"** ⇒ **every conformant receiver on that profile mis-parses the very extended frames the profile exists to carry.** So the hatch needs a **THREE-way change**: an in-band **discriminator (a wire change)** + amend **§4.3.5** + amend **§5.1**. **It READS like "Roy approves a PHY profile" and MEANS "break the wire format."** ⇒ **THE HATCH UNDERSTATES ITS OWN COST BY AN ORDER OF MAGNITUDE** — a stronger reason to kill it than inconsistency: it's **mispriced in a way that invites someone to grant it cheaply.**
>   - **★ NEW — THE DEAD MTU RATIONALE IS *DUPLICATED*, so fixing §5.1 alone leaves the corpse in R2-WIRE.** `§4.3.5:463`: *"On LoRa this is moot: the LoRa bearer is compact-only (R2-LORA §5.1), and a signed extended frame cannot even fit the SF12/BW125 MTU (54-byte floor > 51, R2-LORA §5.2)."* **Same MTU argument, same SF12 scoping, same death on SF7.**
>   - **★ NEW — §4.3.5 HAS §5.1'S EXACT SHAPE: an absolute rule + an unacknowledged escape whose mechanism DOESN'T EXIST.** `:453` states detection-by-transport-context **absolutely**; `:463` then says a signed frame is *"forwarded VERBATIM… the receiver parses it by the **carried format context**, not by transport default"* — an exception `:453` never admits — **and canon concedes the mechanism is undefined on that same line: *"a format-context surface to COORDINATE WITH CORE."*** ⇒ **the exception invokes something that does not exist, and it is CORE's crate that would have to invent it. Two specs, one pattern.** Core has routed the re-grounding to specs: **base the MUST NOT on SINGLE-TIER-PER-BEARER** (no in-band discriminator ⇒ mixed tiers structurally undecodable ⇒ **binds on EVERY profile**), demote MTU to a **coincidental SF12-only enforcer**, and **KILL the hatch** (extended-on-LoRa would need a **discriminator = a wire change, not airtime**).

>   - **✅ I CONFIRMED THE MECHANISM AGAINST THE RAK ARTIFACT (not reasoned):** the RAK feeds EVERY raw RxDone buffer into `handle_rx_frame` with **NO beacon pre-demux** (rak4630 main.rs:954); `handle_rx_frame` step (1) is `decode_extended` and **decode-fail `return no` BEFORE any neighbour formation** (r2-dataplane lib.rs:516-519); **a beacon fails that decode ⇒ forms NO link.** ⇒ **only decodable DATA frames populate the RAK's neighbour table.** In the minimal READ demo the XIAO emits only §8.1 BEACONS on LoRa and the phone transmits nothing ⇒ **the RAK hears exactly ONE data source, D4 the sender** ⇒ table = {sender} ⇒ F2 empties the plan ⇒ dead relay leg. **The phone sees only the direct D4→XIAO path (route_len=1) at 30cm — indistinguishable from success.**
>   - **★ THE FLIP IS *TOPOLOGY*, NOT COMPOSE:** if ANY hive other than D4 transmits a **decodable LoRa DATA** frame the RAK hears (2nd LoRa node #66, or D2 on-air on LoRa), F2's exclusion leaves a viable neighbour ⇒ relay alive. So the member compose is dead **IFF the RAK hears only D4** — non-deterministic if a 2nd transmitter is intermittent (**two runs of the same demo can differ** — worse than deterministic failure). **PIN THE TOPOLOGY, not just the compose.**

> - **✅ core RETRACTED THE ROTATION CLAIM AND VERIFIED IT AT THE SHA ITSELF — AND ITS METHOD DEFECT TURNS OUT TO BE THE SAME CLASS AS MY #106 (2026-07-20).** core added the datum I did not have: **both callers** (`:4996 compute_rbid(&sk, current_beacon_epoch())` and `:5414 resolve_rbid_windowed(.., current_beacon_epoch(), 1)`) **receive a constant zero.** *I checked the supplier; core checked the consumers; together it closes.*
>   - **★★★ A FOURTH INSTRUMENT, AND IT HAD TWO INSTANCES TONIGHT THAT WE FILED AS UNRELATED FINDINGS:** **#107 (core's)** — `compute_rbid(&key, epoch)` **takes an epoch** ⇒ *looks* rotating; `current_beacon_epoch()` **returns 0** ⇒ it is not. **#106 (mine)** — `set_neighbour_count(n)` → `duty_cycle_refill(n)` **takes a neighbour count** ⇒ *looks* per-bearer; `NBRS` is a **global** counter ⇒ it is not. ⇒ **SAME SHAPE FROM BOTH DIRECTIONS: AN API WHOSE PARAMETER IMPLIES A PROPERTY ITS SUPPLIER DOES NOT DELIVER.** I found mine by tracing the supplier and **never generalised it**; core hit its by inferring from the signature.
>   - **THE FAMILY IS NOW FOUR, AND NONE SUBSUMES THE OTHERS — banked as [[four-reachability-instruments]]:** **caller-grep** *does this ever run* · **emitter-trace** *does anything ELSE run instead* · **argument-read** *the caller runs and passes a value making the branch unreachable* · **★ supplier-trace** *the parameter exists — trace it to its PRODUCER.* **Presence of a parameter is not evidence of its value.**
>   - **⚠ AND THE DOC LIES BY OMISSION IN BOTH CASES WITHOUT BEING FALSE:** `:4974`'s *"INTERIM … not yet wired"* and `set_neighbour_count`'s *"the caller feeds it in"* are **both honest, and neither warns the value is degenerate.** **Form 4 cannot be discharged by reading the doc.**
>   - **META, core AGAINST ITSELF AND WORTH KEEPING:** it ran a comment/code-contradiction counter all night and **would have absorbed an honest INTERIM comment into it.** ***"A tally that grows by mis-classification stops measuring anything."*** **A counter cited as evidence needs a classification rule stated in advance** — this one had none.
>   - **★ LEDGER, SYMMETRIC:** core was twice wrong **in the direction that sounds most rigorous** (over-self-flagging, then escalating on an unverified premise); **I was twice wrong in the direction that sounds most humble** (over-conceding a defect I did not have, both times on a premise someone else supplied). **Both look like care. Both cost the record accuracy. AND EACH OF US CAUGHT THE OTHER'S, NOT OUR OWN** — the argument for the opposite-lane refuter, made twice tonight without either of us intending to make it.
> - **🔴🔴 PRIVACY — TWO GAPS, NOT ONE. core ESCALATED THEM TO ROY AS ONE MIS-ATTRIBUTED FINDING AND I CORRECTED IT BEFORE IT LANDED (task #107, 2026-07-20).**
>   - **core's CLAIM: *"the beacon rotates; the static compact route origin DEFEATS that rotation."* THE SECOND HALF IS RIGHT. THE FIRST IS FALSE.** Measured at `15014508`, `:4978-4981` verbatim: **`fn current_beacon_epoch() -> u64 { let _ = LORA_BEACON_T_ROTATE_S; 0 }`**, and `LORA_BEACON_T_ROTATE_S` has **exactly three references — the const, the doc, and a `let _ =` to silence dead-code.** ⇒ **`compute_rbid(&my_key, epoch)` runs at epoch=0 forever. THE rbid IS CONSTANT PER BOARD, ON BOTH BEARERS. THERE IS NO ROTATION TO DEFEAT.** *(`:4974`'s doc is HONEST — *"INTERIM … not yet wired"* — so this is **NOT** a comment/code contradiction; do not add it to that tally.)*
>   - **THE CORRECTED COMPARISON, AND IT IS STRONGER THAN core's:** **beacon rbid = KEYED pseudonym, STATIC** ⇒ correlatable across time but **identity-OPAQUE** without `hk`; **compact route origin = UNKEYED, STATIC, a MAC byte in the clear** ⇒ correlatable **AND leaks hardware identity, surviving reflash.** **Both static; they differ in whether they leak hardware identity. The route origin is STRICTLY WORSE than the rbid — unkeyed where the rbid is keyed.**
>   - **⇒ TWO GAPS:** **(1) rbid rotation is UNIMPLEMENTED on both paths**, blocked on a **shared coarse-time base** — *the real dependency, and nobody's fault*; **(2) the compact route origin is UNKEYED and hardware-derived** — **core's, and real.**
>   - **★ WHY THE FRAMING MATTERED RIGHT THEN:** *"the data path defeats the beacon's rotation"* **sends specs looking for a data-path fix to protect a property that does not exist yet — wrong remedy, wrong layer.** The honest ask is: **rotation needs the coarse-time base FIRST; separately the route origin should be a keyed pseudonym, not a MAC truncation.**
>   - **WHAT SURVIVES OF core's UNCHANGED:** the origin **is** static, **is** in the clear (HMAC covers **integrity, not confidentiality**), **is** on every data frame, **is** a MAC byte on unprovisioned boards, and **is a cross-device correlator riding the ROUTING layer** — a direct hit on connectivity-is-location. **Pre-existing canon, NOT introduced by `15014508`, NOT a new RF exposure, NOT a flash blocker.** core's log added a **PUBLICATION** leak, not a radio one. **And core's relay constraint is the real design question: a relay must preserve `route_stack[0]` verbatim without re-signing, so a rotating origin may be impossible without a wire change — better asked once (1) is separated out.**
>   - **METHOD, MINE:** I only looked because a **dated memory note from an android exchange** said `current_beacon_epoch()` returns 0 and `T_ROTATE` is dead. **I did not trust the note — I grepped it at the sha.** *A dated memory is a dated claim: it was right, and it was still only a lead until measured.*
> - **✅ core's COMPLIANCE VERIFIED AT SOURCE (`15014508`), ALL THREE RULINGS — NOT TAKEN ON REPORT.** **Ruling 2:** `:1379 seen: heapless::Vec<(u32,u32,u8),16>` and **exactly ONE `let mut seen` in the file** ⇒ a **tag on a shared table, NO per-bearer tables**. *core's prose overreached; its diff did not.* **Ruling 3:** `:2033 let verified = r2_wire::verify_compact(&cm, &group_hmac);` — **a real HMAC, not `couple_ok`** — reached **before** the ruling arrived, and the log reports **decode and verify SEPARATELY**. *The single most valuable line in the commit.*
> - **★★ RULING 1 — core OVER-SELF-FLAGGED, AND THE REAL IN-CODE GAP IS A DIFFERENT ONE.** The loose clause at `:1370` (*"Without the tag … becomes TWO entries (nbrs DOUBLE-COUNTS)"*) is true **with** the tag too, so it implies a fix it does not deliver — **core's self-catch is right on that clause.** **BUT `:1375-1378` says verbatim *"STILL UNFIXED, DELIBERATELY: `NBRS` remains a GLOBAL count feeding a PER-BEARER airtime budget … Recorded as unfixed, not as addressed"*, and `:1775` says *"the fix itself is NOT in this commit."*** ⇒ **two adjacent comments record the gap correctly; a reader reaching `:1375` cannot inherit "double-count solved".** core reported a ninth comment/code contradiction; **measured, it is one loose clause inside an otherwise honest block — over-self-flagging, the mirror of the over-concession I have been catching all night, now aimed inward.**

>   - **⇒ I AGREE: DO NOT RE-PUSH.** Code correct, gap substantially recorded in-code, **and the missing number belongs in the reference-implementation record — exactly where Roy's directive puts it.** A new sha would de-sync a verified artifact to sharpen one clause. **core's reasoning holds and is stronger than core made it.**
> - **⚠★★ LEAK HAZARD IN THE EVIDENCE LINE — RAISED BEFORE THIS ROW GOES INTO A PUBLIC GH ISSUE.** The new log prints **`origin={:?}` ⇒ `Some(0x00XX)`**, and that value is `(my_hive >> 16)` where an unprovisioned `my_hive = mac_low3 = MAC & 0x00FF_FFFF` ⇒ **`0x00XX` IS A BYTE OF THE DEVICE MAC.** ⇒ **`LORA-CPT … origin=Some(0x0052)` IS A PARTIAL MAC CORRELATOR.** Fine on a bench console; **MUST NOT be pasted verbatim into issue 19, a spec, or a commit message.** **Quote it with the origin redacted (`origin=Some(0x00__)`) or cite `decode=`/`verify=` only — the evidentiary value is entirely in those two booleans; the origin adds nothing to the proof and everything to the exposure.** Same class as the board-id rule we have run all night, and **the first time an evidence artifact carries one INTO a public record.**
>
> - **✅ #109 BOUND NOW TRACED ON BOTH SIDES — MY AIRTIME ARGUMENT IS DEAD, core's *"invisible at N=2"* IS DEAD, AND THE REAL HARM IS A FORMATION-TIME RANKING PROBLEM.**
>   - **LIMB 2 — core RIGHT, MY CHALLENGE REFUTED, VERIFIED MYSELF:** `main.rs:2386-2390` the `ForwardAction::Flood(hops)` arm is **a `println!` and nothing else** — it prints `fanout={}` from `hops.len()`. **The emission is not there**; the re-broadcast sits in the dedup-guarded relay block below and calls `mesh_broadcast_extended` **ONCE**, not per hop. ⇒ **fanout is an ACCOUNTING figure in a log line. One flood = one transmission regardless of candidate count. A phantom adds a ROW to the set, not a FRAME to the air. THE AIRTIME BUDGET IS UNTOUCHED.** *(My "even one extra emission per cycle" would have been decisive if true. It is not.)*
>   - **★ AND THAT IS THE NIGHT'S RECURRING DEFECT, THIRD INSTANCE, MINE:** *"a phantom neighbour IS a flood target, so it MUST cost a transmission."* **Reasoning from what the thing IS to how it BEHAVES — the same substitution as the two I had named an hour earlier, committed while naming them.**
>   - **LIMB 1 — core's SELF-CORRECTION CONFIRMED, AND IT IS 5× NOT MARGINAL:** `constants.rs:66 NEIGHBOUR_INIT_CONF = 0.5` vs `:145 FORWARDING_CONFIDENCE_FLOOR = 0.1` ⇒ **a fresh unauthenticated entry is forwarding-viable on the FIRST frame — no decay window, no warm-up.** *"Invisible at N=2"* correctly retired by core.
>   - **★★ MY SHARPENING — THE RANKING HARM IS A *FORMATION* PROBLEM, NOT A STEADY-STATE ONE:** `NEIGHBOUR_INIT_CONF` is the init for **every** neighbour, so **a freshly-formed REAL peer also sits at 0.5.** ⇒ **at formation the phantom is RANK-INDISTINGUISHABLE from a genuine new link**, and the K-cut becomes a **tie-break against a real peer** rather than a contest it loses. ⇒ **THE HARM PEAKS DURING COLD MESH BRING-UP — exactly Roy's 9- and 12-board scenario — and fades as real links climb above 0.5.** More specific and more testable than *"harmful at N≥3"*. **core's to confirm against the ranking comparator.**
>   - **CORRECTED BOUND, both sides traced, neither lane inflating: PRESENT at N=2 · COSTS NO AIRTIME at any N · HARMFUL at N≥3 VIA RANKING, PEAKING AT FORMATION.**
>   - **SEQUENCING SETTLED (core revised): FIX THE EXTENDED PATH ALONE, NOW, AS ITS OWN COMMIT.** `ExtendedRouteStack::last_hop` is on the branch at `types.rs:271` — **no merge required.** The compact path is already correct, **carries no harm while it waits**, and converges when the merge lands.

> ## 🔴 SHIPPING PRE-AUTH — `u32::MAX` PROMOTED INTO A NEIGHBOUR KEY (task #109, 2026-07-20)
> **core reported this as item 1 of a seven-item queue inside a message about a `{:?}` format specifier. I lifted it out and verified it independently at `15014508`.**
> - **`main.rs:2087` verbatim: `let sender_hive = m.route.and_then(|r| r.origin()).unwrap_or(u32::MAX);`** ⇒ a **route-less extended frame** gives `origin() == None` ⇒ **`sender_hive = 0xFFFFFFFF`**, which is then used as a **neighbour key** in `is_reachability_blocked`, `seen.push`, and `Observation { hive_id, .. }` into the engine.
> - **PRE-AUTH, CONFIRMED:** the unverified arm — `} else if reach_ok { engine.ingest_observation(obs) }` — **does not test `couple_ok` at all.** And on the verified arm, `couple_ok` on a non-`multitg` build is **the plaintext tag compare**, which is not verification either.
> - **REACHABLE ON THE FLASHED IMAGE:** extended rides **BLE (`:4105`)** and **ESP-NOW (`:5795`)**, and `ble` ∈ closure. **NOT reachable on LoRa — and core's new compact path is CORRECT** (`:2034` takes the `Option`, `:2044` skips `None` rather than promoting it). **Gate 3 did not introduce this and models the right pattern.**
> - **THE BOUND, so severity stays honest: every route-less frame collapses to the SAME key ⇒ ONE phantom entry, not a table flood.** `seen` is `heapless::Vec<_,16>`; the attacker gets one slot, not sixteen.
> - **★ BUT NOT COSMETIC — and the reason is tonight's own arithmetic:** that one entry **increments `NBRS`**, and `NBRS` feeds `duty_cycle_refill`. **With the cliff at 3 boards, a single injected entry is a meaningful fraction of the margin ⇒ an unauthenticated peer can remotely tighten a victim's LoRa duty cycle at zero cost.** A better reason to rank it first than *"reserved value used as a key"*.
> - **NOT A REASON TO UNFLASH.** The bound is real and the gates 3+4 result stands.
> - **★★ THE PLACEMENT IS THE POINT: a SHIPPING pre-auth defect filed adjacent to cosmetics READS AS ROUTINE.** **Burial by adjacency — the mirror of the amplification problem this session spent hours on: a CLOSING conclusion travels too fast; an OPENING one placed in a housekeeping list travels too slowly.** It needed its own dispatch, not a bullet.
> - **OWNER: core's** (it says top of its list). The call site is the platform file; the ROUTE-ORIGIN-1 enforcement question is `r2-wire`. **Not mine to write — `main.rs` is core's under the standing ownership ruling.**
> - **AND core's EMITTER FIX BEATS MY REDACTION RULE — ADOPTED.** *"An allowlist cannot fail on encoding"* is still true, **but it is a convention applied after the fact to a line that prints a MAC byte on every received frame, and a doc-only gate gets omitted.** **REMOVE THE FIELD:** `decode=` and `verify=` carried the entire result 10/10 and 10/10 — **the origin contributed nothing to the evidence and everything to the exposure.** Then the allowlist has nothing to exclude and the encoding question cannot arise. **Enforce by construction, not convention.** *(And the chain is core's to name: it chose `{:?}` · I read its line and specified hex · supervisor built a filter from my pattern. Three lanes, one unexamined assumption about what a value LOOKS like.)*

> ## ⛔ MY #116 MECHANISM WAS INVENTED — AND THE BLAME CLOSES supervisor's OPEN ITEM IN core's FAVOUR (2026-07-20)

> ## 🔬 #115(c) — I ATTACKED core's `:865` THREE WAYS. TWO DIED, ONE SURVIVED AND IS MEASURED (2026-07-20)
> - **LINE DIVERGENCE, both cites correct:** `r2-core@33ee6295 crates/r2-route/src/engine.rs:865` **==** `dfr1195-fw@15014508 crates/r2-route/src/engine.rs:856`. Same statement, **9 lines apart, vendored vs live** — a bare `:865` between us is ambiguous. *(My own [[shared-checkout-path-dep-coupling]] trap, in the benign direction this time.)*
> - **ATTACK 1 — "the proxy is UNSOUND; an unauthenticated entry could exceed the ceiling". DIED.** Every `NeighbourEntry.confidence` writer is monotone-safe: `:313 new()` = `INIT_CONF` · `:360 update()` **min-clamps when `!is_authenticated`** · `:394 decay` and `:412` both **multiply by ≤1**. No other writer (`path.rs` is a DIFFERENT struct; `engine.rs:936/:994` only COPY out). ⇒ **an unauthenticated entry provably CANNOT exceed the ceiling. NO false positives — a forger cannot pass `:865`. core's security read holds.**
> - **ATTACK 2 — "the canonical predicate has no caller; phantom gate". DIED, AND HOW IT DIED IS THE FINDING ABOUT ME.** My caller-grep for `has_authenticated_viable` returned **ZERO non-test hits — because I scoped it to the VENDORED dfr1195 tree, which does not vendor `r2-harness`.** The real caller is `r2-core crates/r2-harness/src/node.rs:1252`. **And `node.rs:1233-1238` already documents the `:865` choice as DELIBERATE and flagged to supervisor:** *"The bound AB-006 suppress gate (plan_forward buffer-for-wake) **already uses the ceiling form**."* ⇒ **I would have filed a phantom-gate claim that the very file I was citing refutes, from a grep whose SCOPE excluded the caller.** *The exact defect class I have been auditing all session, run by me, tonight. Caught only by widening.*
> - **★★ ATTACK 3 SURVIVES — THE CEILING FORM IS ONE-WAY SOUND: NO FALSE POSITIVES, BUT FALSE NEGATIVES FOR GENUINE PEERS, AND ONE OF THEM IS NOT core's AND core's FIX WILL NOT REMOVE IT.** **MEASURED f32, not reasoned:** `0.5 + 0.2*(1.0-0.5)` = **`0.60000002384185791` = the EXACT bit pattern of `0.6f32`.** Equal, not near. ⇒ **a genuine peer heard ONCE as link-only then authenticated lands on EXACTLY the ceiling, and strict `>` is FALSE.** It needs a **second** authenticated reinforcement (0.68) to clear the bar. **That false negative exists with NO ordering bug present.**
> - ⇒ **TWO FALSE NEGATIVES AT ONE SITE WITH DIFFERENT CAUSES:** **(i)** core's (b) — entry at 0.6, clamped back by stamp-after-upsert; **(ii)** MINE — entry at 0.5, lands exactly on the boundary, **(b) is not its cause and fixing (b) does not fix it.** ⇒ **`:865`'s false-negative window is WIDER than (b).** *Direction is fail-**OPEN** both times (floods rather than black-holes) ⇒ functional lag, NOT a security hole — core's severity call stands unchanged.*
> - **★ DURABLE: A STRICT `>` AGAINST A BOUNDARY THE ARITHMETIC LANDS ON *EXACTLY* IS DECIDED BY FLOAT REPRESENTATION, NOT BY INTENT.** `>=` fires; `>` does not; **nothing in the code says which was meant.** `is_authenticated_viable()` (`neighbour.rs:428`) removes the boundary question entirely rather than re-tuning it. **Filed as hive task #110; OWNER IS core — reported, no hive write.**
> - **ACCEPTED FROM core WITHOUT ARGUMENT:** my *"it can only tie"* was **scoped to the comparator and stated as general. Wrong as stated** — `:865` is strict and does not tie. And core's own split (strict-above is the **provisional band operating as designed**, not (b)) is the right cut.
>
> ## 🔬 #115(b) CONFIRMED — AND IT IS NOT A ONE-LINE REORDER (2026-07-20)
> - **core's ORDERING BUG, VERBATIM at `15014508 neighbour.rs:660-662`:** `let entry = self.upsert(obs);` **reinforces**, then `entry.keepalive_hwm = Some(..)` **stamps after** — while `:372 is_authenticated() { keepalive_hwm.is_some() }` is what the clamp at `:360` reads. ⇒ **during the first verified keepalive's own `upsert`, a genuine peer is clamped to the provisional ceiling as if it were an attacker.** **And `:355-358`'s comment names the exact mechanism its own statement order defeats:** *"only a verified+fresh keepalive (`accept_keepalive`, **which stamps `keepalive_hwm`**) lifts it out of the provisional band."* *(Arithmetic re-derived: `0.5+0.2×0.5 = 0.600` exactly; `0.6+0.2×0.4 = 0.680`. **Attacker at the ceiling in two frames; defender needs two 30 s rounds — the attacker's clock is FRAMES, the defender's is the EMIT INTERVAL.**)*
> - **★★ BUT THE FIX IS NOT AVAILABLE AS STATED — `upsert` (`:550-568`) IS CREATE-OR-FIND *AND* REINFORCE, FUSED:** existing ⇒ `entry.update(&obs)` **which IS the reinforce/clamp**; absent ⇒ `evict_lowest()` then `NeighbourEntry::new(&obs)` — **the entry does not exist until then.** ⇒ **ON A FIRST-SEEN ORIGIN THERE IS NOTHING TO STAMP BEFORE `upsert`. THE REORDER CANNOT BE WRITTEN.** It works only for an entry that already exists — **the case that is not broken.** **The fix must get the auth state TO the clamp** (an `authenticated: bool` parameter, or splitting `find_or_create` from `update`); **re-reinforcing after the stamp double-counts α.** **core's finding stands unchanged; only the sizing moves.**
> - **?LEAD, NOT EXTENDED — the eviction path is scoped OUT by ruling and I am holding that:** the same ordering means **`evict_lowest()` inside `upsert` also runs before the stamp**, while `:371` documents that authenticated entries *"MUST NOT be evicted to admit an unauthenticated upsert"* ⇒ **a genuine peer's first keepalive is an unauthenticated upsert for EVICTION purposes too.** **NOT claiming a defect — flagging so that when (b) lands the eviction path is RE-CHECKED rather than assumed fixed.** *(And it hits TWO cases: a first-seen origin AND an existing link-only entry being authenticated for the first time — a test should target both.)*
> - **★★ SUPERVISOR'S NARROWING RE-DERIVED AT THE SHA AND IT HOLDS — `new()` NEVER RUNS THE CLAMP, SO THE FIRST-SEEN CASE IS INERT.** `15014508 neighbour.rs:297-320`: `NeighbourEntry::new` sets `confidence: NEIGHBOUR_INIT_CONF` **in the struct literal — it does NOT call `update()`.** No reinforce, no clamp. ⇒ **(b) bites ONLY the PRE-EXISTING LINK-ONLY entry** — heard first as a data/beacon frame, authenticated later. **My "two cases" was one case.** *I derived "the reorder cannot be written" from `upsert`'s shape and stopped at the call site instead of reading the constructor — right conclusion, one link short of the trace.* Constants confirmed: `constants.rs:66 INIT_CONF=0.5 · :72 PROVISIONAL_CEILING=0.6 · :80 POS_ALPHA=0.2`; clamp `:360-364`.
> - **★ TIGHTER BOUND (MINE) — (b) COSTS EXACTLY ONE CYCLE, NOT A PERSISTING WINDOW.** `:661` stamps `keepalive_hwm` **immediately after** the clamped `update()`, so the **next** keepalive sees `is_authenticated()==true` and reinforces **unclamped**. ⇒ magnitude is **one reinforcement lost — 0.68 → 0.6, recovered on the following beat: ~30 s at the emit interval, Δ 0.08.** The 60 s bring-up figure is the right order; the mechanism is a **one-cycle LAG, not sustained suppression.** And it is **zero at 0.5** (`min(0.6,0.6)` no-op) — real only for an entry heard ≥2× before authenticating.
> - **★★ CORRECTION TO "RANKS AT-OR-ABOVE" — IT CANNOT RANK ABOVE. IT TIES.** An unauthenticated entry is **clamped to 0.6**, and 0.6 is also the clamped genuine value ⇒ **(b) does not hand the attacker a LEAD; it manufactures an EXACT EQUALITY for one cycle.** ⇒ **#115(a) AND #115(b) ARE COUPLED, NOT TWO ITEMS: (b) MANUFACTURES THE TIE, (a) DECIDES IT.** Filed separately in #115, but the severity of (b) is **entirely a function of how the comparator breaks equal confidence** — tie-break on auth state ⇒ (b) is cosmetic; tie-break on recency or slot order ⇒ (b) is the whole defect. *Comparator is core's and scoped to core: naming the coupling, not extending into it.*
> - **✅ MY EVICTION LEAD IS REFUTED — KILLED, NOT LEFT PARKED.** There are **TWO evictors and the split is by CALLER, not by entry state**: `:706 evict_lowest()` **ungated** vs `:740 evict_lowest_provisional()` which **skips `is_authenticated()` slots at `:721`**; `:558 upsert` → ungated, `:588 upsert_provisional` → gated. **Caller-grep on `NeighbourTable::upsert`: 18 hits, ONE production caller — `:660`, inside `accept_keepalive`, the VERIFIED path.** The rest are `tests.rs` plus a **different 3-arg `upsert`** on dfr1195 `peers.rs`/`ble.rs`/`lora.rs`/`wifi.rs`. ⇒ **`:371`'s MUST NOT binds admission of an UNAUTHENTICATED upsert, and that path uses the gated evictor. The prohibition does not bind where I flagged it. The re-check trigger supervisor attached to the park is DISCHARGED — nothing owed when (b) lands.**
> - **METHOD: the lead died on instrument 1, the cheapest one I have.** Raising it as a lead rather than a claim was right; **leaving it unrun for a full exchange was not** — a park has a cost, and the cost is that everyone downstream carries it as live.
> - **★ MANIFEST CURRENCY — core's "three generations behind HEAD" lands on my own file, and it survives only because of an anchor choice worth naming:** `f8b78415` landed after I wrote it, **but the manifest anchors staleness to the FLASHED STATE (`2ba6612b`), not to HEAD**, and the boards have not been reflashed — **so every claim in it is still true.** ⇒ **A STALENESS CLAIM ANCHORED TO HEAD DECAYS ON EVERY PUSH; ONE ANCHORED TO THE DEPLOYED STATE DECAYS ONLY ON A DEPLOY.** **That was half luck** — I anchored there because the flashed sha was the fact I had, not because I reasoned it. **Recorded as a rule: manifests anchor to the deployed state, never to a branch tip.** *(android's CURRENCY axis, second application within the hour, on my own artefact.)*

> - **THE HOLD STANDS FOR A DIFFERENT REASON, AND THE REASON IS THE POINT: ESTABLISHED** — built at `4f17efa`. **NOT ESTABLISHED** — the branch has moved through `15014508` to `f8b78415` and **nobody has traced whether any intervening commit reaches the `xiaobridge` path.** `xiao_bridge_task` is spawned *instead of* `io_task`, so recent changes land in code this target never runs — **but "probably unaffected" is a CONJECTURE, not a provenance check, and the file will not record one as the other.** ⇒ **NOT-TO-FLASH pending a rebuild at a named commit or a trace of `4f17efa..`.**

> - **★★ android's FRAMING IS BETTER THAN MY FIX: *A BLANKET HEADER IS NOT A PER-ARTEFACT STATUS; THE TABLE IS WHAT PEOPLE READ WHEN THEY ALREADY HAVE A SHA.*** That is **filename-is-not-a-key one level up** — **I wrote a sha table to defeat name-based reasoning and then put a name-shaped generalisation above it. A blanket header is a filename for a directory.** And **when a header and a row disagree, the RESTRICTIVE reading is the safe default** — android held rather than resolving by inference, which is what stopped a stale status becoming a bad flash.
> - **★★★ AND ITS SELF-CORRECTION IS A THIRD VERIFICATION AXIS I DID NOT HAVE: *"byte-verified means the file is what the record said. It never meant the record was live."*** ⇒ **IDENTITY · FUNCTION · CURRENCY.** A sha match proves **which file**, never **whether the record naming it is still true.** **It applied to me the same hour: I verified `2ba6612b` byte-identically and reported it as THE artifact — an IDENTITY claim whose CURRENCY held only because it was flashed within the hour.** Banked to [[identity-verified-is-not-function-verified]] as android's.

One flood = one transmission at any candidate count. A phantom adds a ROW, not a FRAME. Airtime untouched.**

> | measure | ttyACM3 | ttyACM0 |
> |---|---|---|
> | control (status lines) | 146 | 146 |
> | `LORA-CPT` | **10** | **10** |
> | `decode=ok` | **10/10** | **10/10** |

> | `LORA-BEACON` / `LORA-RX` | 10 / 10 | 10 / 10 |
> | **`nbrs` non-zero** | **38/146 = 26.0%** | **32/146 = 21.9%** |
>
> - **artifact `2ba6612b1bb4aaffb39e48751efb2992e0a325f8e71908cb00701edbdc9a7f8c` on BOTH boards**, flashed **17 s apart (stamps in supervisor's report; written here as a delta because `HH:MM:SS` false-positives the hygiene gate's MAC-tail matcher), INSIDE the safe band** *(`offset > 1647 ms` and `period − offset > 1647 ms`)*, **so no stagger reset was needed.** The recipe worked as a *prediction*, not just a post-hoc explanation.
> - **★★ MY TTL MODEL HELD TO WITHIN ONE SAMPLE.** Predicted `peer_ttl_s`/emit = 7/30 = **23.3% ⇒ ~34 of 146**; **measured mean 35.** ⇒ **THIS IS THE PAYOFF FOR REFUSING core's *"draw no negative conclusion from this run"*.** Without the denominator, *"`nbrs` is intermittent"* is unreadable — **is 26% good?** With it, **26% against a predicted 23% is a CONFIRMATION OF THE CHARACTERISED DEFECT.** *The number only became evidence because the model was written down first.*
> - **★ BOTH PRE-REGISTRATIONS WRONG — AND THAT IS THE STRONGEST FORM OF THE RESULT.** I said the demux; core said `verify_compact` and named it as the line it would read first. **10/10 decode, 10/10 verify, zero failures.** **Neither lane could retro-fit a story afterwards, because both stories were on the record before the run and both are dead.**
> - **ROW RECORDED IN GH ISSUE 19 — REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATION RECORD — with its pinned sha, the shared-crate vs platform-file split, and EIGHT gaps travelling with it.** *That is what makes it an inheritance rather than a status.*
> - **⚠★★ THE REDACTION FAILURE IS MINE BEFORE IT IS SUPERVISOR'S.** I raised the leak correctly and then **supplied the redaction as `origin=Some(0x00__)`; supervisor built its filter from my pattern.** Measured `:2040`: `"… origin={:?} …", origin` with `origin: Option<u16>` — **Rust `{:?}` on a `u16` prints DECIMAL**, so the line emits the origin **in DECIMAL**, while my pattern matched only the **hex** form. **Both MAC bytes passed untouched.** **AND I HAD READ THAT EXACT LINE while verifying core's compliance** — I reasoned *"it is a hive_id, so it is hex"*, **from the value's conceptual form instead of the emitter's format string.** ⇒ **A REDACTION PATTERN MUST BE DERIVED FROM THE EMITTER'S FORMAT STRING. A redactor tuned to the wrong encoding is a scanner with no emitter.** **★ THE DURABLE FIX IS NOT A BETTER PATTERN: QUOTE ONLY THE FIELDS THAT CARRY EVIDENTIARY VALUE — AN ALLOWLIST CANNOT FAIL ON ENCODING; A BLOCKLIST CAN, AND DID, TWICE IN ONE SESSION.** Banked to [[green-cell-needs-pinned-code]]. **Scope: issue 19's published body is clean by leak check; the exposure is supervisor's transcript — bench-chat, two MAC bytes, disclosed.**
> - **SYMMETRY WORTH KEEPING:** I corrected a **durable memory**; supervisor corrected a **task description**. **Both are artifacts that propagate a claim past the point anyone re-checks it** — supervisor named that about its own record before I would have.
> - **POST-FLASH, MINE:** the `seen` per-bearer **one-line filter** (on the tag core landed), and **running the coverage-inversion check WITH step (ii) on `r2-hive-bin` and the wasm hive — the reciprocal I owe core and have not run.**

> - **📜 ROY STANDING DIRECTIVE (2026-07-20) — A GREEN CELL IS A STATUS; A GREEN CELL WITH ITS PINNED CODE IS AN INHERITANCE.** Every row that turns green is recorded in `reality2-ai/r2-specifications` issue 19, **REFERENCE IMPLEMENTATION RECORD**, **in the same act as flipping the cell**, carrying five things: capability+board · **source sha AND artifact sha256** · mechanism **AND whether it lives in a SHARED CRATE (every board inherits free) or a PLATFORM FILE (per-board, must be re-implemented)** · metal evidence with the instrument **named by what it PHYSICALLY OBSERVES** (*`tx_hi_admitted` = handed to the radio, NOT on air* — that precision survived three hops because it was named honestly) · **★ the KNOWN GAPS that travel with it, NOT optional** (*"a reference implementation that hides its caveats is a trap"*). **Banked to memory: [[green-cell-needs-pinned-code]].** **Why it exists is my most expensive lesson today:** a known-good bidirectional RX state existed from 2026-06-22 and **nobody could point to it — I asserted the opposite from recall while holding the archive that refuted it.** **PINNED TO A SHA, NOT REMEMBERED.**

> - **✅ core's CANONICAL-BRANCH CLAIM VERIFIED IN MY OWN CHECKOUT — MY "COMPACT HAS NO `last_hop`" WAS TRUE OF THE BRANCH I READ AND FALSE OF CANON.** `@r2-core crates/r2-wire/src/types.rs` on `r2-core-consolidation`: **`:197 pub fn last_hop(&self) -> Option<u16>`** and **`:209 pub fn append(&mut self, hive_id: u16)`** — both present on `CompactRouteStack`; **the fw branch has neither.** ⇒ **MERGE FORWARD, DO NOT ADD AN ACCESSOR. Fourth cross-branch divergence, and the first that would have cost real work** — core would have written a **second copy of a method that already exists**, conflicting with its own original. **core's deliberate full branch-diff BEFORE writing is right and I back it.**
> - **🔴🔴 THE `seen` TAG DOES NOT DO WHAT THE RULING SAYS IT DOES — IT DOES NOT MOVE THE CLIFF BACK TO 4 BOARDS.** `:1753-1757` verbatim: `seen.iter().filter(|(_, t)| …).count()` — **IT COUNTS ENTRIES, NOT DISTINCT PEERS.** With the tag, one peer heard on both bearers still yields **two rows** — `(0x0052, t, Lora)` and `(0x00529928, t, Ble)` — **and the filter counts 2.** **The tag makes them LEGITIMATELY different rows instead of ACCIDENTALLY colliding ones; it cannot MERGE them**, because merging needs truncated→full resolution, which needs the roster, **which cannot match an unprovisioned board. Same wall, third consumer.** ⇒ **"the tag keeps gates 3+4 safe on a 3-board bench" is FALSE — with a global NBRS, 3 boards on two bearers still reads nbrs=4 ⇒ refill 50 ⇒ 1.98× over. THE CLIFF IS STILL AT 3.** **What the tag DOES buy is real and worth its 4 lines — it stops a 16-bit truncated key sharing a namespace with a 32-bit hive_id. It is just not the cliff fix.** **TONIGHT IS SAFE EITHER WAY: 2 boards ⇒ nbrs ≤ 2 ⇒ inside `0..=2 => 100` ⇒ 0.99×.**
> - **⚠ SCOPE CONFLICT — THE RULING AND core's ADOPTION CROSSED AND ARE DIFFERENT CHANGES.** supervisor **ruled** `Vec<(u32,u32,u8)>` **plus** *"NBRS remains a global count … record it as unfixed"*; core **then** wrote *"per-bearer: your subsumption is right and I adopt it over my own tag proposal … 3 boards reads as nbrs=2, the cliff stays at 4."* **A tagged shared table ≠ per-bearer tables.** core's cliff-stays-at-4 is **true of per-bearer tables and false of the tag that was ruled.** ⇒ **core MUST NOT implement per-bearer tables under a ruling that authorised a tag — scope creep by crossed messages.** **My lean, stated as a lean: ship the TAG only tonight** — minimum that removes the type confusion, 4 lines, and the per-bearer table then becomes a one-line filter later, **which is the very argument used to approve the tag. Do not grow tonight's commit.**

>   - **PRE-REGISTERED, AS ASKED — I SUSPECT THE *DEMUX*, NOT THE PUSH, AND FOR A CHECKABLE REASON:** `:6423 target: my_tg_hash, // compact single target = TG hash (0xF305FE07)` ⇒ **`couple_ok` WILL PASS on a compact Event** ⇒ **once a frame decodes the push follows almost immediately**, so a null implicates the **decode**. The push is a guarded 3-line move; the demux must branch on an ordinal destructured at the drain, **and `:4443` makes a content fallback silently wrong.**
>   - **★★ FINDING 1 (pre-write, core's call) — ROY'S RULING IS NOT ENFORCED BY THE GATE SUPERVISOR NAMED.** `:1989-1992`: `#[cfg(not(feature="multitg"))] couple_ok = m.header.target_group == my_tg_hash;` vs `#[cfg(feature="multitg")] couple_ok = verify_extended(&m, &group_hmac);` — **`multitg` is NOT in `closure(fakesensor,ble)`** ⇒ **on the flashed build `couple_ok` is a PLAINTEXT TAG COMPARE, NOT an HMAC verification**, and the tg_hash rides in the clear in every frame. `:2038`'s comment (*"VERIFIED pulse ONLY … AUTHENTICATED payload"*) **overclaims — eighth comment/code contradiction.** ⇒ **as specified, gate 4 would let an UNAUTHENTICATED frame create a neighbour — the exact thing supervisor said MUST NOT happen.** Masked today because only HBs reach the arm; **(b) widens it to every Event on every bearer.** **core's call: gate the push on a real `verify_*`, or knowingly relax Roy's ruling to plaintext-tag on non-`multitg` builds. It MUST be a decision, not an inheritance.**
>   - **★ FINDING 2 (recorded, not for this commit) — THE COMPACT ROUTE ID HAS ONLY 8 EFFECTIVE BITS ON UNPROVISIONED BOARDS.** `:6430 route.entries[0] = (my_hive >> 16) as u16;` and an unprovisioned `my_hive = mac_low3 = MAC & 0x00FF_FFFF` **always has a 0x00 high byte by construction** ⇒ **`0x00XX`, an 8-bit space.** **Tonight is safe — the two boards give `0x0050` and `0x0052`, distinct.** But across N unprovisioned boards it is a **birthday problem over 256: N=9 ≈ 14%, N=12 ≈ 23%** chance some pair collides ⇒ two peers merge in `seen` ⇒ **`nbrs` UNDERCOUNTS ⇒ into the duty budget again**, plus dedup/routing confusion. **Roy's 9–12 board roadmap.**
>   - **ACCEPTANCE (supervisor's, with my denominator):** **PRIMARY `nbrs` non-zero at all, either board — one sample is a PASS**; `peer_ttl_s`=7 s vs a 30 s emit ⇒ **~23% of samples, intermittent is NOT failure**; ~35 of ~150 expected ⇒ **0 of ~150 is decisive**. **SECONDARY: `LORA-BEACON` must not regress from 9–10 per 300 s.** **FALSIFIER: `nbrs`=0 while `LORA-RX len=29` prints ⇒ the demux or the push did not take.**
