> - **✅ ROY RULED GATE 4 = OPTION (b): `seen` IS FED BY ANY *VERIFIED* FRAME, NOT ONLY `Heartbeat` (2026-07-20).** My lean, taken. **Verification gate KEPT** — *"any VERIFIED frame", never "any frame"*; `couple_ok && reach_ok` still governs. Liveness becomes **group-keyed, not per-member** — **not a new weakness** (a co-member can already forge any frame under a shared group key) and it **removes no existing protection**. ⚠ **(b) CLOSES THE BENCH BLOCKER, NOT THE SECURITY PROPERTY — per-member insider-proof liveness stays open and MUST NOT be recorded as closed by this.**
>   - **core's H9 TRAP CONFIRMED VERBATIM (`:2035-2051`) AND ADOPTED:** the arm holds **two independent mechanisms**. `parse_seq(m.payload).unwrap_or(0)` / `parse_dc` / `accept_keepalive` / `set_neighbour_duty_class` are **HB-payload-specific and MUST STAY GATED on `MsgType::Heartbeat`** — moving the whole block would feed **`hb_seq = 0`** (a silent `unwrap_or(0)` on an Event with no seq field) into an **H9 monotonic keepalive-HWM freshness check**, best case rejecting every Event, worst case corrupting freshness for real heartbeats. **`seen` takes only `sender_hive` + `now_s` — no payload parse — so ONLY the `seen` push moves.**
> - **🔴🔴🔴 #111 BLOCKER, NOW SUBSUMING #106 — `seen` NEEDS A PER-BEARER KEY. THREE DEFECTS, ONE STRUCTURAL FIX, AND TWO OF THEM WOULD HAVE BEEN *INTRODUCED* BY THE GATE-3+4 CHANGE (task #106, 2026-07-20).** Found by checking whether my own intended change would actually work, before writing a line.
>   - **★★ B — u16/u32 KEY COLLISION, TYPE-LEVEL:** `crates/r2-wire/src/types.rs:255` **`ExtendedRouteStack::origin() -> Option<u32>`** vs `:189` **`CompactRouteStack::origin() -> Option<u16>`**, with `:166` verbatim *"Each entry is bits **[31:16]** of FNV-1a 32-bit of the hive's device UUID."* **`seen` is keyed on the FULL 32-bit id.** ⇒ **the same peer heard on both bearers yields TWO entries ⇒ `nbrs` DOUBLE-COUNTS ⇒ straight into `duty_cycle_refill`.** **core's 4-board cliff moves to 3** (3 boards both bearers ⇒ nbrs=4 ⇒ refill 50 ⇒ **1.98× over**). `seen` capacity 16 also halves to ~8 real peers.
>   - **★ C — `origin()` IS THE *ORIGINATOR*, NOT THE PEER WE HEARD.** Both `:255`/`:189` are `route_stack[0]`. Extended has `last_hop()` (`:271`); **compact has NO `last_hop` accessor at all.** ⇒ on a **relayed** compact frame, feeding `seen` from `origin()` credits liveness to a node **we cannot hear**, inflating `nbrs` with non-neighbours — again into the duty budget. **Coincides only at 1 hop — tonight's bench, not the 9–12 board target.**
>   - **⇒ ONE FIX FOR ALL THREE: MAKE `seen` PER-BEARER.** LoRa keeps its own table of compact (u16) ids; BLE/ESP-NOW keep theirs of extended (u32) ids. **No cross-width matching, no double-count, and `lora.set_neighbour_count()` reads the LoRa table — which IS the #106 scope fix, arrived at from the opposite direction. I was going to propose two changes; they are one.**
>   - **NOT MINE TO DECIDE:** whether `CompactRouteStack` gains a `last_hop()` or `seen` is documented originator-keyed on LoRa — **core's crate, and I will not add an accessor to r2-wire**; and whether **`CompactHeader.target`** (`:161`, *"Target hive/group … or special value"*, **overloaded, NOT named `target_group`**) carries `tg_hash` for a group-addressed compact Event — **a wire-semantics ruling.**
>   - **RECORDED, NOT DISCOVERED LATER:** compact `hmac_tag: Option<[u8; 8]>` vs extended's 32 ⇒ **Roy's "any VERIFIED frame" liveness is backed by an 8-BYTE tag on LoRa and a 32-byte tag elsewhere. Canon, not new — but the ruled property is BEARER-ASYMMETRIC IN STRENGTH.**
>   - **SHAPE, REPORTED NOT LANDED:** per-bearer `seen` **→** gate-3 demux on `Transport` at `:1981` (**never on content**, `:4443`) **→** gate-4 `seen` push out of the HB arm behind `couple_ok && reach_ok`, **H9 block left behind. Gates 3+4 land TOGETHER** — either alone reads as total failure, the fourth time tonight this stack produced that shape.
>   - **core's OVER-BLOCK CORRECTION ACCEPTED AND RE-DERIVED:** 2 boards ⇒ nbrs=1, 3 ⇒ nbrs=2, **both inside `0..=2 => 100` ⇒ 0.99× unchanged ⇒ gates 3+4 safe on THIS bench** — **but only if the double-count is fixed first, or 3 boards reads as 4.** *(core: "I over-blocked in the direction that protects my own fix from being re-tested" — the mirror of over-closing, second time tonight it leaned that way.)*
>   - **THE 4-BOARD CLIFF IS ON THE RECORD FOR THE NEXT BRING-UP:** at 5+ boards the **beacon alone is 4.4× over** and the **minimum beacon interval becomes 132 s against a `peer_ttl_s` of 7.** **The TTL, the beacon interval and the duty band are ONE COUPLED SYSTEM expressed as THREE INDEPENDENT CONSTANTS** — specs should see them together.
>   - **✅ THE IRQ BIT IS CLOSED FROM THE PART:** circuits cited **Semtech DS.SX1261-2.W.APP rev 2.2, Table 13-29 p.85, PDF sha256 pinned** ⇒ **`PreambleDetected = 1<<2` CONFIRMED, `HeaderValid = 1<<4`, `SyncWordValid = 1<<3` is FSK-only.** **My `1<<4` was wrong and named `HeaderValid` by accident.** *A twice-wrong constant gets closed from the datasheet, not from a fourth memory.*
> - **(superseded, kept for the evidence) 🔴🔴🔴 #111 BLOCKER — `NBRS` IS A CROSS-BEARER COUNT DRIVING A PER-BEARER LoRa DUTY BUDGET. LIVE TODAY, AND IT POISONS core's FIX BEFORE IT IS WRITTEN (task #106, 2026-07-20).**
>   - **core's DUTY-COLLAPSE BLOCKER — RE-DERIVED, EXACT, AND ACCEPTED.** `NBRS` is not a display value: `:5386 lora.set_neighbour_count(NBRS.load())` ⇒ `lora_transport.rs:182 set_refill_rate(duty_cycle_refill(n))`. Demand **98.9 ms/s** (data 1647/30 s = 54.9 + beacon 1319/30 s = 44.0) against **nbrs 0-2 ⇒ 100 ⇒ 0.99×** · **3-4 ⇒ 50 ⇒ 1.98× OVER** · **5+ ⇒ 10 ⇒ 9.89× OVER.** **Beacon ALONE at 1% = 4.4× over with zero data; min beacon interval at 1% is 131.9 s, not 30.** Roy's 9- and 12-board meshes sit in the 1% band. ⇒ **TODAY'S BUDGET WORKS ONLY BECAUSE `nbrs` IS BROKEN — FIXING IT ARMS THE REGRESSION core FIXED TONIGHT.**
>   - **★★ BUT THE COUNT IS THE WRONG QUANTITY.** `:1361 seen: heapless::Vec<(u32, u32), 16>` — **(hive_id, timestamp), NO transport tag** — and every DATA_RX producer drains into the same `io_task` and the same `seen`: **`:4105` Ble · `:5357`/`:5378` Lora · `:5795` WifiMesh/ESP-NOW.** ⇒ **BLE AND ESP-NOW PEERS THROTTLE THE LoRa RADIO.** 3 BLE HB peers on an **empty LoRa channel** ⇒ 5%; 5 peers ⇒ 1%. **Those peers do not contend for LoRa airtime at all.** **R2-LORA §4.2 neighbour-scaling is about LoRa CHANNEL CONTENTION — counting a BLE neighbour is not conservative, it is the WRONG QUANTITY.**
>   - **LIVE NOW, NOT A FUTURE REGRESSION** — invisible tonight only because `nbrs=0` on every bearer. **On any `blemesh`/`espnow` build with peers, the LoRa duty is ALREADY being tightened by traffic on a different radio.**
>   - **⇒ IT BREAKS core's FIX BEFORE IT IS WRITTEN:** `interval >= ToA / refill_fraction` **inherits the contamination** — derive from a wrong count, get a wrong interval. **THE SCOPE FIX IS A PRECONDITION FOR core's PRECONDITION.** `seen` needs a per-bearer key, or `NBRS` a LoRa-scoped sibling. **Gate-4 (b) compounds it: feed `seen` from any verified frame and BLE APPLICATION traffic starts throttling LoRa.**
>   - **★ SECOND, AND IT CUTS AGAINST THE OSCILLATION BEING SELF-LIMITING:** `:5384` recomputes the refill **once per 60 s**. That is **LAG, NOT DAMPING** — a feedback loop whose observable it starves, with a 60 s delay in the loop, is **MORE** prone to a limit cycle. 60 s ≈ 2 emit periods, so it can swing a full band before seeing the consequence. **The update cadence is part of the loop, not an implementation detail.**
>   - **(a) vs (b): core's ARGUMENT BEATS MINE AND I ADOPT IT.** `:1752` already calls `seen` *"peers heard within MESH_PEER_TTL_S"* — **a verified Event IS a peer heard; the Heartbeat-only restriction is an ARTEFACT OF WHERE THE WRITER SITS, not a semantic.** **And core's caveat is a correctness bound I did not have and would have shipped without: liveness driven by APPLICATION traffic means a SILENT SENSOR READS AS GONE, and HB exists precisely to be traffic-independent ⇒ (b) MUST BE ADDITIVE — HB *OR* any verified frame, never HB replaced.**
>   - **SEQUENCING:** **scope-fix (per-bearer count) → interval-from-duty (core) → gate-3 demux (mine) → gate-4 additive (b) → gate-5 TTL (specs). NOTHING LANDS BEFORE THE SCOPE FIX**, because every later step reads that number.
>   - **?SPECS: is the §4.2 neighbour count PER-BEARER or PER-NODE?** If per-node, the coupling is intentional and this is a spec question, not a bug. **I read it as per-bearer (channel contention) and am NOT ruling on core's canon.**
> - **✅ #110 CLOSED — RECEPTION CONFIRMED, PHASE-LOCK WAS CAUSAL, ROOT CAUSE WAS THE FLASHING CADENCE (2026-07-20).** supervisor staggered the resets 16 s (vs the 30 s its flashing imposed) and re-ran 300 s: **`LORA-BEACON` 0 → 9 (ttyACM3) and 0 → 10 (ttyACM0)**, plus **`LORA-RX len=29 rssi=-54dBm` / `-73dBm`** — the 29 B apiary data frame is being received. Beacons at **−34 to −41 dBm**. Positive control 143 status lines in **both** runs, so the original zero was real, not an absent-file pass. **First bidirectional LoRa on this bench since first light.** ⇒ **RETIRED BY ONE MEASUREMENT: RF-switch contention · DIO1 wiring · antenna/PHY · and MY candidate (2), SF12 marginality — SF12 is receiving cleanly.** circuits stood down on measurement rather than inference. **core's crate is clean on the RX path; its `RxDone`-re-arm coupling, DIO2 opt-out and missing CRC counters are all still real and still open, but none was tonight's fault.** `PreambleDetected` has **no consumer tonight** — reception is proven, so the ladder has nothing left to discriminate; it stays worth arming as the **RX denominator**, at leisure, **and `1<<2` still needs the DATASHEET.**
> - **🔴🔴🔴 #111 OPEN — FRAMES ARRIVE AND DO NOT BECOME NEIGHBOURS. FIVE GATES, EACH ALONE SUFFICIENT FOR `nbrs=0`; THREE CLEARED, TWO STRUCTURAL, AND THE FOURTH IS MINE (task #105).** `nbrs=0` on **all 143 samples, both boards**, while `LORA-RX len=29` prints. core predicted the TTL would suppress it to ~23%; **we measured 0%**, so something else also blocks it.
>   - **GATE 3 (core found, my call site) — `io_task` DECODES EXTENDED ONLY.** `:1981 match decode_extended(&scratch[..n])`; `decode_compact` appears **only** at `:5456`/`:5608`, both inside `xiao_bridge_task`, **spawned INSTEAD of `io_task` under `xiaobridge`**; `:6438`/`:6441` apiary emits `sign_compact`+`encode_compact`. ⇒ **a compact LoRa frame fails `decode_extended` and is dropped before any coupling gate.** **Fix seam is clean:** `:5357` pushes `(f, total, 0, Transport::Lora as u8)` — the ordinal is in the tuple and in scope at the drain (`:2259`). **DEMUX ON TRANSPORT, NEVER ON CONTENT** — `:4443` verified verbatim: *extended byte0 is structurally decodable as compact*, so try-compact-first would **mis-parse every extended frame**.
>   - **★★★ GATE 4 — MINE, FOUND NOW, AND core's DEMUX DOES NOT TOUCH IT.** `:1983 MsgType::Heartbeat =>` is the arm containing `seen` (`:2046`/`:2049`), and **`seen` has NO other writer**. `:6411` apiary emits **`MsgType::Event`**, and `:6445 mesh_broadcast` is **the only LoRa egress in the file**. Every Heartbeat egress (`:1651`, `:1706`, `:1804`, `:1939`, `:2361`, `:2508`) is **`mesh_broadcast_extended`**, which `:4421` documents as *"the LoRa carrier is EXCLUDED BY CANON"* — **no LoRa arm.** ⇒ **THE ONLY FRAME CLASS ON LoRa IS `Event`; `seen` IS FED ONLY BY `Heartbeat`; NO HEARTBEAT HAS EVER BEEN TRANSMITTED ON LoRa BY THIS FIRMWARE.** Land the demux and a compact Event decodes, hits the `msg_type` match, falls to a non-Heartbeat arm, **and still never reaches `seen.push`.**
>   - **GATE 4 IS A SPEC CONSEQUENCE, NOT A CODING SLIP:** §5.1 rules compact-on-LoRa · the heartbeat is extended · **therefore LoRa carries no liveness.** *The split was ruled and its consumers were not traced* — the shape core named about §5.1 an hour earlier, **and this is its second broken consumer.**
>   - **THE FIX IS A DESIGN CHOICE AND NOT MINE ALONE:** **(a)** emit a **compact heartbeat** on LoRa — preserves *liveness-comes-from-HB*, needs a canon-legal compact HB, and is **expensive at SF12** (a second frame class on a bearer at 9.9% duty with ~4 s slack in 420 s); **(b)** feed `seen` from **any VERIFIED frame** — a HMAC-verified Event proves liveness at least as well as an HB, needs no new wire form, **but changes what liveness MEANS** and touches core's H9/DG-1 stamping. **My lean is (b) on Occam; liveness semantics are core's and specs'. NOT landing it on my own read.**
>   - **GATE 5 = core's TTL, downstream of all four:** `peer_ttl_s`=7 s vs a 30 s emit **cannot SUSTAIN an entry even once 3 and 4 are fixed.** Constraint is `peer_ttl_s > emit_interval + longest_dark_stretch`.
> - **🔴 THE `PreambleDetected` BIT IS `1<<2`, NOT `1<<4` — I WROTE THE WRONG VALUE WHILE CITING MY OWN COMMIT THAT FIXES IT (2026-07-20).** core caught it. **`609c11e` (mine, r2-hive) reads verbatim: *"on the SX1262 `PreambleDetected` is **BIT 2 (`1<<2` = 0x04)**; `1<<5` (0x20) is `HeaderErr`."*** **I quoted that sha in the same message where I wrote `1<<4`. The correct value was inside the text I was citing.** History of this one constant: **`1<<5` (wrong) → `1<<2` (my own fix) → `1<<4` (wrong again, also mine)** — two of three wrong, and the second written while pointing at the first one's fix. core's method is the right one: **four driver constants (`TX_DONE 1<<0`, `RX_DONE 1<<1`, `CRC_ERR 1<<6`, `TIMEOUT 1<<9`) all corroborate the SX126x table independently**, and my own commit names `1<<5 = HeaderErr`, so **bit 4 is `HeaderValid`.** ⇒ **A CONSTANT THAT HAS BEEN WRONG TWICE MUST BE TAKEN FROM THE DATASHEET, NOT FROM EITHER LANE'S MEMORY, BEFORE THE MASK IS WRITTEN.** **core's `1<<4 = HeaderValid` addition ADOPTED — my wrong bit named a useful one**, and its 5-row ladder separates *energy-heard-never-decoded* (SNR/SF margin) from *decoded-then-corrupted*, which my 4-row could not.
> - **🔴 core's TTL DEFECT — VERIFIED, AND ITS CONSTRAINT OMITS ITS BASE TERM.** Confirmed all three legs at `a26119f6`: `:1362` `profile.peer_ttl_s // §3.2.2 (default 7) — ~3 missed beats`; `:1755` the TTL filter feeding `NBRS`; and **`mesh_broadcast` (the LoRa egress) has EXACTLY ONE caller, `:6445`** — every other site calls `mesh_broadcast_extended`, which `:4421` documents as *"the LoRa carrier is EXCLUDED BY CANON"*. ⇒ **one LoRa-refreshing caller throttled to 1/30 s against a 7 s TTL.** core changed a rate and did not trace its consumers — *the same shape I owned earlier for observables.*
>   - **★★ BUT core FRAMES THE FIX AS *"longest dark stretch < `peer_ttl_s`"*, WHICH OMITS THE BASE TERM.** At `peer_ttl_s`=7 and emit=30, **the neighbour expires between two consecutive SUCCESSFUL receptions** — flawless RX, zero dark stretches, and it still expires for 23 s of every 30. ⇒ **the constraint is `peer_ttl_s > emit_interval + longest_dark_stretch`; the emit interval is the FLOOR.** **No jitter sizing can satisfy it while the TTL sits below the emit period itself** — the two *are* one problem, as core says, **but the TTL term dominates.** *(core's 90 s lands correctly by the corrected formula — 30 base + 2 missed × 30 — so the number is right and the stated reasoning was missing the base.)* **Durable generalisation, core's: ANY BEARER WHOSE FRAME INTERVAL EXCEEDS `peer_ttl_s` CANNOT SUSTAIN A NEIGHBOUR ENTRY** — an unwritten §3.2.2 ↔ §4.2/§4.3 relationship, specs' to pin.
>   - **★★ AND core's SCORING RULE OVER-CORRECTS — I WILL NOT LET *"draw no negative conclusion"* STAND UNQUALIFIED.** The TTL defect degrades `nbrs` from *always-1* to **1 on ~23% of samples — it does not destroy it.** A 300 s capture on a ~2 s beat ≈ **150 samples**, ~10 emit cycles × ~3–4 samples inside each 7 s window ⇒ **~35 expected `nbrs=1` samples if reception works.** ⇒ **ZERO of ~150 when ~35 are expected is DECISIVE, not ambiguous.** *"A single occurrence is a PASS"* is right **as a pass rule**; the blanket no-negative-conclusion is too strong **for the `nbrs` channel**. **What remains genuinely ambiguous is `LORA-BEACON`, and for the CRC reason, not the TTL one — keep them separate or the strongest negative signal on the run gets discarded alongside the weak one.**
>   - **SCORING, PER BOARD, NEVER SUMMED:** `LORA-BEACON` non-zero ⇒ **RX works, phase-lock causal, done** · `nbrs=1` at all ⇒ **PASS** · `nbrs=0` across all ~150 samples ⇒ **STRONG NEGATIVE (≠ proof)** · `LORA-BEACON`=0 alone ⇒ **AMBIGUOUS (CRC invisible)** · **circuits stays down until `preamble==0` is MEASURED.**
> - **🔬🔴 #110 INSTRUMENT — CRC COUNTERS ALONE FAIL TOWARD THE SCHEMATIC. THE DISCRIMINATOR IS `PreambleDetected`, AND IT IS THE ONE IRQ NOT ARMED (task #104, 2026-07-20).**
>   - **core's CLAIMS ALL VERIFIED AT `a26119f6`:** `main.rs:5011` is the **only** crc-err print and sits in `lora_task` (`not(loraroute)`) ⇒ **never runs**; `lora_transport.rs:336` merges `RxTimeout | CrcError`, re-arms, returns `None`, **zero rx error counters in the file**. ⇒ **a CRC error is genuinely invisible in the flashed build, and our zero-`LORA-BEACON` null cannot distinguish DEAF from HEARD-AND-CORRUPTED.**
>   - **★★ BUT core's DISCRIMINATOR HAS A HOLE THAT ROUTES TO circuits ANYWAY.** It states *"crc==0 AND timeout==0 ⇒ genuinely deaf ⇒ circuits"*. **Aborting an RX by issuing `SET_TX` is NOT an RF error** — the radio is *commanded* out of receive, so there is nothing to CRC. **No `CrcError`, no `RxTimeout`, NO EVENT AT ALL.** ⇒ **core's own TX-preempts-RX defect produces `crc==0 AND timeout==0`, identical to genuine deafness** — the counters read "clean" and send circuits after an antenna **on the exact null we just proved cannot distinguish the two.** *(It also splits core's unification: first light's SF12 partial-catch DID produce CRC errors — a reception that completed badly; tonight's self-pre-emption produces SILENCE. Same class, different observable. **The synthesis survives; the instrument for it does not.**)*
>   - **★★★ `PreambleDetected` IS THE DISCRIMINATOR AND IT IS UNARMED.** `crates/r2-sx1262/src/lib.rs:114` — `ALL = TX_DONE | RX_DONE | TIMEOUT | CRC_ERR`; **`PREAMBLE_DETECTED (1<<4)` is absent.** `:560` verbatim: *"so RxDone is the correct wake-and-drain signal (**PreambleDetected is NOT armed** — see docs)."* **That decision is in my own `RESUME.md:2014` and I agreed to it.** RxDone-wake is sufficient to **DRAIN**, not to **DIAGNOSE** — it can only report receptions that *completed*, so every upstream failure collapses into one undifferentiated silence.
>   - **ARMED, FOUR STATES SEPARATE IN ONE RUN:** `preamble>0, rxdone>0` ⇒ **RX works**, problem is downstream · `preamble>0, rxdone==0, crc>0` ⇒ **heard, corrupted** (SF12/RF partial catch, first light's mechanism) · `preamble>0, rxdone==0, crc==0` ⇒ **heard, ABANDONED** (TX-preempts-RX — **core's and mine, NOT circuits'**) · `preamble==0` ⇒ **genuinely deaf** ⇒ **now, and only now, circuits.** **crc/timeout alone cannot separate rows 3 and 4 — the two that decide whose problem it is.**
>   - **★ PRE-REGISTERED SO THE RUN CAN REFUTE ME:** under phase-lock at the measured 1.114 s the boards are **NOT symmetric** — the board transmitting **first** is blocked at preamble (`preamble==0`), the board transmitting **second** detects then self-pre-empts (`preamble>0, rxdone==0`). **An asymmetric per-board reading confirms the two-mechanism model; a symmetric one refutes it. Counters MUST be read PER BOARD, never summed.**
>   - **core's SF CANON POINT ACCEPTED — IT CORRECTS MY FRAMING.** I wrote *"a one-constant change, not a schematic hunt"*: true of the **diagnostic**, but it invites reading as a **remedy**, and **a per-code-path SF override of the SF12 region profile is FORBIDDEN (deaf-node anti-pattern)** with **§3.1 single-SF making any SF change MESH-scoped**. `benchsf7`'s own comment self-scopes: *"SF12 stays FIELD canon (range); benchsf7 is bench-config ONLY."* **Diagnostic on two isolated boards ≠ field remedy.**
>   - **THIRD CROSS-BRANCH DIVERGENCE (core's, verified by me):** `leaf_as923_nz`/`relay_as923_nz` — **2 definitions on the fw branch, 0 consumers, deleted on the canonical branch as a forbidden anti-pattern.** **`dfr1195-fw` IS AN OLDER CANON.** Not live; core's to merge forward.
>   - **core's REAL FINDING, sharpened:** four silent losses in one crate — `tx_overflow` unwired, `tx_hi_overflow` absent, beacon admission absent, RX errors uncounted. **A layer with no loss accounting on either side** — and **no ATTEMPT accounting on the RX side either: you cannot count losses against a denominator you never recorded.**
> - **🧮 #110 FIX SIZING — PER-EMISSION JITTER IS THE RIGHT MECHANISM (core's, I withdraw my per-board period), BUT THE PROCESS IS DIFFUSIVE AND core's COUNTS ARE LINEAR (2026-07-20).**
>   - **core's BIRTHDAY CRITIQUE OF MY GRID — RE-COMPUTED FROM SCRATCH, ALL FOUR EXACT:** 16 slots ⇒ P(some pair shares) **N=2 6.2% · N=4 33.3% · N=9 94.0% · N=12 99.7%.** A shared slot is `delta = 0` ⇒ a permanently locked pair — **the exact failure the fix exists to remove**, near-certain at Roy's 9- and 12-board roadmap. And **widening the grid does not escape it**: more slots ⇒ finer spacing ⇒ smaller `delta` ⇒ slower self-heal. **CONCEDED — per-board period is a 2-board fix and it was mine.** core's Occam point also lands: the `% 60` post-send re-draw at `:5284` **is already per-emission**, so the mechanism is present and undersized **twice, in two places**.
>   - **★★ BUT THE RELATIVE PHASE RANDOM-WALKS, IT DOES NOT DRIFT.** Step per cycle = `U_A − U_B`, `U ~ Uniform(0,J)` ⇒ symmetric triangular, **mean ZERO**, `sigma = J/sqrt(6) ≈ 0.408 J`. **Mean zero is the whole point: there is no systematic drift to divide a distance by.** First passage over `d` scales as **`(d/sigma)²`, not `d/step`** — core divided by the mean step, which is the arithmetic for a **per-board PERIOD** (deterministic drift). **It carried the linear model over from the mechanism it was replacing.**
>   - **MEASURED (worst-case lock at offset ~0, must reach the 1647 ms band edge):** `J=±300ms` **core 11 cyc vs ACTUAL 181 cyc ≈ 90 MINUTES** · `±600` 5.5 vs **45 cyc ≈ 23 min** · `±1000` **3.3 vs 16 cyc ≈ 8 min** · `±1300` 2.5 vs **9.6 cyc ≈ 5 min**. **At core's ±300 ms figure a worst-case pair stays dark for an hour and a half.**
>   - **★ SIZING: ~10-cycle worst-case self-heal needs `sigma >= 521 ms` ⇒ `J >= ~1276 ms`. CALL IT J = 1.5 s.** *(Tonight's specific 1.114 s offset only needs 533 ms of travel — ~19 cycles at J=300 — **but size for the worst case, not for tonight's draw. Sizing against the observed instance is exactly how the 401 ms preamble figure went 4× small.**)*
>   - **core's ONE-SIDED CONSTRAINT IS THE BINDING ONE AND IT SURVIVES MY RESIZE:** `30_000 + 0..J`, **never** `30_000 − J` — a symmetric jitter shortens the instantaneous interval below 30 s and breaks **both** the airtime budget **and** the §8.1.4 MIN-interval floor. At `J=1.5 s` the mean period is 30.75 s ⇒ duty **~0.97×**, i.e. it **improves**. Both checks pass at the size I propose.
>   - **STEADY STATE IS core's, UNCHANGED:** long-run time-in-band ≈ `2×1647/30000` ≈ **11%/cycle, intermittent and self-healing**, invisible to a repeating 30 s discovery beacon. **My correction is to the TRANSIENT (escape time), not the steady state.**

> - **✅🔴 #110 — PHASE-LOCK MEASURED AND CONFIRMED; ROOT CAUSE IS THE FLASHING PROCEDURE. AND IT FAILS BY TWO DIFFERENT MECHANISMS, WHICH CHANGES HOW THE FIX MUST BE SIZED (2026-07-20).** supervisor's 300 s timestamped capture: intra-board period `30.07–30.11 s` on both; **cross-board offset mean `1.114 s`, spread `0.043 s` across 10 cycles (~5 min)** ⇒ **a LOCKED pair.** My predicted random-walk ceiling was ~0.45 s — measured wander came in an order of magnitude *inside* it, so the bound held as a bound. **Cause, plainly: the boards were flashed 30 s apart and the emit interval is 30 s. Reception was never broken.** `nbrs=0` predating `a26119f6` is consistent — the pre-fix boards were also flashed sequentially and also airtime-limited to ~1 TX/15 s. **The queue-starvation fix remains correct and measured (14/14, 0 dropped, 9.9%). Two faults, one symptom.**
>   - **★★ THE STATED MECHANISM EXPLAINS ONLY ONE DIRECTION.** With A at `t`, B at `t+1.114`: **A hears B ⇒ BLOCKED AT PREAMBLE** (B's preamble arrives at `t+1.114`; A is on air to `t+1.319`/`t+1.647`). But **B hears A ⇒ NOT blocked at all** — A's preamble arrives at `t` when B has been idle ~28.9 s, so **B detects it and starts receiving**, then at `t+1.114` **B's own scheduled TX clobbers the in-progress reception 205 ms before A's frame completes.** Verified rather than assumed: `crates/r2-sx1262/src/lib.rs fn transmit` does `clear_irq_status` / buffer / `set_payload_len` / `rxen.set_low()` / `SET_TX` with **no check for an in-progress RX**, and core's CAD grep returns **zero hits in both crates** ⇒ **no listen-before-talk anywhere. B PRE-EMPTS ITSELF.**
>   - **★★★ ⇒ SIZE THE DECORRELATION AGAINST THE FULL FRAME, NEVER THE PREAMBLE.** Preamble is 401 ms @SF12; **a fix sized against 401 ms STILL FAILS** — an 800 ms offset clears the preamble one way and still permits self-pre-emption the other. **Safe band: `offset > 1647 ms` (longest burst) AND `period − offset > 1647 ms`** ⇒ `(1.647 s, 28.353 s)`. **The measured 1.114 s is in the fail band, and so is anything below 1.647.**
>   - **★ core's DEGENERATE CASE IS WIDER THAN "EQUAL PERIODS" — NEARLY-EQUAL LOCK TOO.** Periods differing by `delta` walk the relative phase at `delta`/cycle, so traversing the 1647 ms band takes `1647/delta` cycles. **`hive_id % 3_000` on ADJACENT ids gives `delta = 1 ms` ⇒ ~13.7 HOURS LOCKED** — not 1-in-3000, **any near-neighbour pair.** Self-heal in ~10 cycles needs **`delta >= ~165 ms`.** A hash fixes *uniformity* but **not separation** — it can still emit two values 1 ms apart. **QUANTISE TO A COARSE GRID** (e.g. `30_000 + (hash(hive_id) % 16) * 200`) ⇒ `delta ∈ {200,400,…}` guaranteed. **DISTINCT IS NOT ENOUGH; SEPARATED IS THE REQUIREMENT.** *(core's budget check holds for the grid form: upward-only ⇒ duty only improves; a MIN-INTERVAL FLOOR stays §8.1.4-conformant when lengthened. MUST apply to BOTH emitters or the 30 s beacon collides every cycle.)*
>   - **CAD/LBT = the CLASS fix, not #110** (core's, spec-facing). **Note for the specs question: LBT and a duty-cycle regime are NOT independent** — a deferred transmission still owes its airtime debit, and a **class-blind** bucket cannot price a deferral.
>   - **SEQUENCE: stagger the resets ~15 s and re-run BEFORE any code.** The stagger **swamps** my flash-completion-vs-boot residual — making it moot rather than answered, which is the better outcome. **RX HAS STILL NEVER BEEN DEMONSTRATED ON THIS BENCH:** phase-lock explains the null **without proving reception is possible.** The stagger test is the first thing that could.
>   - **★ core RETRACTED ITS OWN REFUTATION BEFORE ANYONE ACTED — and supervisor had already acted**, tasking circuits on the closing conclusion, then stood them down. core's containment model was **correct arithmetic over a condition that does not govern** (containment, where the governing condition is preamble arrival). **A REFUTATION THAT CLOSES A LINE OF ENQUIRY DESERVES THE SAME SCRUTINY AS A FINDING THAT OPENS ONE** — and supervisor's addition is the sharper half: **a closing conclusion travels further and faster than an opening one, because it ENDS work rather than creating it. That is a property of the RELAY, not of core.**
> - **(superseded framing, kept for the evidence) 🔴🔴 #110 — PHASE-LOCK AS A MEASURED MECHANISM. AND BOTH PROPOSED REMEDIES ARE WRONG, INCLUDING MINE (2026-07-20).** supervisor's espflash stamps: **`23:02:22Z` / `23:02:52Z` = 30 s apart**, both emit intervals **`30_000 ms`** ⇒ **`delta mod period = 0` EXACTLY.** Not an unlucky draw — **an alignment MANUFACTURED BY THE FLASHING PROCEDURE.** With both timers boot-anchored (`:5224`, `:6398`) and the ~0.45 s random walk unable to escape a 1319–1647 ms burst, **overlap persists the whole run and `0/28` is exactly predicted.** core's ~20% prior is superseded by a measurement — the offset was never a random variable.
>   - **★★ MY OWN "WIDEN THE RANGE" ADVICE WAS HALF WRONG AND I CORRECTED IT BEFORE IT LANDED** (supervisor had already relayed it to core as load-bearing). The spread at `:5219` is drawn **ONCE AT BOOT AND NEVER REDRAWN** — a one-shot offset, however wide, **only re-rolls the dice**: uniform over the 30 s period against a `2 × 2966 ms` band leaves **~19.8% chance of a PERMANENTLY DEAF PAIR.** Same bug class, lower probability, **silent and intermittent across bring-ups — harder to diagnose than tonight's reproducible failure.**
>   - **★★ AND core's PRIME-RATIO OPTION DE-CORRELATES THE WRONG PAIR.** `data 31 s / beacon 30 s` de-phases **a board's own two emitters**; it does **NOT** de-phase **board A vs board B**, because identical images run identical constants and the A-vs-B relative phase stays fixed whatever the ratio. *(It would help tonight only BY ACCIDENT — `delta` 30 s mod a 31 s data period ≈ the far end, so data de-collides while the 30 s **beacon still collides every cycle**.)*
>   - **⇒ THE AXIS IS BOARD-vs-BOARD, AND NEITHER OPTION ADDRESSES IT. VARY THE PERIOD PER BOARD, NOT THE OFFSET** — e.g. `30_000 + (hive_id % 3_000)` ms. Different **periods** make the relative phase **WALK**, turning ~20% chance of *permanent* deafness into **~20% loss per cycle that SELF-HEALS**. **An offset moves WHERE a fixed phase sits; only a period makes it MOVE.** Keeps R2-LORA §6.5.2 satisfied. **core's crate, core's call — stated as a design point, not a patch.**
>   - **RESIDUAL I AM NOT PAPERING OVER:** espflash stamps are **flash COMPLETION, not BOOT**. Reset→boot latency would have to differ by >~1.3 s to break alignment — implausible on identical images, **but inferred, not measured.** 1 s stamp resolution is fine against a >1 s burst.
>   - **★ THE CONFIRMING TEST IS STILL OWED: A MECHANISM THAT FITS IS NOT A DEMONSTRATED CAUSE.** Phase-lock explains `0/28` **without proving reception is possible.** **Stagger the two resets by a non-harmonic offset (~15 s) and re-run** — receptions ⇒ CONFIRMED; still 0 ⇒ true-but-not-causal and the field is PHY/RX-chain. Two resets, no code.
>   - **RECIPE, BANKED — [[sequential-flashing-phase-aligns-boards]]:** **flashing N boards sequentially can PHASE-ALIGN them** whenever per-board flash time is near a multiple of a protocol interval. **A property of the PROCEDURE, not the firmware**, so it recurs on every multi-board bring-up and no code review finds it. Record flash-completion stamps; stagger resets non-harmonically before any discovery test. *(Second recipe item tonight, after the ~70 s reservoir rule.)*
>   - **core's SELF-CORRECTION I WOULD HAVE MISSED:** *"a fixed unlucky offset IS random phase — I refuted a strawman of my own construction and then cited it as support."* Treating a fixed parameter as an i.i.d. draw. **I accepted its 0/28-refutes-random-phase arithmetic without checking the sample space**, so it got past me too.
> - **(earlier framing, superseded above) 🔬 #110 RX — core's PHASE-LOCK HYPOTHESIS (task #102, 2026-07-20).** Capture: `lora_btx` 14/14 both boards, `bdr` 0, `dr` 0, airtime 9.9% vs 10% modelled, **`LORA-BEACON` heard = 0 and `nbrs` = 0 on both** ⇒ TX proven both sides, **nothing received at all**. One fault upstream of roster, verification and `seen`.
>   - **★ core's PROPOSED REMEDY IS ALREADY IMPLEMENTED — DO NOT RE-ADD IT.** `:5214-5219` seeds an LCG from `my_hive ^ 0x9E37_79B9` and draws `((lcg >> 22) % 200)` = **0..1 s first-TX spread**, citing **R2-LORA §6.5.2 (MUST)** — de-correlate the mains-restore cohort. **A per-board `hive_id`-seeded phase offset is present, deliberate and spec-cited. It is UNDERSIZED by ~an order of magnitude against a 1319–1647 ms burst.** The fix is to **widen the range**, not add a mechanism. *(Cite correction for core: the `% 60` 0..300 ms at `:5284` is the POST-SEND re-draw; the first-TX spread at `:5219` is `% 200`.)*
>   - **THE REFUTATION I RAN, WHICH FAILED — so it strengthens core:** the post-send backoff random-walks the two boards apart by only `~sqrt(14) x sigma`, `sigma`(uniform-difference 0..300 ms) ≈ 122 ms ⇒ **~0.45 s over 14 emissions. That cannot escape a 1319–1647 ms burst**, so **a lock, once established, persists for the whole run by arithmetic.** Crystal drift ~20 ppm over 420 s ≈ 8 ms — also negligible.
>   - **⚠ BUT THE LOAD-BEARING PREMISE IS UNMEASURED:** core assumes *near-simultaneous boot*. **espflash on a 1,359,420 B image is not instantaneous and the boards were written SEQUENTIALLY**, so the boot offset is plausibly **minutes** and `delta mod 30_000` is effectively **arbitrary**. Both timers seed from boot — `last_beacon_ms = 0` (`:5224`, so the first beacon waits a full 30 s) and the apiary path short-circuits on `last_emit_ms != 0` (`:6398`, so **data fires on the first tick**). Under a common delta both schedules shift **together**, so lock needs `delta mod 30_000 ≈ 0` within ~1.3 s, **and nothing in the code aligns them.** ⇒ **MUST NOT be recorded as structural before core's `ENQUEUED`-timestamp grep. If it DOES show lock, the alignment itself is the finding.**
>   - **ELIMINATED:** `lora.service(now_ms)` (`:5295`) is called **unconditionally every tick**, outside the `tx_backoff` branch ⇒ the RX drain runs every iteration regardless of TX state. *(Earlier eliminations: `standby` ∉ closure, RXEN polarity, `listen()` armed in the constructor, `can_hear_hive`, SF/freq — and **core's is stronger than mine on `can_hear_hive`: I read the BODY and called it hear-all; core read the CALLERS and found it DEAD.** Body-correct and never-invoked are different facts.)*
>   - **core's LATENT, adopted:** `lora_transport.rs:323-345` — **`RxDone` is the only match arm that does not call `arm_rx`.** Safe today **only because the driver chose `RX_CONTINUOUS`** ⇒ **a layer whose correctness depends on a constant it never names.** Same silent-cross-layer shape as the vendored-vs-live trap. Not tonight's cause; core's, post-flash.
> - **⛔ RETRACTED — `nbrs` IS *NOT* ROSTER-GATED. core REFUTED THIS AND I VERIFIED THE REFUTATION AT SOURCE (2026-07-20).** `:1757 NBRS.store(live)` where `live` = `seen` filtered by TTL (`:1753-1756`), and **`seen` has EXACTLY TWO writers, both `:2046`/`:2049`, keyed on `sender_hive` inside the `couple_ok` VERIFIED branch — no roster, no `resolve_rbid_windowed`, no beacon.** The unverified branch at `:2052+` calls `ingest_observation` but **does NOT touch `seen`**, so an unverified peer raises the route table and never raises `nbrs`. **Two structures, two gates — and I conflated them.** ⇒ `nbrs` is a **live end-to-end observable**; recording it as retired would have hidden a real failure behind a gate that does not sit on that path. **core's stated precondition ANSWERED:** both boards unprovisioned ⇒ `:354 None => (TG_HK_DEMO, …)`, a compile-time constant in a byte-identical image ⇒ **both derive the SAME `hk`**, so verification cannot fail for key-mismatch reasons. **★ LEDGER, CORRECTED BY core AND supervisor — I OVER-CONCEDED AND THE OVER-CONCESSION WAS ITSELF THE DEFECT.** I first wrote this up as *"nbrs was the wrong observable, my design error"*. **FALSE.** supervisor attached its roster finding to a counter on a different path and I absorbed a charge built on that broken link — **the second over-concession in three messages, a failure mode I had named myself.** core's separation is the one to keep, and it is sharper than mine: **A CORRECT CHOICE MADE WITHOUT THE TRACE IS AN UNEARNED CORRECT ANSWER, NOT AN ERROR — different entries in the ledger.** (My own [[grow-strong-ideas-method]] already says a right answer for a wrong reason is a liability; it does not say it is a defect.) **WHAT STANDS:** the rule — *an observable MUST be traced to its preconditions before it is proposed as an acceptance criterion* — and the narrow fact that **I did not trace it**. **WHAT IS RETRACTED:** that the choice was wrong. **An over-concession puts a false defect in the record**, and a hollow reason discounts the reasons that do hold. **WHAT SURVIVES BELOW IS THE ROSTER GATE ITSELF — real, type-level, and it gates RELAY VIABILITY plus the §4.4 cross-mode gate at `r2-core crates/r2-route/src/engine.rs:919/:982`, NEITHER of which is `nbrs`. Roy has DEFERRED it.**
> - **(superseded framing, kept for the evidence) 🔴 THE ROSTER GATE (task #101, 2026-07-20).** core went looking to falsify its own fix and found the precondition; supervisor measured it; **I ran the attack that would have refuted it and it held.**
>   - **THE ATTACK (a const enumeration is only sound if nothing populates the registry at runtime):** `beacon_registry` has **exactly two refs** — built `:5231`, read `:5319`. **No NVS path, no provisioning path, no runtime insert.** ⇒ the const enumeration IS the whole population.
>   - **STRUCTURAL, NOT BAD LUCK:** `:349` masks `mac_low3` with `0x00FF_FFFF` ⇒ **an unprovisioned `hive_id` ALWAYS has a `0x00` high byte, by construction.** No roster entry has one ⇒ **the roster holds provisioned HKDF-derived ids ONLY and cannot match ANY unprovisioned board.** Adding these two ids fixes these two boards and leaves the next one equally invisible.
>   - **MEMBERSHIP CORRECTION to supervisor's enumeration — the roster is 4 slots, not 6.** `:4166 KNOWN_HIVE_IDS = [FR4_SENSOR_HIVE, 0x2cab_5f69, FR4_RECV_HIVE, 0x0dca_dbf8]`; **`FR4_ROUTER_HIVE` and `FR4_BRIDGE_HIVE` are never referenced by the registry.** Actual set: `not(labrig)` `0x480e_900e·0x2cab_5f69·0x06ae_082b·0x0dca_dbf8`; `labrig` `0x998d_e7fc·0x2cab_5f69·0x2c81_b4a3·0x0dca_dbf8`. **High bytes `0x48/0x2c/0x06/0x0d` and `0x99/0x2c/0x2c/0x0d` — none is `0x00`, so the verdict holds on the corrected set.** *(Latent: `0x2cab_5f69` is a literal equal to `not(labrig)` `FR4_ROUTER_HIVE`, so a `labrig` build carries a `not(labrig)` D2 id.)*
>   - **`hk` IS NOT THE BLOCKER:** both boards unprovisioned ⇒ both on `TG_HK_DEMO` ⇒ `derive_beacon_session_key(&hk, h)` agrees. **The `hive_id` is the sole mismatch.**
>   - **THE FAILURE IS SILENT:** `if let Some(hive)` at `:5319` has **no else arm**, so a heard-but-unresolved beacon still prints `LORA-BEACON rbid=` at `:5306` and forms no neighbour. **The log line looks like success, and `nbrs=0` reads as "the queue fix failed" — the exact symptom we started from.**
>   - **★★ THIS ONE IS MINE AND I AM NOT TAKING THE OFFERED EXCUSE.** Supervisor wrote *"not a design error — the gate is 800 lines away from the counter"*. **It is a design error.** I chose `nbrs` as the zero-console observable because it was **visible on the LCD**, and never traced what gates it — `resolve_rbid_windowed` is named at the call site I would have had to read. **AN OBSERVABLE MUST BE TRACED TO ITS PRECONDITIONS BEFORE IT IS PROPOSED AS AN ACCEPTANCE CRITERION.** Same defect I caught four times in others' code tonight and once in my own. **Had core's falsification arrived AFTER the capture, we would have re-opened a closed defect and chased the queue again.**
>   - **RE-ANCHORING VERIFIED, NOT ASSUMED:** `:5291 LORA_BEACON_TX.store(lora.tx_hi_admitted())` and `:5290 LORA_TX_DROPPED.store(lora.tx_overflow())` read **straight off the LoRaTransport in the TX path — no roster, no resolver, no registry.** ⇒ roster-independent, and they measure the thing that was actually fixed.

Positive control: grep count 4 = 3 callers + the definition, same grep. ⇒ **the branch and its `NEG-REFUSE cross-mode peer` println are dead code.** And the doc comment at `:4718` asserts the **opposite**, verbatim: *"Undeclared cannot occur at this boundary: an observed beacon IS a declaration (absent byte decodes 0x00 = prod), so plain equality on from_wire(BUILD_CLASS) is the whole gate."* **The comment describes a design; the call sites implement its negation.**

> - **⚠ SUPERVISOR'S GH #19 CORRECTION IS RIGHT IN SUBSTANCE, WRONG IN MECHANISM — and the mechanism is the part Roy needs.** #19's banner claims *"all boards … are in dev mode, reporting that with their beacons as required"*. Measured: `:4913` `if BUILD_CLASS == 2 { buf[16] = BUILD_CLASS; 17 } else { 16 }`, whose own comment reads *"a PROD build emits at most 16 bytes — **zero dev bytes on air**"*; `:4952` decodes `Some(p[16])` only at len 17, else `None`; `:5321` `let bclass = _build_class.unwrap_or(0); // absence = prod (R2-BUILDMODE §2)`. ⇒ **THE PROD BEACON DOES NOT DECLARE ANYTHING — it carries no build-mode byte at all. The RECEIVER infers prod from ABSENCE.** So #19's row is not merely false-in-value: **there is NO EMITTER for it in a prod build.** The correction to Roy should read *"no dev bytes are emitted; prod is inferred from absence"*, **not** *"the beacon declares prod"*. **Spec-level consequence, flagged as a question not a bug: absence-as-declaration makes a TRUNCATED beacon and a PROD board indistinguishable on air** (R2-BUILDMODE §2).
> - **CORE'S SECOND BEACON EMITTER — verified NOT LIVE here, and the inverse trace is a genuinely new instrument.** `build_lora_beacon` has **two** call sites: `:5259` (mine, via `send_class(Discovery)`) and **`:5018` inside `lora_task`, which calls `radio.transmit(pl)` DIRECTLY on the Sx1262** — no `LoRaTransport`, no `AirtimeBucket`, no queue, no class, **debits nothing**. `:854-856` spawns `lora_route_task` under `loraroute` and `lora_task` under `not(loraroute)` — **mutually exclusive**, and `loraroute` ∈ `closure(fakesensor)` ⇒ **the flashed image has exactly one beacon emitter and it is the prioritised one.** `lora_task` is still **compiled** (gated on `lora`, which `loraroute` pulls) — **which is exactly why `nm` could never have settled this: BOTH paths are linked.** **LATENT, core's, post-flash:** any build *without* `loraroute` emits 1319 ms SF12 frames on a 100 ms poll loop with **zero duty accounting** — that breaches R2-LORA §4.2/§4.3 outright rather than starving something.

> - **★★★ THE TIER DISCRIMINATOR IS *SPENT*, NOT *ABSENT* — and it REFUTES core's proposed §5.1 re-grounding before it reaches canon. VERIFIED AT SOURCE, banked as [[tier-discriminator-is-spent-not-absent]].**
>   - **CORE'S CLAIMS — ALL VERIFIED EXACTLY (not banked):** `R2-LORA.md:349` **verbatim** — *"**Beacon-vs-data demux on the shared LoRa carrier (MUST).** A receiver distinguishes an R2-BEACON §8.1.1 LoRa beacon from a data frame by **content + length**, NOT a carrier prefix: a beacon is the {15,16,17}-byte form with `magic = 0xB2` at offset 0."* · `types.rs:124` `return Err(WireError::InvalidVersion)` with `decode_byte0` requiring `ver == 0` · `0xB2 >> 6 = 2` ⇒ **a beacon CANNOT mint a `CompactFrame`** ⇒ **core's own `Frame = CompactFrame` would have made discovery UNSENDABLE — they caught it themselves, the first self-catch of the day.** · `r2-transport/src/transport.rs:248` `fn send(&self, target: u32, frame: &[u8]) -> Result<(), SendError>` — **untyped bytes, generic, 5+ impls ⇒ core-owned.**
>   - **★★ THEIR SPEC ARGUMENT UNDERSTATES ITSELF.** Core: *"canon knows how to do in-band demux, it just NEVER GAVE compact/extended one."* **VERIFIED SHARPER — canon GAVE them one and SPENT IT ON THE SAME VALUE TWICE:** `compact.rs:54` and `extended.rs:50` are **THE SAME CALL** — `buf[0] = encode_byte0(h.version, h.msg_type, h.flags)`. `decode_byte0` rejects `ver != 0` ⇒ **3 of 4 version values (1,2,3) UNUSED.** And **the beacon demux works PRECISELY BECAUSE the beacon uses ver=2** — it is discriminable **by the very field the two tiers left identical.** ⇒ **THE DISCRIMINATOR IS PRESENT, 2 BITS WIDE, 3 OF 4 VALUES FREE, AND BOTH TIERS WERE ASSIGNED ver=0.** `§4.3.5:453`'s *"detection by transport context"* is a workaround for a **SOLVED** problem left unsolved in one place.
>   - **★★★ ⇒ THIS REFUTES CORE'S RE-GROUNDING AS WORDED.** *"No in-band discriminator ⇒ mixed tiers are **STRUCTURALLY** undecodable — binds on EVERY profile"* is **FALSE.** They are undecodable **BY CHOICE**, one spent value away from decodable. **Same over-claim shape as core's other four** (prose-as-proof → proxy-as-boundary → architecture-as-mitigation → proxy-as-boundary-in-a-type → **structural-from-current-state**) — *"count is now five, one shape"* — **and this one would have gone into CANON.** ⇒ **A rule needs a ground that is TRUE, not merely CURRENTLY TRUE**: a re-grounding on "structurally impossible" gets refuted **the day someone reads `types.rs`**, and then the MUST NOT has lost its **SECOND** ground in a week (the MTU one is already dead on benchsf7).
>   - **THE HONEST GROUND (still core's): mixed tiers are undecodable BECAUSE BOTH FORMATS WERE ASSIGNED ver=0** — contingent, fixable, **and the fix converts a MIS-PARSE into a clean `Err`**, which is the property core actually cares about: **today** an extended frame on LoRa **passes** `decode_byte0` (ver=0 ✓) then garbages; **at ver=1, TODAY'S UNMODIFIED DECODER returns `InvalidVersion` — it FAILS CLOSED.** ⚠ **I did NOT prescribe ver=1** — core's crate, and the cost is real: `version` is a **protocol version**, so tier-tagging it spends version space (2 bits = 4 values) and makes tier×version a product; a free **flag bit** may be better (`b & 0x07`) — **unverified, and not mine to design.** **My only claim: "structurally undecodable" is NOT AVAILABLE AS A PREMISE.**
>   - **★ AND IT RE-AIMS THE HATCH KILL (strengthening it):** with a discriminator the SF9 hatch becomes **SOUND** — a named profile *could* carry extended if receivers could tell. ⇒ **kill it not as "unsound forever" but as "unsound AS WRITTEN: it grants a PHY PROFILE where a WIRE DISCRIMINATOR is required, and prices that wire change at ZERO."** **My mispricing argument survives intact; core's unsoundness argument becomes CONDITIONAL on the byte0 assignment.**
>   - **CORE'S SELF-REFUTATION IS RIGHT AND THE SUM TYPE IS THE ANSWER: `LoRaTransport::Frame = LoRaFrame { Data(CompactFrame), Beacon(BeaconFrame) }`** — it closes **all three senders at the REAL edge** (which the queue newtype structurally cannot) and **encodes `:349`'s beacon-demux MUST in the type.** **Safe precisely because `:349` HAS a real discriminator — the type REFLECTS an invariant canon states correctly. The tier arm does NOT have that. Do the sum; don't let it pretend the tier arm is as well-grounded as the beacon arm.** Trait change is **ruling-independent**; only the per-bearer `Frame` **bindings** await specs (WiFi/IP's binding is exactly where `§4.3.5:463`'s verbatim-forward exception lands). **Core-sequenced: specs re-grounding → design + heads-up to me and composer → land. NOT before Roy's slot — and note it breaks me INSTANTLY even unpushed (I path-dep core's checkout, see [[shared-checkout-path-dep-coupling]]).**

> - **★★ CORE'S GENERALISATION — the most valuable output of the day, and bigger than LoRa: "A PHYSICAL LIMIT IS NOT A CONFORMANCE CHECK — it only HIDES the violation on the profile where the limit binds."** Review question for specs: **WHICH OF OUR MUSTs ARE ONLY "ENFORCED" BY A LIMIT SOME FUTURE PROFILE REMOVES?** Wherever a spec MUST coincides with a physical constraint, **the MUST is UNTESTED** — and the day someone widens the constraint (a bench profile, a faster PHY, a bigger MTU) the violation ships silently. **MY COROLLARY:** the constraint is often removed by the SAFEST-LOOKING change — `benchsf7` exists purely to make the demo fast, and it is what unmasked a 7-day-old canon violation. **A convenience knob removed an accidental safety property nobody knew they were relying on.** Routed to specs.

> - **★ WHY IT'S LIVE ON THE BENCH BUT INVISIBLE IN THE FIELD (core's catch, and it's sharp):** a SIGNED extended frame is 22B hdr + 32B HMAC = **54B floor > the 51B SF12/BW125 control-profile MTU**, and §5.2 rejects over-MTU **with no fragmentation** => on the FIELD SF12 profile a signed extended frame is **physically un-transmittable** and the bug can never show. **The demo runs benchsf7 (SF7/BW125 = 222B MTU) — which is EXACTLY what makes the non-conformant leg emittable. The bench profile is the unmasker.** My io_task LoRa emissions are a MIX: **4 signed** (sign_extended -> encode_extended -> mesh_broadcast) + **2 forward/relay re-encodes**. HAZARD (why it's worse than a dropped frame): a Compact-mode RAK does NOT cleanly Err on extended — extended byte0 is structurally decodable (same ver|type|flags packing) => decode_compact MIS-PARSES it, and with core's #2 (any heard frame forms a LINK) it would form a neighbour under a **GARBAGE hive_id**, then relay-opaque re-broadcast garbage (TTL/dedup-bounded, but pollutes the table + burns airtime). There is NO reliable in-band discriminator — which is precisely WHY canon makes the bearer single-tier.

Only other XIAO TX = phone->LoRa ingress (only if the phone sends). => even WITH core's #2, the RAK's ONLY neighbour is D4 = the SOURCE, which F2 excludes from the flood => build_flood_plan empty hop set => NoViableNeighbour => relay_on=0. **#2+#3 are necessary but NOT sufficient unless #3's egress policy re-broadcasts same-medium WITHOUT requiring a neighbour ENTRY** (which is core's own insight: on a broadcast medium a flood IS a same-medium re-TX). > **▶ RE-PASS ROUND 2 (2026-07-16) — hive-codex read-only re-pass of the amended commit returned 3 findings; all triaged, NO PUSH.**
> - **F1 (HIGH, CI blocker) — first fix was itself fail-OPEN; SUPERSEDED by round 4 (see below).** The
>   `m=$(grep … | … | sort)` substitutions abort the docs step under Actions' `bash -e -o pipefail` when a
>   grep matches NOTHING (clean) or all matches are allowlisted. My round-2 fix wrapped the WHOLE pipeline in
>   `|| true` — which ALSO swallowed a scanner CRASH (rc>1: bad pattern, missing grep) and mapped it to a clean
>   result. hive-codex round-4 caught that as a NEW fail-open. Correct fix is in round 4: a `scan()` helper that
>   treats grep rc 0/1 as success but PROPAGATES rc>1 (fail-closed), with `|| true` on ONLY the allowlist filter.
> - **F3 (MED, test weakness) — DONE.** `kat()` now accepts optional `reason` ([MAC]/[TAIL]/[TAIL-0x]/[TAIL-COMPACT]) and exact `count`; high-value KATs assert them so a wrong-CLASSIFIER regression (MAC misread as TAIL, or the 4-group run's 2-window count) can no longer stay green on a bare flag/no-flag check. Selftest **41/41** with the stricter asserts.
> - **F2 (MED, false-positives) — VERIFIED, one sub-claim REFUTED, narrowing DEFERRED as a Roy-canon tradeoff.**
>   (Examples described abstractly here on purpose — writing the literal token beside a context word would trip
>   this very gate on RESUME.md; see the self-inflicted-trap note in memory.) Confirmed latent FPs, all currently
>   ABSENT from the tree: a time-of-day triple or a short two-digit-group date sitting beside a board/device word
>   classifies as a TAIL; a six-digit baud constant beside a board-id label classifies as a compact tail; a
>   revision-like six-hex filename segment can too. REFUTED: ISO-date *filenames* with a four-digit year do NOT
>   flag — the hex negative-lookbehind already blocks them (the year's last digit is hex before the date run).
>   Decision: the gate is fail-SAFE by design (errs toward flagging, exact-allowlist escape hatch); every F2 fix
>   narrows CONTEXT = the fail-OPEN direction that burned this workstream twice, and the real tree is currently
>   clean (exit 0). Not narrowing unilaterally; routed to hive-codex/supervisor as a noise-vs-fail-open tradeoff on
>   Roy-canon context rules. **Do-not-assume:** narrowing the tail-context set to quiet F2 without KATs proving no
>   new fail-open is the exact regression class this branch exists to kill.

> **▶ RE-PASS ROUND 4 (2026-07-16) — hive-codex refuted my OWN round-2/3 fixes; both were real. FIXED. NO PUSH.**
> - **docs F1 fail-OPEN (HIGH) — properly FIXED.** The round-2 blanket `|| true` mapped a scanner CRASH (grep
>   rc>1: missing binary, invalid pattern, unreadable tree) to the same empty/clean result as a legit no-match —
>   fail-open. Replaced with a `scan()` helper: grep rc 0/1 = success (emit matches, empty on no-match), rc>1
>   PROPAGATES so `set -e` aborts = fail-CLOSED; `|| true` now wraps ONLY the allowlist filter (its rc1 = all
>   placeholders, never a tool failure). Verified end-to-end incl. the decisive case: a broken grep (rc2) now
>   makes the step EXIT 2 (fail-closed), not exit-0-clean. Clean→0, planted MAC→1, allowlisted-only→0 all hold.
> - **kat() crash-suppression (MED) — FIXED.** `kat()` used `hygiene_scan || true`, so a scanner crash on a
>   VALID must-pass fixture false-passed. Now captures the scanner status (`&& src=0 || src=$?`) and FAILs the
>   KAT on any non-zero on valid input; the malformed-stream crash path is checked separately. Proved with an
>   injected `hygiene_scan(){ return 3; }` — kat() reports FAIL (old code printed ok). Selftest **43/43**.
> - **merge-legitimate-fragments precision (noise, NOT fail-open) — documented tradeoff.** A timestamp+segment
>   like a time triple joined by a separator to another triple normalises to six pairs and flags [MAC]; spaced
>   fragments pass. Inherently ambiguous; under the fail-SAFE policy this is a noise tradeoff, not a hole. Policy:
>   keep flagging (fail-safe); if a real doc trips it, use a `T`/space separator or an exact allowlist entry.
>
> **▶ RE-PASS ROUND 5 (2026-07-16) — hive-codex found my round-4 fix STILL had two fail-opens. FIXED. NO PUSH.**
> - **docs allowlist filter fail-OPEN (HIGH) — FIXED.** Round 4 fixed the primary `scan()` grep but left the
>   allowlist step as `{ grep -vixE … || true; }`. That `|| true` ALSO swallowed a filter tool failure (rc>1): if
>   the allowlist grep errored while upstream emitted a REAL MAC, the leak was erased and the pipeline read clean.
>   Reproduced. Fixed with an `allow_filter` helper (same rc discipline as `scan`): rc0/1 = success, rc>1 propagates
>   = fail-CLOSED. Verified: allowlist-grep rc2 + upstream real MAC now EXITS NONZERO, not clean.
> - **end-to-end KATs discarded exit status (MED) — FIXED.** The `hygiene_scan_tree` KATs used `[ -n "$(…)" ]` /
>   `[ -z … ]`, which drop the command-substitution status, so a scanner crash that emitted a finding (or emitted
>   nothing) false-passed. Replaced with an `e2e MODE NAME` helper that captures output AND status separately:
>   flag = findings+rc0, clean = empty+rc0, failclosed = rc≠0. The empty-tree KAT is the one explicit rc≠0 case.
> - RESUME durable line corrected (no longer claims blanket `|| true`); strongest temp-repo mixed-EUI/mixed-separator
>   replay recorded PASS (both mixed orders + mixed EUI-64 + underscore/-if00 path form all flag [MAC] end-to-end;
>   allowlisted placeholder passes). F4/Pages branch stays HELD (supervisor-codex: publication policy, not a hygiene

## 🔬 XIAO BENCH decode-support (android, 2026-07-12) — golden frames handed + board-health cleared (commit 95d5148)
android hit two things decoding the XIAO USB egress: (1) InvalidRouteLen on live captures, (2) the stream went QUIET.
**Both answered via fleet send + persisted to docs/BENCH-BOARD-FACTS.md.** (1) ROOT CAUSE = capture drop, NOT a
decoder bug: `dd bs=1` byte-drops the egress (27–30B vs true fixed 31B); byte0=0x06 sets has_route, so ONE dropped
byte reads data[12] as rlen=0x00 = InvalidRouteLen exactly. Handed a byte-exact GOLDEN frame from canonical
`r2_wire::encode_compact` (round-trips decode_compact): compact 31B = `0653000164cedbf305fe0701011234a10018eaa101182a0102030405060708`;
R2-USB DATA record 33B = `1f00…` (1f00 = payload_len 31 LE). Emitter LANDED = `crates/r2-hive-bin/examples/gen_golden_compact_frame.rs`
(regen: `cargo run -p r2-hive --example gen_golden_compact_frame`). 0xA1 sighting golden already byte-exact in
dfr1195 `USB-BEACON-SIGHTING-FORMAT.md` KAT. (2) QUIET = peer-silence (egress is PURE forwarded LoRa RX, NO
keepalive); board still enumerated at same MAC = NOT in ROM download mode; forward-task can't wedge on a DTR toggle
(USB-JTAG egress drops-when-unread, never blocks). Did NOT touch the board.
**★ BEARER-OWNER DECISIONS LOCKED (composer eb0bc75 + android, 2026-07-12):** LoRa REAL + WiFi REAL + BLE dark.
**(a) fw inject-per-transport harness CANCELLED** (composer #2 — no no-RF sim leg needed; removed from open items).
**(b) NEW hive task #66 (composer #1), GATED on supervisor GO:** stand a 2nd LoRa node at SF7 (`benchsf7`) as the
R2-PROVISION §3.2 JOIN counterparty to the XIAO (android is phone-provisioner ONLY). Deps on GO: 2nd SX1262 board
attached (RAK DISCONNECTED — need Roy hw) + a JOIN-role build (not keyless xiaobridge). **BLE-REAL FINALIZED (composer 0b2d0bd)** — not skip. Reflash `xiaobridge,ble` still HELD but ADDITIVE (keeps LoRa
bridge + adds ble_task); trigger = AFTER (a) WiFi leg proven AND (b) android BlueZ central built, at a convenient
break in android's live capture. **✅ compile-verified locally (xtensa esp toolchain): `xiaobridge,ble,benchsf7`
builds GREEN (warnings-only) = no feature-unification blocker.** **⚠ compile-green ≠ coex-proven** — BLE+WiFi+LoRa on

**★★ 2026-07-13 — core RULED the staging layout; full OTA flow now specified end-to-end.** wire-order != storage-order resolves it: composer's 0x03 stream = header||sig||payload (sig up-front) so the RECEIVER verify-before-writes, but STORAGE = payload@0 bootable + header/sig persisted separately. verify_staged_slot is LAYOUT-AGNOSTIC (takes header+sig DETACHED args + payload_chunks = the RAW BOOTABLE IMAGE only = exact mint-SHA256 bytes; caller slices). **CONFIRMED to core:** (c) = RETURN-PREFIX — finish(self)->(AppliedUpdate, S, prefix:[u8;201]); FlashSink stages PAYLOAD ONLY to DFU[0..] (never sees header/sig), I write the header+sig prefix + SWAP magic in MY activate metal (no ImageSink trait change). ORDERING CONTRACT (honoured): write payload(verify-before-write)->finish->write prefix->SWAP MAGIC LAST (single commit anchor; crash-before-magic=no-swap=safe; corrupt-after=boot-gate Err=erase+clear=fail-closed). **(b) prefix placement = MY metal (doesn't affect core's finish()): leaning DEDICATED METADATA REGION over in-DFU-trailer** — SAFETY: embassy-boot swap uses DFU's extra pages (DFU=ACTIVE+2pg) as rotation SCRATCH, so an in-DFU-end trailer is clobbered mid-swap; survivable on a FRESH boot (read before prepare_boot) but a POWER-LOSS-MID-SWAP RESUME would read a corrupt trailer + partially-rotated payload → re-verify fails → clearing magic mid-swap BRICKS a half-swapped ACTIVE. **⚠ SAFETY-CRITICAL GATE RULE (mine, codex-refute): verify ONLY on a FRESH (not-started) swap; NEVER re-verify/cancel an in-progress one — let embassy-boot resume.** A metadata region (never swap-touched) makes the prefix always-readable + sidesteps this. capacity() = full DFU_usable (region) OR DFU_usable-201 (if trailer). **FULL FLOW — RECEIVE(core receiver): reassemble header||sig → OwnedOtaApply::start[early-reject] → feed payload→DFU[0..] → finish → (applied,sink,prefix) → I write prefix+magic. BOOT(my bootloader): magic pending & FRESH? → read prefix(header,sig) → verify_staged_slot(header,sig,DFU[0..payload_len] page-streamed,ctx) → Ok=prepare/swap; Err=erase DFU+clear magic.** Core BUILDING the receiver (return-prefix). Gate wiring next block: re-vendor → wire (incl fresh-vs-resume logic + region placement) → compile → codex-refute.

**★★★ 2026-07-13 — cad8b57 HELD (hive-codex CRITICAL, correctly caught); SUPERSEDE with a redesigned local successor (GO, compile-only, no push/flash until twin-clean).** cad8b57 (bootloader gate) + ec29da4 (re-vendor) = LOCAL commits, UNPUSHED. Parked app edits = stash 6dcfccc (embassy_boot relink @0x24000 + the insufficient 201→204 align). **Confirmed defects (all real vs the exact release ELF):** C1 approval guard DEAD — gate_flag@201, 201%4≠0 → Nvmc Unaligned → optimizer removed the approve write → NO durable approval → power-cut brick (most reproducible fact). C2 reject ignores STATE-erase failure → erased bytes copied into ACTIVE. **CORRECTED MAP (successor):** BOOTLOADER 0x0-0x20000 | STATE 0x20000-0x21000 (4K, proven) | OTA-META 0x21000-0x22000 (candidate prefix+approval) | PERSONA 0x22000-0x24000 | ACTIVE 0x24000-0x91000 (436K/109pg) | DFU 0x91000-0xFF000 (440K/110pg = ACTIVE+1, the documented min) | JOURNAL 0xFF000-0x100000 (4K confirmed-floor, OUTSIDE the swap). **SUCCESSOR REQUIREMENTS (GO):** (1) ONE shared geometry source (app+boot+ota.rs+persona) + build-time overlap/boundary KATs. (2) ALWAYS-VERIFY, gated on embassy-boot's OWN progress counter — NO separate approval record/digest (supervisor Occam+security refutation 2026-07-13, VERIFIED vs embassy-boot-0.7.0 source). Why the digest was dropped: (a) the payload-SHA256 (the expensive part) is paid EITHER WAY (verify checks payload_hash; skip recomputes the digest over the same bytes) — skip saves ONLY the Ed25519 (~tens of ms) ONCE PER OTA (fresh swap), not per boot (normal State::Boot = zero crypto); (b) the digest adds ZERO security — a flash-writing attacker forges the skip in BOTH models (writes record = SHA256(their header‖sig‖payload); bootloader recomputes over their DFU, matches, skips), identical to forging the progress counter; both rely SOLELY on H4 ACL flash-lock. Ground truth (boot_loader.rs): read_state()==Swap for BOTH fresh & in-progress (magic-only); swap() physically ROTATES DFU↔ACTIVE pages, so mid-swap the DFU payload is scrambled/unverifiable; at current_progress()==0 NOTHING is written yet (first op touches only the DFU scratch page at progress→1; first DFU-payload overwrite not until progress≥2) ⇒ progress==0 is a HARD pristine-DFU guarantee. Gate: State::Swap && progress==0 ⇒ FRESH ⇒ read header+sig from OTA-META + stream pristine DFU payload ⇒ full verify_staged_slot (Ed25519 + SHA256==payload_hash + seq>floor) ⇒ PASS → call prepare_boot (starts swap); FAIL → checked-reject. State::Swap && progress>0 ⇒ swap already begun (scrambled) ⇒ NEVER verify, NEVER reject/erase ⇒ pass straight to prepare_boot (embassy resumes). Power-cut in the verify→prepare window leaves progress==0 ⇒ next boot re-verifies pristine DFU (idempotent). The durable "already-authorized" signal is embassy-boot's progress counter itself — no record to write/bind. NOTE: this reads STATE progress words directly (magic@0, valid-marker@WRITE_SIZE, progress@2·WRITE_SIZE+, per embassy-boot 0.7/0.12) — KAT-pin this layout + re-verify on any embassy-boot bump. (3) checked reject — prove STATE non-SWAP (readback) before DFU erase, else fail-stop. (4) payload gate — 0<len≤ACTIVE_LEN, PT_FIRMWARE_FULL, bootable-vector sanity, USE VerifiedUpdate. (5) split dev-bench vs prod DeviceContext (prod = persona/board/device/battery, fail-closed if unavailable). (6) confirmed floor in the SEPARATE atomic JOURNAL page + pending/confirm lifecycle, NO floor=0 fallback. (7) H4 BPROT/ACL — NOT a permitted follow-up for a prod-compilable successor (coordinator correction 2026-07-13): the PROD bootloader build MUST apply reset-time BPROT/ACL protecting BOOTLOADER (0x0-0x20000) + PERSONA (0x22000-0x24000) so a compromised app cannot rewrite the anchor/bootloader, AND partition-wrap the app's Nvmc writes to its own regions; the ONLY unprotected build is an EXPLICITLY-NAMED dev/bench feature; a prod build without protection MUST fail-closed at COMPILE time (compile_error!/const-assert), never silently ship unprotected. Implemented WITH increment 2 (bootloader). ★ ACCEPTANCE (exact re-pass, coordinator 2026-07-13): there must be NO production path that boots with a WRITABLE bootloader/persona — every prod build either boots ACL-protected or does not compile; only the explicit dev/bench feature boots unprotected. (8) falsifiers: power-cut@every write/erase/swap-boundary, stale-approval/new-candidate, map-overlap, reject-fail, floor. LOCAL commit only → exact hive-codex re-pass. DO-NOT-FLASH + Roy tg_pk gate stand.
**★ APP-SEAM FLASHSINK SUB-INCREMENT SPEC (pickup-ready; GATED behind a clean re-review of 9135db2 — do NOT start until re-pass clean; supervisor sequencing).** Files = `rak4630-fw/platforms/rak4630/{src/ota.rs, src/main.rs, build.rs}`. Contract (core-blessed staging ruling + my OTA-META metadata-region choice + F1):
> (1) **ota.rs consume rak-geometry:** `SLOT_B_BASE`→`DFU_ORIGIN` (0x91000), `SLOT_SIZE`/`capacity()`→`ACTIVE_LEN` (0x6D000; matches the boot gate `payload_size≤ACTIVE_LEN` bound). (2) **★F1 app-half — FULL-SLOT ERASE:** `begin()` MUST erase the WHOLE DFU slot `DFU[0..DFU_LEN]` (not just payload-rounded), so the unauthenticated tail `DFU[payload_size..ACTIVE_LEN]` is 0xFF — ELSE the boot gate's tail-all-0xFF assert (9135db2) REJECTS a legit image. (3) **Receiver flow (#19/#35):** use `r2_update::OtaReceiver` (import the SIGNED one BY NAME — NOT the legacy unsigned `r2_hive_core::ota::OtaReceiver`): `new(ctx, PT_FIRMWARE_FULL, FlashSink)` → `push(&[u8])->Result<(RxProgress, consumed), RxError>` (preserve `sdu[consumed..]` post-package bytes) → `finish(self)->(AppliedUpdate, S, prefix:[u8;201])`. `abort()` idempotent + safe after a FAILED/partial `begin()`. (4) **commit_swap (ORDER = the core atomicity contract):** payload→DFU[0..] via FlashSink (verify-before-write) → finish → write `prefix[201]` (header137+sig64) → `OTA_META[0..201]` → set STATE `[0xF0;4]` SWAP_MAGIC **LAST** (plain Nvmc; embassy-boot magic word). Crash anywhere before the magic = no swap = old image boots (safe); corrupt after = boot-gate `verify_staged_slot` Err = fail-closed. (5) persona read `0x12000`→`PERSONA_ORIGIN` (0x22000). (6) app `build.rs` FLASH origin→`ACTIVE_ORIGIN` (0x24000) + VTOR reloc; reconcile parked stash `6dcfccc` (KEEP its embassy_boot relink@0x24000 + VTOR; DROP the obsolete 201→204 align — no approval record anymore). ## 🔨🚧 BUILDING — P3 USB-PAIR simple-secure PERIPHERAL SM (task #67) — supervisor GO 2026-07-12 against R2-PROVISION v0.50 @0f61c81
**★ GO #4 = BUILD ORDER (supervisor 2026-07-12):** build the simple pairing PERIPHERAL SM INTO the xiaobridge fw against twin-clean **v0.50 @`0f61c81`** (verified: ancestor of specs HEAD aff328a on spec-conformance-v0.2), regenerate vectors, re-verify terminal MACs, THEN reflash the XIAO so pairing lights over the live USB link (android runs PairingHost over ttyACM1 = the bench-critical reflash). **✅ SPEC READ @0f61c81 (scratchpad/R2-PROVISION-0f61c81.md §5.3.4 lines 448-798).** Frame vocab (R2-USB §3.7 control `[0xFF]‖CBOR({0:msg_type,1:fields})`): 4 PAIR_HELLO_HOST host→p `{}` · 5 PAIR_COMMIT p→host `{1:commit(32)}` · 13 PAIR_HOST_REVEAL host→p `{1:eph_pk_host(32),2:nonce_host(32)}` · 6 PAIR_REVEAL p→host `{1:eph_pk_p(32),2:nonce_p(32)}` · 7 PAIR_CONFIRM host→p `{1:confirm_mac(16)}` · 8 PAIR_DONE p→host `{1:done_mac(16)}` · 14 PAIR_ACK host→p `{1:ack_mac(16)}` · 9 RECONNECT_CHALLENGE host→p `{1:nonce_rc(16)}` · 10 RECONNECT_RESPONSE p→host `{1:tag(16)}` · 11 PAIR_ABORT either `{1:reason tstr}`. (msg_type 12=observation, 15=retired.) **PERIPHERAL SM:** recv HELLO(4)→RETAIN persisted key, gen fresh eph+nonce, send COMMIT(5); recv HOST_REVEAL(13); send REVEAL(6); Z=X25519, reject all-zero→ABORT{bad_key}; recv CONFIRM(7) verify confirm-host MAC; send DONE(8); recv ACK(14) verify ack-host MAC→**PERSIST K**. Reconnect: recv CHALLENGE(9)→tag=HMAC(link_key,"r2-usb-reconnect-v1"‖nonce_rc‖usb_link_id)[..16]→RESPONSE(10); activation host-local (peripheral proves to host only). Idempotent in-session dup (RAM, 60s terminal timeout): dup CONFIRM→resend DONE, dup ACK→no-op. Key preservation: persisted key retained until final ACK-verify; re-pair on any doubt (no journal/gen/rotation/crash-recovery). transcript = eph_pk_host‖eph_pk_p‖nonce_host‖nonce_p (128B). usb_link_id = CAPS hive_id_bytes (16B) = HKDF("r2-usb-link-v1",device_master_secret,"")[..16].
**✅ TERMINAL MACs RE-VERIFIED byte-exact vs v0.50 (supervisor's re-verify check DONE):** usb_pair.rs labels + asserted hex == spec UP14/UP18 (confirm `4e4c5ff2…`/done `08ba274f…`/ack `1ec03c3d…`/reconnect `2f62edaa…`); KDF domains did NOT move (spec line 570: byte-exact constructions unchanged, naming-only). 14 usb_pair tests green. Crypto restored @5fc3a20 is spec-valid — no revector needed.

## 🤝 tn_base recipe modeling — SPECS RULED (§3.3.1 v0.30 @8c8310d); SHA-fidelity = remaining open item for core
Specs ratified the TWO-AXIS model (matches what I told composer): **tn_base@ver** = shared core-TN-base@1.0.0 (board-INDEPENDENT ABI_VERSION/CORE_ABI_VERSION = abi_hash/min_core_abi) + **board_profile@ver** = platforms/rak4630 (pinmap/flash/OTA); "pin the platform" pins the board_profile axis, NOT tn_base; the flashed r2-rak4630 binary = BUILD OUTPUT (compose of both + ensembles + switches), provenance ref not a pin. Core confirms on ruling.
- **CRITICAL #1 — anti-rollback FAIL-OPEN (ota_tcp.rs):** load_anti_rollback() returns (0,0) on an NVS OPEN/READ ERROR (not just absent) → a corrupt/unavailable NVS floors anti-rollback to 0 → an OLD signed seq is ADMITTED (downgrade); and commit/stage/clear discard every NVS write error (let _ = set_u32) → a failed floor advance is SILENT. FIX (agreed, fail-CLOSED): NVS ops return Result + refuse-to-START an OTA if the floor is unreadable + durably stage {seq,payload_hash} BEFORE esp_ota set_boot + reconcile pending after mark-valid (same discipline as the RAK FlashSink).

Blind-authored (core verified by reasoning); **I compile + metal-verify on espup.**

NOT a firmware edit.** **★ SF12 re-size before field (CORRECTED 2026-07-11, supervisor-codex): 8-sym SF12 preamble = 262 MILLIseconds = the DETECTION budget (rx+sleep ≤ 262ms); the 24-bit sleepPeriod hardware cap = 262 SECONDS (0xFFFFFF×15.625µs), 1000× larger + NON-binding. SF12 thus ALLOWS a LONGER sleep than SF7 — don't carry 3/5ms because it WASTES SF12's ~250ms headroom, not because a cap blocks it; re-size from preamble/detection-margin+SCF/power policy** ([[setrxdutycycle-preamble-sizing]]). ## 🧩 WASM HOST — LINKABLE BASE (NEW workstream, Roy GO 2026-07-10, task #64; parallel to RAK)
Roy ruled BUILD the linkable base; hive owns the **wasm HOST** (base HOSTS wasm ensemble modules = Level 2, greenfield — NOT r2-hive-wasm, which is R2 compiled TO wasm). Ref: r2-specifications docs/proposals/R2-LINKABLE-BASE-AND-VARIANT-MANAGEMENT-2026-07-10.md (D.3 steps 4-5). **Prep design committed: docs/WASM-HOST-LINKABLE-BASE-PREP.md (c709e23).**
- **Two ABI surfaces** (both = the §12.4 Plugin trait lowered to repr(C) per proposal A.5.3): module-EXPORTS (execute/init/poll → wasm ptr+len) + host-IMPORTS (the capabilities.requires §12.3 syscall surface = "the host-import surface"). A wasm module becomes a Rust Plugin impl trampolining into its exports → plugs into existing engine dispatch.
- **Phasing (D.3 4-5, core A.5 binding):** std host (wasmtime) + browser (native WebAssembly) FIRST; then esp32s3+PSRAM wasm3; **nrf52840 = ONE bounded (<=32KB) boot-reserved wasm3 slot only** (A.5.1 — general multi-module REFUTED; binding constraint = 64KB-page CONTIGUITY on MMU-less heap, not total RAM). **Level-0 hot-path/crypto NEVER modularized** (A.5.4 — route/dedup/wire/CBOR/FNV, radio io_task, HMAC/HKDF/Ed25519). Host = orchestration-class only.
